Which is why it goes without saying that it's exceptionally important to learn how to effectively start and manage a blog in a way that supports your business.</p> \n<p>Without a blog, you'll find yourself experiencing a number of problems such as poor <a href=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/marketing/blog-search-engine-optimization?_ga=2.164410620.271223718.1616532009-1705428839.1616532009\">search engine optimization (SEO)</a>, lack of promotional content for social, little clout with your leads and customers, and fewer pages that you can use to share lead-generating calls-to-action (CTAs).</p> \n<p>So why, oh why, do so many marketers still have a laundry list of excuses for why they can't maintain a blog?</p> \n<a class=\"cta_button\" href=\"https://www.hubspot.com/cs/ci/?pg=ccc95db5-9007-49cf-b69c-94bb5c46b366&amp;pid=53&amp;ecid=&amp;hseid=&amp;hsic=\"><img class=\"hs-cta-img \" style=\"border-width: 0px; /*hs-extra-styles*/; margin: 0 auto; display: block; margin-top: 20px; margin-bottom: 20px\" alt=\"→ Download Now: 6 Free Blog Post Templates\" src=\"https://no-cache.hubspot.com/cta/default/53/ccc95db5-9007-49cf-b69c-94bb5c46b366.png\" align=\"middle\" /></a> \n<p>Maybe because, unless you enjoy writing, business blogging might seem uninteresting, time consuming, and difficult.</p> \n<p>Well, the time for excuses is over and this guide is here to help you understand why. We'll cover how to write and manage your business's blog as well as provide helpful templates to simplify your blogging efforts.</p> \n<p></p> \n<p>Let's get started with an important question.</p> \n<a></a> \n<p>Blog posts allow you and your business to publish insights, thoughts, and stories on your website about any topic. They can help you boost brand awareness, credibility, conversions, and revenue. Most importantly, they can help you drive traffic to your website.</p> \n<p>Today, people and organizations of all walks of life manage blogs to share analyses, instruction, criticisms, product information, industry findings, and more. There are many popular blog formats, but here are <a href=\"https://offers.hubspot.com/blog-post-templates?hubs_post=blog.hubspot.com/marketing/how-to-start-a-blog&amp;hubs_post-cta=six%20of%20the%20most%20common\">six of the most common</a>:</p> \n<ul> \n <li>The \"How-To\" Post</li> \n <li>The List-Based Post</li> \n <li>The \"What Is\" Post</li> \n <li>The Pillar Page Post (“Ultimate Guide”)</li> \n <li>The Newsjacking Post</li> \n <li>The Infographic Post</li> \n</ul> \n<p><a href=\"https://offers.hubspot.com/blog-post-templates?hubs_post-cta=pillar_allphrase&amp;hubs_post=blog.hubspot.com/marketing/how-to-start-a-blog\">Save time and download six blog post templates for free.</a></p> \n<p>So, how do you ensure your blog post catches the eyes of your target audience, buyer personas, and customers?</p> \n<p></p> \n<a></a> \n<h2>What makes a good blog post?</h2> \n<p>Before you write a blog, make sure you know the answers to questions like, <em>\"Why would someone keep reading this entire blog post?\"</em> and <em>\"What makes our audience come back for more?\"</em></p> \n<p>To start, a good blog post is interesting and educational. Blogs should answer questions and help readers resolve a challenge they're experiencing — and you have to do so in an interesting way.</p> \n<p>It's not enough just to answer someone's questions — you also have to provide actionable steps while being engaging. For instance, your introduction should hook the reader and make them want to continue reading your post. Then, use examples to keep your readers interested in what you have to say.</p> \n<p><strong>Remember, a good blog post is interesting to read and provides educational content to audience members.</strong></p> \n<p>(Want to learn how to apply blogging and other forms of content marketing to your business? Check out HubSpot Academy's <a href=\"https://academy.hubspot.com/courses/content-marketing\">free content marketing course</a>.)</p> \n<p>So, how do you actually go about writing one of these engaging and informational pieces?</p> \n<h2>How to Write a Blog Post</h2> \n<p>Here are the steps you'll want to follow while writing a blog post.</p> \n<h3>1. Understand your audience.</h3> \n<p>Before you start writing your blog post, make sure you have a clear understanding of your target audience.</p> \n<p>Ask questions like: What do they want to know about? What will resonate with them?</p> \n<p>This is where the process of <a href=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/marketing/buyer-persona-research\">creating buyer personas</a> comes in handy. Consider what you know about your buyer personas and their interests while you're coming up with a topic for your blog post.</p> \n<p>For instance, if your readers are millennials looking to start a business, you probably don't need to provide them with information about getting started in social media — most of them already have that down.</p> \n<p>You might, however, want to give them information about how to adjust their social media approach (for example — from what may be a casual, personal approach to a more business-savvy, networking-focused approach). That kind of tweak is what helps you publish content about the topics your audience really wants and needs.</p> \n<p>Don't have buyer personas in place for your business? Here are a few resources to help you get started:</p> \n<ul> \n <li><a href=\"https://offers.hubspot.com/free-template-creating-buyer-personas?hubs_post=blog.hubspot.com/marketing/how-to-start-a-blog&amp;hubs_post-cta=Create%20Buyer%20Personas%20for%20Your%20Business%20%5BFree%20Template%5D\">Create Buyer Personas for Your Business [Free Template]</a></li> \n <li><a href=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/marketing/buyer-persona-research\">Guide: How to Create Detailed Buyer Personas for Your Business</a></li> \n <li><a href=\"https://www.hubspot.com/make-my-persona?hubs_post=blog.hubspot.com/marketing/how-to-start-a-blog&amp;hubs_post-cta=%5BFree%20Tool%5D%20Make%20My%20Persona%3A%20Buyer%20Persona%20Generator\">[Free Tool] Make My Persona: Buyer Persona Generator</a></li> \n</ul> \n<h3>2. Create your blog domain.</h3> \n<p>Next, you'll need a place to host this post and every other blog post you write. This requires choosing a <a href=\"https://www.hubspot.com/products/cms?hubs_post=blog.hubspot.com/marketing/how-to-start-a-blog&amp;hubs_post-cta=content%20management%20system%20(CMS)\">content management system (CMS)</a> and a website <a href=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/marketing/what-is-a-domain\">domain</a> hosting service.</p> \n<h4 style=\"font-weight: normal;\">Choose a CMS.</h4> \n<p>A <a href=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/blog/tabid/6307/bid/7969/what-is-a-cms-and-why-should-you-care.aspx\">CMS</a> helps you create a website domain where you'll actually publish your blog. CMS platforms can manage domains (where you create your website) and subdomains (where you create a webpage that connects to an existing website).</p> \n<p>HubSpot customers host web content via <a href=\"https://www.hubspot.com/products/cms?hubs_post=blog.hubspot.com/marketing/how-to-start-a-blog&amp;hubs_post-cta=CMS%20Hub\">CMS Hub</a>. Another popular option is a self-hosted <a href=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/marketing/wordpress-website\">WordPress website</a> on a hosting site such as <a href=\"https://wpengine.com/\">WP Engine</a>. Whether you create a domain or a subdomain to start your blog, you'll need to choose a <a href=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/website/web-hosting\">web hosting</a> service after you pick a CMS.</p> \n<h4 style=\"font-weight: normal;\">Register a domain or subdomain with a website host.</h4> \n<p>Your blog's domain will look like this: www.yourblog.com. The name between the two periods is up to you, as long as this domain name doesn't yet exist on the internet.</p> \n<p>Want to create a subdomain for your blog? If you already own a cooking business at www.yourcompany.com, you might create a blog that looks like this: blog.yourcompany.com. In other words, your blog's subdomain will live in its own section of yourcompany.com.</p> \n<p>Some CMS platforms offer subdomains as a free service, where your blog lives on the CMS, rather than your business's website. For example, it might look like this: yourblog.contentmanagementsystem.com. However, to create a subdomain that belongs to your company website, register the subdomain with a <a href=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/website/web-hosting\">website host</a>.</p> \n<p>Most <a href=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/marketing/best-wordpress-hosting\">website hosting services</a> charge very little to host an original domain — in fact, website costs can be as inexpensive as $3 per month when you commit to a 36-month term.</p> \n<p>Here are five popular web hosting services to choose from:</p> \n<ul> \n <li><a href=\"https://www.godaddy.com/\">GoDaddy</a></li> \n <li><a href=\"https://www.hostgator.com/\">HostGator</a></li> \n <li><a href=\"https://www.dreamhost.com/\">DreamHost</a></li> \n <li><a href=\"https://www.bluehost.com/\">Bluehost</a></li> \n <li><a href=\"https://www.ipage.com/\">iPage</a></li> \n</ul> \n<h3>3. Customize your blog's theme.</h3> \n<p>Once you have your domain name set up, customize the appearance of your blog to reflect the theme of the content you plan on creating and your brand.</p> \n<p>For example, if you're writing about sustainability and the environment, green might be a color to keep in mind while designing your blog.</p> \n<p>If you already manage a website and are writing the first post for that existing website, ensure the article is consistent with the website in appearance and subject matter. Two ways to do this are including your:</p> \n<ul> \n <li><strong>Logo</strong>: This can be your business's name and logo — it will remind blog readers of who's publishing the content. (How heavily you want to brand your blog, however, is up to you.)</li> \n <li><strong>\"About\" Page</strong>: You might already have an \"About\" blurb describing yourself or your business. Your blog's \"About\" section is an extension of this higher-level statement. Think of it as your blog's mission statement, which serves to support your company's goals.</li> \n</ul> \n<h3>4. Identify your first blog post's topic.</h3> \n<p>Before you write anything, pick a topic for your blog post. The topic can be pretty general to start. For example, if you're a company that sells a <a href=\"https://www.hubspot.com/products/crm?hubs_post=blog.hubspot.com/marketing/how-to-start-a-blog&amp;hubs_post-cta=CRM%20for%20small-to-enterprise%20businesses\">CRM for small-to-enterprise businesses</a>, your post might be about the importance of using a single software to keep your marketing, sales, and service teams aligned.</p> \n<p><strong>Pro tip:</strong> You may not want to jump into a \"how-to\" article for your first blog post.</p> \n<p>Why?</p> \n<p>Your credibility hasn’t been established yet. Before teaching others how to do something, you’ll first want to show that you’re a leader in your field and an authoritative source.</p> \n<p>For instance, if you're a plumber writing your first post, you won’t yet write a post titled “How to Replace the Piping System in your Bathroom.” First, you'd write about modern faucet setups, or tell a particular success story you had rescuing a faucet before it flooded a customer's house. Here are four other <a href=\"https://offers.hubspot.com/blog-post-templates?_ga=2.19944184.1115648469.1587910754-1675356138.1572978608&amp;hubs_post=blog.hubspot.com/marketing/how-to-start-a-blog&amp;hubs_post-cta=types%20of%20blog%20posts\">types of blog posts</a> you could start with:</p> \n<ul> \n <li><strong>List (\"Listicle\")</strong>: 5 ways to fix a leaky faucet</li> \n <li><strong>Curated Collection</strong>: 10 faucet and sink brands to consider today</li> \n <li><strong>SlideShare Presentation</strong>: 5 types of faucets to replace your old one (with pictures)</li> \n <li><strong>News Piece</strong>: New study shows X% of people don't replace their faucet frequently enough</li> \n</ul> \n<p>If you're having trouble coming up with topic ideas, a good <a href=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/marketing/blog-post-topic-brainstorm\">topic brainstorming session</a> should help. In the post I’ve linked, my colleague walks you through a helpful process for turning one idea into many. Similar to the \"leaky faucet\" examples above, you would \"iterate off old topics to come up with unique and compelling new topics.\"</p> \n<p>This can be done by:</p> \n<ul> \n <li>Changing the topic scope</li> \n <li>Adjusting your time frame</li> \n <li>Choosing a new audience</li> \n <li>Taking a positive/negative approach</li> \n <li>Introducing a new format</li> \n</ul> \n<h3>5. Come up with a working title.</h3> \n<p>You might come up with a few different working titles — in other words, iterations of approaching that topic to help you focus your writing.</p> \n<p>For example, you may decide to narrow your topic to \"Tools for Fixing Leaky Faucets\" or \"Common Causes of Leaky Faucets.\" A working title is specific and will guide your post so you can start writing.</p> \n<p>Let's take a real post as an example: \"<a href=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/marketing/how-to-choose-solid-topic-next-blog-post-ht\">How to Choose a Solid Topic for Your Next Blog Post</a>.\"</p> \n<p>Appropriate, right? The topic, in this case, was probably \"blogging.\" Then the working title may have been something like, \"The Process for Selecting a Blog Post Topic.\" And the final title ended up being \"How to Choose a Solid Topic for Your Next Blog Post.\"</p> \n<p>See that evolution from topic, to working title, to final title? Even though the working title may not end up being the final title (more on that in a moment), it still provides enough information so you can focus your blog post on something more specific than a generic, overwhelming topic.</p> \n<h3>6. Write an intro (and make it captivating).</h3> \n<p>We've written more specifically about writing captivating introductions in the post \"<a href=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/marketing/how-to-write-introduction-quick-tip-ht\">How to Write an Introduction</a>,\" but let's review, shall we?</p> \n<p>First, grab the reader's attention. If you lose the reader in the first few paragraphs — or even sentences — of the introduction, they'll stop reading (even before they've given your post a fair shake). You can do this in a number of ways: tell a story or a joke, be empathetic, or grip the reader with an interesting fact or statistic.</p> \n<p>Then, describe the purpose of your post and explain how it will address a problem the reader may be experiencing. This will give the reader a reason to continue reading and show them how the post will help them improve their work or lives.</p> \n<p>Here's an example of an intro we think does a good job of attracting a reader's attention right away:</p> \n<p>“Blink. Blink. Blink. It's the dreaded cursor-on-a-blank-screen experience that all writers — amateur or professional, aspiring or experienced — know and dread. And of all times for it to occur, it seems to plague us the most when trying to write an introduction.”</p> \n<h3>7. Organize your content in an outline.</h3> \n<p>Sometimes, blog posts can have an overwhelming amount of information — for the reader and the writer. The trick is to organize the info in a way so readers aren't intimidated by length or amount of content. This organization can take multiple forms — sections, lists, tips — whatever's most appropriate. But it must be organized!</p> \n<h3 style=\"text-align: center;\">Featured Resource: <a href=\"https://offers.hubspot.com/blog-post-templates?hubs_post-cta=header\">6 Free Blog Post Templates</a></h3> \n<p><img src=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/hs-fs/hubfs/blog-post-templates.png?width=400&amp;name=blog-post-templates.png\" alt=\"Free Blog Post Templates\" width=\"400\" style=\"width: 400px; margin-left: auto; margin-right: auto; display: block;\" /></p> \n<p style=\"text-align: center;\"><a href=\"https://offers.hubspot.com/blog-post-templates?hubs_post-cta=imagebottom\">Download These Templates for Free</a></p> \n<p>Let's take a look at the post, \"<a href=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/marketing/how-to-use-snapchat-for-business\">How to Use Snapchat: A Detailed Look Into HubSpot’s Snapchat Strategy.</a>\" There's a lot of content in the piece, so it's broken up into a few sections using descriptive headers. The major sections are separated into subsections that go into more detail, making the content easier to read.</p> \n<p>To complete this step, all you really need to do is outline your post. This way, before you start writing, you'll know which points you want to cover and the best order to do so in. And to make things even easier, you can <a href=\"https://offers.hubspot.com/blog-post-templates?hubs_post=blog.hubspot.com/marketing/how-to-start-a-blog&amp;hubs_post-cta=download%20and%20use%20our%20free%20blog%20post%20templates\">download and use our free blog post templates</a>, which are pre-organized for six of the most common blogs. Just fill in the blanks!</p> \n<h3>8. Write your blog post!</h3> \n<p>The next step — but not the last — is actually writing the content. We can't forget about that, of course.</p> \n<p>Now that you have your outline or template, you're ready to fill in the blanks. Use your outline as a guide and expand on all points as needed. Write about what you already know, and if necessary, conduct additional research to gather more information, examples, and data to back up your points, while <a href=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/blog/tabid/6307/bid/33098/How-Not-to-Steal-People-s-Content-on-the-Web.aspx\">providing proper attribution</a> when incorporating external sources. When you do, always try to <a href=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/marketing/find-good-data\">find accurate and compelling data</a> to use in your post.</p> \n<p>If you're having trouble stringing sentences together, you're not alone. <a href=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/marketing/simple-productivity-tips\">Finding your \"flow\"</a> can be challenging for a lot of folks. Luckily, there are a ton of tools you can lean on to help you improve your writing. Here are a few to get you started:</p> \n<ul> \n <li><a href=\"https://www.powerthesaurus.org/\">Power Thesaurus</a>: Stuck on a word? Power Thesaurus is a crowdsourced tool that provides users with a number of alternative word choices from a community of writers.</li> \n <li><a href=\"http://www.zenpen.io/\">ZenPen</a>: If you're having trouble staying focused, check out this distraction-free writing tool. ZenPen creates a minimalist \"writing zone\" designed to help you get words down without having to fuss with formatting right away.</li> \n <li><a href=\"http://cliche.theinfo.org/\">Cliché Finder</a>: Feeling like your writing might be coming off a little cheesy? Identify instances where you can be more specific using this handy cliché tool.</li> \n</ul> \n<p>You can also refer to our <a href=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/marketing/improving-writing-skills-tools\">complete list of tools for improving your writing skills</a>. And if you're looking for more direction, the following resources are chock-full of valuable writing advice:</p> \n<ul> \n <li><a href=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/marketing/good-copywriting-practices-list\">Copywriting 101: 6 Traits of Excellent Copy Readers Will Remember</a></li> \n <li><a href=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/marketing/write-compelling-copy-tips#sm.0001ralmokx9oe96wpl15ahh67v4e\">How to Write Compelling Copy: 7 Tips for Writing Content That Converts</a></li> \n <li><a href=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/marketing/write-with-clarity-tips#sm.0001ralmokx9oe96wpl15ahh67v4e\">How to Write With Clarity: 9 Tips for Simplifying Your Message</a></li> \n <li><a href=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/marketing/kurt-vonnegut-guide-copywriting?&amp;_ga=2.29174140.1924088651.1560881619-1267545967.1551979014#sm.0001ralmokx9oe96wpl15ahh67v4e\">The Kurt Vonnegut Guide to Great Copywriting: 8 Rules That Apply to Anyone</a></li> \n <li><a href=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/marketing/how-to-write-interesting-content#sm.0001ralmokx9oe96wpl15ahh67v4e\">Your Blog Posts Are Boring: 9 Tips for Making Your Writing More Interesting</a></li> \n</ul> \n<h3>9. Proofread and edit your post.</h3> \n<p>You're not quite done yet, but you're close! The editing process is an important part of blogging — don't overlook it.</p> \n<p>Ask a grammar-conscious co-worker to copyedit and proofread your post. You may also consider enlisting the help of <a href=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/marketing/ultimate-editing-checklist\">The Ultimate Editing Checklist</a> or using a free grammar checker like <a href=\"https://www.grammarly.com/grammar-check\">Grammarly</a>.</p> \n<p>If you're looking to brush up on your self-editing skills, turn to these helpful posts for some tips and tricks to get you started:</p> \n<ul> \n <li><a href=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/marketing/hubspot-editing-tips\">How to Become a (Better) Editor: 13 Editorial Tips</a></li> \n <li><a href=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/marketing/speed-up-editorial-process#sm.0001ralmokx9oe96wpl15ahh67v4e\">How to Become a More Efficient Editor: 12 Ways to Speed Up the Editorial Process</a></li> \n <li><a href=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/marketing/edits-improve-writing#sm.0001ralmokx9oe96wpl15ahh67v4e\">10 Simple Edits That'll Instantly Improve Any Piece of Writing</a></li> \n</ul> \n<p>When you're ready to check your formatting, keep the blog elements in mind:</p> \n<h4 style=\"font-weight: normal;\">Featured Image</h4> \n<p>Choose a visually appealing and relevant image for your post. As social networks treat content with images more prominently, visuals are more responsible than ever for the success of your blog content.</p> \n<p><img src=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/hs-fs/hubfs/blog-post-with-featured-image.jpeg?width=650&amp;name=blog-post-with-featured-image.jpeg\" alt=\"Blog post with a featured image to the right\" width=\"650\" style=\"width: 650px; margin-left: auto; margin-right: auto; display: block;\" /></p> \n<p>For help selecting an image for your post, read \"<a href=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/marketing/blog-post-image-selection-ht-list\">How to Select the Perfect Image for Your Next Blog Post</a>\" and pay close attention to the section about copyright law.</p> \n<h4 style=\"font-weight: normal;\">Visual Appearance</h4> \n<p>No one likes an unattractive blog post. And it's not just pictures that make a post visually appealing — it's the formatting and organization of the post, too.</p> \n<p>In a well-formatted and visually-appealing blog post, you'll notice that header and sub-headers are used to break up large blocks of text — and those headers are styled consistently.</p> \n<p>Here's an example of what that looks like:</p> \n<p><img class=\"alignCenter shadow\" src=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/hs-fs/hubfs/header-and-sub-headers-blog-posts.png?width=1500&amp;name=header-and-sub-headers-blog-posts.png\" alt=\"Visual appearance tips on writing a blog.\" title=\"header-and-sub-headers-blog-posts.png\" width=\"1500\" style=\"width: 1500px; display: block; margin: 0px auto;\" /></p> \n<p>Screenshots should always have a similar, defined border so they don't appear as if they're floating in space — that style should stay consistent from post to post.</p> \n<p>Maintaining this consistency makes your content look more professional and easier on the eyes.</p> \n<h4 style=\"font-weight: normal;\">Topics and Tags</h4> \n<p>Tags are specific, public-facing keywords that describe a post. They also allow readers to browse for more content in the same category on your blog. Refrain from adding a laundry list of tags to each post. Instead, put some thought into a blog tagging strategy.</p> \n<p>Think of tags as \"topics\" or \"categories,\" and choose 10-20 tags that represent all the main topics you want to cover on your blog. Then stick to those.</p> \n<h3>10. Insert a CTA.</h3> \n<p>At the end of every blog post, <a href=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/blog/tabid/6307/bid/34005/How-to-Pick-the-Perfect-CTA-for-Every-Blog-Post.aspx\">insert a CTA</a> that indicates what you want the reader to do next — subscribe to your blog, download an ebook, register for a webinar or event, read a related article, etc.</p> \n<p>After your visitors read your blog post, they click on the CTA, and eventually you generate a lead. But the CTA is also a valuable resource for the person reading your content — use your CTAs to offer more content similar to the subject of the post they just finished reading. If you’re not sure how to get started, take a look at some <a href=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/marketing/call-to-action-examples\">CTA examples</a>.</p> \n<p>In the blog post \"<a href=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/marketing/what-to-post-on-instagram#sm.0001ralmokx9oe96wpl15ahh67v4e\">What to Post on Instagram: 18 Photo &amp; Video Ideas to Spark Inspiration</a>,\" readers are given actionable ideas for creating valuable Instagram content. At the end of the post is a CTA prompting readers to take a social media certification course:</p> \n<p><img src=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/hs-fs/hubfs/call-to-action-bottom-of-post.jpeg?width=686&amp;name=call-to-action-bottom-of-post.jpeg\" alt=\"Blog post about Instagram with a CTA at the bottom of the post\" width=\"686\" style=\"width: 686px;\" /></p> \n<p>See how that's a win-win for everyone? Readers who want to learn more have the opportunity to do so, and the business receives a lead they can nurture ... who may even become a customer!</p> \n<h3>11. Optimize for on-page SEO.</h3> \n<p>After you finish writing, go back and <a href=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/blog/tabid/6307/bid/33655/a-step-by-step-guide-to-flawless-on-page-seo-free-template.aspx\">optimize the on-page elements</a> of your post.</p> \n<p>Don't obsess over how many keywords to include. If there are opportunities to incorporate keywords you're targeting, and it won't impact reader experience, do it. If you can make your URL shorter and more keyword-friendly, go for it. But don't cram keywords or shoot for some arbitrary keyword density — Google's smarter than that!</p> \n<p>Here's a little <a href=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/marketing/blog-search-engine-optimization\">blog SEO</a> reminder about what you should review and optimize:</p> \n<h4 style=\"font-weight: normal;\">Meta Description</h4> \n<p>Meta descriptions are the descriptions below the post's page title on Google's search results pages. They provide searchers with a short summary of the post before clicking into it. They are ideally between 150-160 characters and start with a verb, such as \"Learn,\" \"Read,\" or \"Discover.\"</p> \n<p>While meta descriptions no longer factor into Google's keyword ranking algorithm, they give searchers a snapshot of what they'll get from reading the post and help improve your clickthrough rate from search.</p> \n<h4 style=\"font-weight: normal;\">Page Title and Headers</h4> \n<p>Most <a href=\"https://www.hubspot.com/products/blog?hubs_post=blog.hubspot.com/marketing/how-to-start-a-blog&amp;hubs_post-cta=blogging%20software\">blogging software</a> uses your post title as your page title, which is the most important on-page SEO element at your disposal. But if you've followed our formula so far, you should already have a working title that will naturally include keywords or phrases your target audience is interested in.</p> \n<p>Don't over-complicate your title by trying to fit in keywords where they don't naturally belong. With that said, if there are clear opportunities to add keywords you're targeting to your post title and headers, feel free to take them. Also, try to keep your headlines short — ideally, under 65 characters — so they don't get truncated in the search engine results.</p> \n<h4 style=\"font-weight: normal;\">Anchor Text</h4> \n<p>Anchor text is the word or words that link to another page — either on your website or on another website. Carefully select which keywords you want to link to other pages on your site because search engines take that into consideration when ranking your page for certain keywords.</p> \n<p>It's also important to consider which pages you link to. Consider linking pages that you want to rank for a specific keyword. You could end up getting it to rank on Google's first page of results instead of its second page — and that isn’t small potatoes!</p> \n<h4 style=\"font-weight: normal;\">Mobile Optimization</h4> \n<p>More than <a href=\"https://www.statista.com/statistics/297137/mobile-share-of-us-organic-search-engine-visits/\">60%</a> of organic visits are carried out on a mobile device. As such, having a website with a <a href=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/marketing/responsive-web-design\">responsive design</a> is critical. In addition to making sure your website's visitors (including your blog's visitors) have the best experience possible, optimizing for mobile will score your website some SEO points.</p> \n<h3>12. Pick a catchy title.</h3> \n<p>Last but not least, it's time to spruce up that working title of yours. Luckily, we have a <a href=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/marketing/a-simple-formula-for-writing-kick-ass-titles-ht\">simple formula for writing catchy titles</a> that will grab the attention of your reader. Here's what to consider:</p> \n<ol> \n <li>Start with your working title.</li> \n <li>As you start to edit your title, keep in mind that it's important to keep the title accurate and clear.</li> \n <li>Then, work on making your title sexy — whether it's through strong language, alliteration, or another literary tactic.</li> \n <li>If you can, optimize for SEO by sneaking some keywords in there (only if it's natural, though!).</li> \n <li>Finally, see if you can shorten it at all. No one likes a long, overwhelming title — remember, Google prefers 65 characters or fewer before it truncates it on its search engine results pages.</li> \n</ol> \n<p>Let’s summarize everything we’ve learned.</p> \n<img src=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/hs-fs/hubfs/how-to-write-a-blog-post.png?width=500&amp;name=how-to-write-a-blog-post.png\" alt=\"Visual overview of how to write a blog post with all the previous steps listed\" width=\"500\" style=\"width: 500px; margin-left: auto; margin-right: auto; display: block;\"> <p>If you've mastered the steps above, learn about some <a href=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/marketing/blog-optimization-tips\">ways to take your blog posts to the next level</a>.</p> <p>By now, you should know who you’re writing for, have a blog all set up, and understand the basics of writing a blog post. While it’s easy to understand the practicalities of writing a post, it’s difficult to get started on your very first article.</p> <p>Let’s go through the process of writing your first blog post.</p> <h2>Your First Blog Post: Choosing a Topic, Writing the Post, and Actually Getting Hits</h2> <p>You’ve got the technical and practical tidbits down — now it’s time to write your very first blog post. And nope, this isn’t the space to introduce yourself and your new blog (i.e. “Welcome to my blog! This is the topic I’ll be covering. Here are my social media handles. Will you please follow?”).</p> <p>We’ve briefly touched upon it in the previous section, but your first blog post shouldn’t be a how-to guide. Remember: you’ve yet to establish authority in the field. You should instead start with “low-hanging fruit,” writing about a highly specific topic that serves a small segment of your target audience.</p> <p>That seems unintuitive, right? If more people are searching for a term or a topic, that should mean more readers for you.</p> <p>But that’s not true. If you choose a general and highly searched topic that’s been covered by major competitors or more established brands, it’s unlikely that your post will rank on the first page of search engine results pages (SERPs). Give your newly born blog a chance by choosing a topic that few bloggers have written about.</p> <p><strong>TLDR; </strong>Your first post should cover a niche, low-volume topic. As you write more and more on your blog and establish topical authority, you can begin to cover more highly-searched keywords.</p> <p>Let’s walk through this process.</p> <h3>1. Find a low-volume topic.</h3> <p>The first step is to find a topic with low searches in Google (we recommend sticking to about 10 to 150 monthly searches). These topics offer less competition and should therefore allow your new blog post to rank more easily.</p> <p>To choose a topic, you can either do a traditional brainstorming session or carry out keyword research. We suggest the latter because you can actually see how many people are looking for that topic.</p> <p>Now, don’t be intimidated by the term “keyword research.” It’s not just for marketers, but for new bloggers, too. And it’s really easy to do.</p> <p>To jumpstart your keyword research, first begin by identifying the general topic of your blog.</p> <p>Say you’re a plumber. Your general, high-level topic might be “plumbing” (67K monthly searches).</p> <a></a> <p>Next, put this term into a keyword research tool such as:</p> \n <ul> \n  <li><a href=\"https://ahrefs.com\">Ahrefs</a></li> \n  <li><a href=\"https://moz.com/explorer\">Moz</a></li> \n  <li><a href=\"https://app.neilpatel.com/\">Ubersuggest</a></li> \n  <li><a href=\"https://www.wordtracker.com/\">Wordtracker</a></li> \n </ul> <p>When you run this term through the tool, a list of related keywords will appear. Scan the list and choose one with a lower search volume. For this example, we’ll use “under sink plumbing” (1.4K monthly searches).</p> <p>Run that keyword in the keyword research tool again. Look at the related keywords. Find one with a lower search volume. Do that again.</p> <p>For this example, we’ll settle on “plumbing problems under kitchen sink” (10 monthly searches). That’s the topic for our first post.</p> <p><strong>TLDR</strong>; Choose a low-volume, low-competition keyword that will ensure your first post ranks.</p> <p>For more help on keyword research, here are more resources you can use:</p> \n <ul> \n  <li><a href=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/marketing/how-to-do-keyword-research-ht\">How to Do Keyword Research for SEO: A Beginner's Guide</a></li> \n  <li><a href=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/marketing/how-to-rank-hubspot-seo-strategist\">How to Perform Keyword Research and Rank</a></li> \n  <li><a href=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/website/best-tools-to-find-long-tail-keywords\">Top Tools For Finding Long-Tail Keywords</a></li> \n </ul> <h3>2. Google the term to double-check search intent.</h3> <p>You’ve got your topic — now, double-check that the user’s search intent would be fulfilled by a blog post.</p> <p>What does that mean?</p> <p>If someone is looking for “plumbing problems under kitchen sink,” they might be looking for a tutorial, a diagram, an article, or a product that can fix the issue. If they’re looking for the first three, you’re good — that can be covered in a blog post. A product, however, is different, and your blog post won’t rank.</p> <p>How do you double-check search intent?</p> <p>Google the term and look at the results. If other articles and blog posts rank for that term, you’re good to go. If you only find product pages or listicles from major publications, then find a new topic to cover in your first post.</p> <p>Consider the term “under sink plumbing bathroom” (30 monthly searches). It seemed like a perfect fit because it had low monthly searches.</p> <p>Upon Googling the term, we found product carousels, product pages from Home Depot and Lowes, and guides written by major publications. (You’ll also want to avoid topics that have been covered by major publications, at least for now.)</p> <p><strong>TLDR</strong>; Before writing your first blog post about a low-volume topic, double-check the user intent by Googling the keyword. Also, don’t forget to take a look at who’s written about that topic so far. If you see a major brand, consider writing about another topic.</p> <h3>3. Find questions and terms related to that topic.</h3> <p>You’ve got a highly unique topic that’s been covered by just a few people so far. It’s time to flesh it out by covering related or adjacent topics.</p> <p>Use the following tools:</p> \n <ul> \n  <li><a href=\"https://answerthepublic.com/\"><strong>Answer the Public</strong></a>: When you place your keyword into this tool, it will give you a list of questions related to that term.</li> \n  <li><a href=\"https://www.google.com/\"><strong>Google</strong></a>: Google is your best friend. Search for the term and look under “People also ask” and “People also search for.” Be sure to touch upon those topics in the post.</li> \n </ul> <p>You can also use these keyword research tools <a href=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/marketing/how-to-start-a-blog#step-one\">we mentioned above in step one</a>.&nbsp;</p> <h3>5. Outline and write the post.</h3> <p>Now, it’s time to outline and write your first post!</p> <p>With your niche topic and related questions as guideposts, you can now write a post that’s highly relevant to your niche and doesn’t have as much competition.</p> <p>Use the how-to guide we shared in the previous section to help you write a great first post.</p> <p>Don’t forget to:</p> \n <ul> \n  <li><strong>Hit at least 1,000 words.</strong> It’s been proven time and again that longer posts rank better.</li> \n  <li><strong>Put your target keyword in the title</strong>. Remember that niche topic we chose in step one? Try to work it into your title naturally.</li> \n  <li><strong>Include at least two H2s with related search terms.</strong> Remember those related topics we found in step three? Use them as H2s to build the topical authority of your piece.</li> \n </ul> <h3>6. Promote your first post via outreach.</h3> <p>As a new blogger, you likely don’t have a social media following yet. The solution? Build a few backlinks to the post to get it off the ground.</p> <p>Backlinks are a major ranking factor, but you don’t want to use black-hat methods such as spamming the comment sections in other blogs. Instead, reach out to people and let them know this new resource exists so they can link to your post.</p> <p>If you’re a plumber, for example, you might reach out to your local plumber’s association. Here are more blog post promotion resources:</p> \n <ul> \n  <li><a href=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/marketing/blog-promotion-tactics\">12 Tried-and-True Ways to Promote Your Blog Posts</a></li> \n  <li><a href=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/blog/tabid/6307/bid/3013/8-free-links-to-promote-a-blog.aspx\">10 Sites You Can Use for Free Blog Promotion</a></li> \n  <li><a href=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/marketing/link-building-email-templates\">9 Link Building Email Outreach Templates That Actually Work</a></li> \n  <li><a href=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/marketing/build-inbound-links\">Inbound Link Building 101: 34 Ways to Build Backlinks for SEO</a></li> \n  <li><a href=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/marketing/backlink-strategies\">11 Creative (But 100% White Hat!) Ways to Earn Backlinks</a></li> \n </ul> <h3>First Blog Post Ideas</h3> <p>Stuck? Let’s take a look at some first blog post ideas.</p> <h5><strong>The Difference Between [Niche Topic] and [Niche Topic], Explained by a [Niche Expert] </strong></h5> \n <ul> \n  <li>The Difference Between SEM and SEO, Explained by a Marketing Expert</li> \n  <li>The Difference Between Sedans and Coupes, Explained by a Car Mechanic</li> \n  <li>The Difference Between Baking and Broiling, Explained by a Professional Baker</li> \n </ul> <h5><strong>The 10 Best and Worst [Niche Tool] for [Niche Activity]</strong></h5> \n <ul> \n  <li>The 10 Best and Worst Writing Software for Fiction Writing</li> \n  <li>The 10 Best and Worst CRMs for Nurturing Prospects</li> \n  <li>The 10 Best and Worst Family Cars for Cross-Country Roadtrips</li> \n </ul> <h5><strong>8 [Niche Activity] Common Mistakes (+ Ways to Fix Them)</strong></h5> \n <ul> \n  <li>8 Non-Fiction Writing Common Mistakes (+ Ways to Fix Them)</li> \n  <li>8 Salmon Broiling Common Mistakes (+ Ways to Fix Them)</li> \n  <li>8 Car Maintenance Common Mistakes (+ Ways to Fix Them)</li> \n </ul> <h5><strong>9 Proven Tips for [Niche Activity] </strong></h5> \n <ul> \n  <li>9 Proven Tips for Checking Plumbing Problems under Your Kitchen Sink</li> \n  <li>9 Proven Tips for Writing a Non-Fiction Bestseller</li> \n  <li>9 Proven Tips for Doing DIY Car Maintenance</li> \n </ul> <h5><strong>Why We/I Switched from [Niche Tool] to [Niche Tool] (Comparison) </strong></h5> \n <ul> \n  <li>Why We Switched from Pipedrive to HubSpot (Comparison)</li> \n  <li>Why I Switched from Microsoft Word to Scrivener (Comparison)</li> \n  <li>Why We Switched from iMacs to Surface Studio (Comparison)</li> \n </ul> <h5><strong>[Niche Tool] vs [Niche Tool]: Which [Tool] is Best for You? </strong></h5> \n <ul> \n  <li>Zendesk vs Freshcaller: Which Call Software is Best for You?</li> \n  <li>Air Fryer vs Convection Oven: Which One is Best for You?</li> \n  <li>Mazda Miata vs Toyota Supra: Which Sports Car is Best for You?</li> \n </ul> <h5><strong>The Ultimate Roundup of [Niche Activity] Tips and Tricks</strong></h5> \n <ul> \n  <li>The Ultimate Roundup of Novel Writing Tips and Tricks</li> \n  <li>The Ultimate Roundup of Macaroon Baking Tips and Tricks</li> \n  <li>The Ultimate Roundup of Solo Traveling Tips and Tricks</li> \n </ul> <p>Want some real examples of blog posts? See what your first blog post can look like based on the topic you choose and the audience you're targeting.</p> <a></a> <h3>1. List-Based Blog Post</h3> <h4>List-Based Post Example: <a href=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/marketing/beginner-blogger-mistakes\">17 Blogging Mistakes to Avoid in 2021, According to HubSpot Bloggers</a></h4> <p><img src=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/hs-fs/hubfs/list-based-blog-post-example.jpeg?width=650&amp;name=list-based-blog-post-example.jpeg\" alt=\"List based blog post example about blogging mistakes\" width=\"650\" style=\"width: 650px; margin-left: auto; margin-right: auto; display: block;\" /></p> <p>List-based posts are sometimes called \"listicles,\" a mix of the words \"list\" and \"article.\" These are articles that deliver information in the form of a list. A listicle uses sub-headers to break down the blog post into individual pieces, helping readers skim and digest your content more easily.</p> <p>As you can see in the example from our blog, listicles can offer various tips and methods for solving a problem.</p> <h3>2. Thought Leadership Post</h3> <h4>Example: <a href=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/marketing/how-hubspot-customers-shape-next-normal\">How HubSpot's Customers Are Shaping the Next Normal</a></h4> <p><img src=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/hs-fs/hubfs/thought-leadership-post-example.jpeg?width=650&amp;name=thought-leadership-post-example.jpeg\" alt=\"Thought leadership blog post example about HubSpot's customers\" width=\"650\" style=\"width: 650px; margin-left: auto; margin-right: auto; display: block;\" /></p> <p>Thought leadership posts allow you to share your expertise on a particular subject matter and share firsthand knowledge with your readers.</p> <p>These pieces — which can be written in the first person, like the post shown above — help you build trust with your audience so people take your blog seriously as you continue to write for it.</p> <h3>3. Curated Collection Post</h3> <h4>Example: <a href=\"https://listverse.com/2011/11/19/8-examples-of-evolution-in-action/\">8 Examples of Evolution in Action</a></h4> <p><img src=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/hs-fs/hubfs/curated-collection-example.png?width=650&amp;name=curated-collection-example.png\" width=\"650\" style=\"width: 650px; display: block; margin-left: auto; margin-right: auto;\" alt=\"Curated collection blog post example about evolution\" /></p> <p>Curated collections are a special type of listicle blog post. Rather than sharing tips or methods for doing something, this type of blog post shares a list of real examples that all have something in common in order to prove a larger point.</p> <p>In the example post above, Listverse shares eight real examples of evolution in action among eight different animals — starting with the peppered moth.</p> <h3>4. SlideShare Presentation</h3> <h4>Example: <a href=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/blog/tabid/6307/bid/34234/the-hubspot-culture-code-creating-a-company-we-love.aspx\">The HubSpot Culture Code</a></h4> <p><img src=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/hs-fs/hubfs/slideshare-presentation-blog-post-example.jpeg?width=650&amp;name=slideshare-presentation-blog-post-example.jpeg\" alt=\"Slideshare presentation blog post example about HubSpot's culture code\" width=\"650\" style=\"width: 650px; margin-left: auto; margin-right: auto; display: block;\" /></p> <p><a href=\"https://www.slideshare.net/\">SlideShare</a> is a presentation tool that helps publishers package a lot of information into easily shareable slides. Think of it like a PowerPoint, but for the web. With this in mind, SlideShare blog posts help you promote your SlideShare so that it can generate a steady stream of visitors.</p> <p>Unlike blogs, SlideShare decks don't often rank well on search engines, so they need a platform for getting their message out there to the people who are looking for it. By embedding and summarizing your SlideShare on a blog post, you can share a great deal of information and give it a chance to rank on Google at the same time.</p> <p>Need some SlideShare ideas? In the example above, we turned our company's \"Culture Code\" into a SlideShare presentation that anyone can look through and take lessons from, and then promoted it in a blog post.</p> <h3>5. Newsjacking Post</h3> <h4>Example: <a href=\"https://blog.houzz.com/ivy-goes-mobile-with-new-app-for-designers/\">Ivy Goes Mobile With New App for Designers</a></h4> <p><img src=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/hs-fs/hubfs/news-post-example.png?width=1500&amp;name=news-post-example.png\" alt=\"Newsjack blog post by Houzz on news of a mobile app launch\" width=\"1500\" style=\"width: 1500px; display: block; margin-left: auto; margin-right: auto;\" /></p> <p>\"Newsjacking\" is a nickname for \"hijacking\" your blog to break important news related to your industry. Therefore, the newsjack post is a type of article whose sole purpose is to garner consumers' attention and, while offering them timeless professional advice, prove your blog is a trusted resource for learning about the big things that happen in your industry.</p> <p>The newsjack example above was published by Houzz, a home decor merchant and interior design resource, about a new mobile app that launched just for interior designers. Houzz didn't launch the app, but the news of its launching is no less important to Houzz's audience.</p> <h3>6. Infographic Post</h3> <h4>Example: <a href=\"https://www.opencolleges.edu.au/careers/blog/key-benefits-of-studying-online-infographic\">The Key Benefits of Studying Online [Infographic]</a></h4> <p><img src=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/hs-fs/hubfs/studying-infographic-blog-post-example.jpeg?width=1500&amp;name=studying-infographic-blog-post-example.jpeg\" alt=\"Infographic blog post example - close-up of the infographic\" width=\"1500\" style=\"width: 1500px;\">The infographic post serves a similar purpose as the SlideShare post — the fourth example, explained above — in that it conveys information for which plain blog copy might not be the best format.</img></p> <p>For example, when you're looking to share a lot of statistical information (without boring or confusing your readers), building this data into a well-designed, even <a href=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/marketing/best-infographics-2016\">engaging infographic</a> can keep your readers engaged with your content. It also helps readers remember the information long after they leave your website.</p> <h3>7. How-to Post</h3> <h4>Example: How to Write a Blog Post: A Step-by-Step Guide</h4> <p>For this example, you need not look any further than the blog post you're reading right now! How-to guides like this one help solve a problem for your readers. They're like a cookbook for your industry, walking your audience through a project step by step to improve their literacy on the subject.</p> <p>The more posts like this you create, the more equipped your readers will be to work with you and invest in the services you offer.</p> <h3>8. Guest Post</h3> <h4>Example: <a href=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/marketing/ultimate-guide-social-media-image-dimensions-infographic\">Your Bookmarkable Guide to Social Media Image Sizes in 2020 [Infographic]</a></h4> <p><img src=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/hs-fs/hubfs/guest-post-example.jpeg?width=650&amp;name=guest-post-example.jpeg\" alt=\"Guest post example about social media sizes\" width=\"650\" style=\"width: 650px; margin-left: auto; margin-right: auto; display: block;\">Guest posts are a type of blog post that you can use to include other voices on your blog. For example, if you want to get an outside expert's opinion on a topic, a guest post is perfect for that.</img></p> <p>Additionally, these posts give your blog variety in topic and viewpoint. If your customer has a problem you can't solve, a guest post is a great solution.</p> <p>If you begin accepting guest posts, set up editorial guidelines to ensure they're up to the same standards as your posts.</p> <h2>Ready to blog?</h2> <p>Blogging can help you build brand awareness, become a thought-leader and expert in your industry, attract qualified leads, and boost conversions. Follow the steps and tips we covered above to begin publishing and enhancing your blog today.</p> <p><em>Editor's note: This post was originally published in October 2013 and has been updated for comprehensiveness.</em></p> <a class=\"cta_button\" href=\"https://www.hubspot.com/cs/ci/?pg=648420ad-1760-40e2-994f-7833315a7b7d&amp;pid=53&amp;ecid=&amp;hseid=&amp;hsic=\"><img class=\"hs-cta-img \" 01:35:38","updatedTime":"2021-04-24 01:35:38","title":"4 Content Types That Get Non-Organic Traffic, According to Content Strategists","link":"https://blog.hubspot.com/marketing/non-organic-traffic-content","description":"<p>Traffic is a low-impact word for most people but a high-impact word for marketers. Traffic can ultimately dictate success, whether it’s the number of leads that come to your website, visit your social channels, or watch your videos.</p> \n<p>There are two different types of traffic you can have, organic and non-organic, that can come from all over: email, social media, organic searches, backlinks — the list goes on.</p> \n<p>Non-organic traffic can be a bit harder to come by, which is why, when creating non-organic content, you want to ensure that it will drive results. However, it’s easier said than done when it comes to figuring out what works for your business. In this post, hear from HubSpot content strategists and marketers about the types of content that bring in the most non-organic traffic as inspiration for creating your own.</p> \n<p><a class=\"cta_button\" href=\"https://www.hubspot.com/cs/ci/?pg=a145a75e-59f6-4b51-a482-4f3ea486e740&amp;pid=53&amp;ecid=&amp;hseid=&amp;hsic=\"><img class=\"hs-cta-img \" style=\"border-width: 0px; /*hs-extra-styles*/; margin: 0 auto; display: block; margin-top: 20px; margin-bottom: 20px\" alt=\"Free Resource: Content Marketing Planning Template\" src=\"https://no-cache.hubspot.com/cta/default/53/a145a75e-59f6-4b51-a482-4f3ea486e740.png\" align=\"middle\"></a></p> \n<h2>4 Content Types That Get Non-Organic Traffic, According to Content Strategists</h2> \n<h3>Data-Driven Content</h3> \n<p>Pam Bump, Audience Growth Marketing Manager &amp; Staff Writer for the HubSpot Blogs, says that she often sees solid non-organic traffic from email and social media to blog posts that feature statistics or recent industry figures. Bump says, “People love to share, link to, or read up on new data that impacts their career, industry, or lives in some way.</p> \n<p>The data-driven content you share can be related to overall industry trends, stat roundup posts <a href=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/marketing/state-of-social-media-demographics?_ga=2.21103419.1067442037.1618000241-478881053.1618000241\">(like this one)</a>, and data comparison pieces, like this one about <a href=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/marketing/millennials-vs-gen-z?_ga=2.21103419.1067442037.1618000241-478881053.1618000241\">Millenials vs. Gen Z</a>, written by Bump herself.</p> \n<p>If you have the means, it’s worth considering running internal experiments and publishing your own original data. This can help you drive referrals and backlinks from other websites as non-organic leads and build your domain authority. When HubSpot does this, Bump says, “A credible website might include our data and say ‘according to Hubspot,’ and link to our original data post because it simply has information readers can’t get anywhere else.”</p> \n<h3>Content Featuring Quotes and Interviews</h3> \n<p>In the same vein as data-driven content, people want to learn something from what you have to offer, especially if they’re learning it from experienced industry leaders and professionals.</p> \n<p>Bump gives a piece titled <a href=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/marketing/marketing-predictions-experts?_ga=2.123980810.1067442037.1618000241-478881053.1618000241\">Marketing Trends to Watch in 2021, According to 21 Experts</a>, as an example. It was written by MOZ CMO Christina Mautz, and she included quotes from reputable industry leaders. The piece was shared on HubSpot social channels and emails and has since received a significant amount of views from non-organic sources in just three months.</p> \n<p>When you create content like this, the industry leaders you feature in the piece may share the posts with their audiences, helping you gain brand awareness and traffic from additional sources. Francesca McCaffrey, Tech Content Strategies, notes that leadership-type content brings in significant non-organic traffic for the HubSpot Product Blog, especially when shared on social media. She says, “Leadership thought pieces are also a significant source of non-organic traffic for us, as they tend to inspire lots of commentary and clicks on networking sites like LinkedIn.”</p> \n<h3>Emerging Trends</h3> \n<p>Making an effort to create content about emerging industry-related trends can do wonders in terms of attracting email, social media, and referral traffic.</p> \n<p>Bump wrote a post about <a href=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/marketing/what-is-clubhouse?_ga=2.123980810.1067442037.1618000241-478881053.1618000241\">Clubhouse</a>, a relatively new social platform that didn’t have high MSV search terms affiliated with it yet. Bump added headlines to the content that would gain traction when the app got bigger, like “What Is Clubhouse?” Since publication, the post has earned an impressive amount of non-organic views and, as expected, has picked up organic traffic as the app grows in popularity.</p> \n<p>Covering emerging trends also helps you stay on top of new keywords that aren’t as competitive. If you’re one of the only sources creating content for the keywords, search engines will recognize you as a source of authority when the trend becomes more popular.</p> \n<h3>Technical Guides and How-Tos</h3> \n<p>McCaffrey says that technical guides and how-to type content from the Product Blog submitted to reputable industry sites perform especially well with non-organic traffic.</p> \n<p>She gives <a href=\"https://product.hubspot.com/blog/how-to-learn-complex-things-quickly?_ga=2.123980810.1067442037.1618000241-478881053.1618000241\">this piece</a>&nbsp;as an example that was submitted to Hacker News, a reputable cybersecurity publication. McCaffrey says, “Making it to the first or second page of a site like Hacker News can really boost non-organic traffic, and translate into organic traffic over time. The piece made it to the front page, driving thousands of viewers to that post in a day.”</p> \n<p>Like pieces containing quotes and interviews, this type of content performs well because people can learn from it; they can take away actionable skills to apply to their own lives.</p> \n<p>All in all, the content you choose to create should directly relate to your business, as you’ll find the most success if you’re creating content your audience is already looking for.</p> \n<p>However, it’s worth considering purposely creating content that you know has the potential to bring in a significant amount of non-organic traffic. Leverage these tips from expert HubSpot content strategists, and begin<a href=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/marketing/content-creation?_ga=2.123980810.1067442037.1618000241-478881053.1618000241#:~:text=Content%20creation%20is%20the%20process,%2C%20infographic%2C%20or%20other%20format.\">&nbsp;creating content</a> that drives traffic.</p> \n<p></p> \n<p><a class=\"cta_button\" href=\"https://www.hubspot.com/cs/ci/?pg=870b6a31-0a25-444f-b61e-ff427ef5d5e9&amp;pid=53&amp;ecid=&amp;hseid=&amp;hsic=\"><img class=\"hs-cta-img \" style=\"border-width: 0px; \">","descriptionType":"html","publishedDate":"Wed, 21 Apr 2021 11:00:00 +0000","feedId":54,"bgimg":"https://no-cache.hubspot.com/cta/default/53/a145a75e-59f6-4b51-a482-4f3ea486e740.png","linkMd5":"969a138853dbbf07941ee256376a0560","bgimgJsdelivr":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx27/cdn27@2020_4/2021/04/23/17-35-38-450_f8c910eb1e0201f6.webp","destWidth":483,"destHeight":60,"sourceBytes":4217,"destBytes":7328,"author":"fneedle@hubspot.com (Flori Needle)","articleImgCdnMap":{"https://no-cache.hubspot.com/cta/default/53/a145a75e-59f6-4b51-a482-4f3ea486e740.png":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx27/cdn27@2020_4/2021/04/23/17-35-38-450_f8c910eb1e0201f6.webp","https://no-cache.hubspot.com/cta/default/53/870b6a31-0a25-444f-b61e-ff427ef5d5e9.png":null,"https://track.hubspot.com/__ptq.gif?a=53&k=14&r=https%3A%2F%2Fblog.hubspot.com%2Fmarketing%2Fnon-organic-traffic-content&bu=https%253A%252F%252Fblog.hubspot.com%252Fmarketing&bvt=rss":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx21/cdn4@2020_5/2021/04/23/17-35-49-794_bd8728f55c69cc68.webp"},"publishedOrCreatedDate":1619199338326},{"createdTime":"2021-04-24 01:35:38","updatedTime":"2021-04-24 01:35:38","title":"How Brands Creatively Hosted Virtual Offsite Meetings","link":"https://blog.hubspot.com/marketing/virtual-offsites","description":"<p>As the world continues to move in a remote-first direction, it's important to consider how to make your company's in-person events remote-friendly.</p> \n<p>Even if you don't always do remote events, the remote option is great for anytime your team is spread around the world.</p> \n<p></p> \n<p>But, a virtual offsite meeting? Sounds oxymoronic. How can you have an offsite, that doesn't feel like work, virtually?</p> \n<p>In this post, we'll take a deep dive into how these brands thought about virtual offsites in a creative way. And didn't just ask everyone to be on Zoom for 8 hours.</p> \n<p><a class=\"cta_button\" href=\"https://www.hubspot.com/cs/ci/?pg=52250291-8fed-4fe7-ad28-e6e244e1fcd8&amp;pid=53&amp;ecid=&amp;hseid=&amp;hsic=\"><img class=\"hs-cta-img \" style=\"border-width: 0px; /*hs-extra-styles*/; margin: 0 auto; display: block; margin-top: 20px; margin-bottom: 20px\" alt=\"Download our complete productivity guide here for more tips on improving your  productivity at work.\" src=\"https://no-cache.hubspot.com/cta/default/53/52250291-8fed-4fe7-ad28-e6e244e1fcd8.png\" align=\"middle\"></a></p> \n<p></p> \n<h3>1. Loom VR Virtual Offsite</h3> \n<p>At the end of 2020, Loom decided to host a virtual offsite. What made this different than attending an 8-hour Zoom meeting?</p> \n<p>Well, first, the company sent VR headsets to their team to allow employees to feel like they were leaving their homes for a large company meeting they used to travel for.</p> \n<blockquote class=\"twitter-tweet\"> \n <p>We just announced our <a href=\"https://twitter.com/loom?ref_src=twsrc%5Etfw\">@loom</a> offsite being done in VR and us shipping everyone an Oculus headset. The smiles. 🙂</p> — Vinay Hiremath (@vhmth) \n <a href=\"https://twitter.com/vhmth/status/1337084527739473920?ref_src=twsrc%5Etfw\">December 10, 2020</a>\n</blockquote>  \n<p>According to <a href=\"https://www.loom.com/blog/virtual-offsite-tips\">Loom</a>, \"with virtual reality, we were able to send everyone an <a href=\"https://www.oculus.com/quest-2/\">Oculus Quest 2</a> headset to bring the virtual world to them. Plus, we were able to limit Zoom content to only two hours per day to keep the content engaging.\"</p> \n<p>Once they got started with virtual reality, they had to find virtual reality apps to host their events. But they also included their employees in the planning process. The company sent a Google Form to employees to share any ideas for activities and sessions they could do during the virtual offsite.</p> \n<p>Loom worked with a partner to create a virtual reality island where team members could go for watercooler conversations, ice breakers, and happy hour.</p> \n<p>Interestingly, the virtual reality component was not mandatory. Any events that were VR exclusives were optional. And the VR island they created was also accessible via desktop, so everyone could participate.</p> \n<p>It's important to remember that when you're creating a virtual offsite experience, you want everyone to be able to show up. Hopefully, the tools you use will be available on several devices or you can make those events not mandatory if it takes a special device.</p> \n<p>The team also created unstructured time during their day so that people working from home could still do their normal work and activities.</p> \n<h3>2. First Round Review Interactive Virtual Offsite</h3> \n<p>Another company thinking about virtual offsites creatively is First Round Review.</p> \n<p><a href=\"https://review.firstround.com/use-this-startups-playbook-for-running-impactful-virtual-offsites\">First Round Review held a virtual offsite</a> and had activities including group meals, cooking competitions, self-reflection exercises, group presentations, unconference events, and more.</p> \n<p>The company knew that they wanted to use all different kinds of formats for their activities so that they could keep people's attention.</p> \n<p>Before they planned the event, they wrote down their objectives, breaking them into task- and team-focused outcomes. Then, they came up with ideas to achieve those outcomes.</p> \n<p>Again, First Round Review knew they didn't want to spend all day on Zoom. A few things they did to make their virtual offsite interactive and successful were:</p> \n<ul> \n <li>Send an interactive surprise: The team sent everyone a kit that they were instructed not to open beforehand. The kit included candy, a chalkboard to write on, coffee, and a kombucha starter kit. This was a fun way to kick off the virtual offsite.</li> \n <li>Get in costume: The team was all sent special hats and everyone showed up to the meeting wearing their merch.</li> \n <li>Cooking challenge: Groups were split into breakout rooms so each group could cook together live. Then, everyone presented their meals together and people voted on creativity and presentation.</li> \n <li>Unstructured time: This is huge. Don't make people spend all day on the computer. Include unstructured time and breaks.</li> \n <li>Playtime: Include team bonding events such as trivia or virtual escape rooms. First Round Review even hired a magician to join them for a group dinner.</li> \n <li>Show gratitude: First Round Review spent an entire meeting having everyone write out gratitude for every team member and then emailed everyone their list of comments from their coworkers. For each teammate, they had everyone spend one minute answering by writing a line or two in response to the following questions: What's something you admire about this individual? What's something this person did recently that you appreciate? Why are you grateful to count this person as a teammate? Answers are anonymous. After they're all in, the meeting owner will round up the lines for each individual and share them in a private email.</li> \n</ul> \n<p>One of the biggest takeaways from this virtual offsite is that you can have several formats, different sessions, interactive and engaging content, and still get work done in strategy sessions.</p> \n<h3>3. Wikimedia Product Team Virtual Offsite</h3> \n<p>The <a href=\"https://medium.com/@ItsJazTanner/how-planning-a-virtual-offsite-prepared-me-for-covid-19-remote-work-c0e92bb4fefb\">Wikimedia Foundation Product team</a> also had productive virtual strategy sessions and meaningful team bonding in a remote environment across various time zones.</p> \n<p>To achieve this, a lot of planning went into it. The team first decided what story they wanted to tell during their offsite. To ensure this was discussed throughout the virtual offsite, they revisited their product roadmap to understand where the team had been and where they're going. On the first day, they held a retrospective to accomplish this.</p> \n<p>Ultimately, the creative way that the company thought about this offsite was in the agenda and planning.</p> \n<p>If there was a presentation or low energy session, they wanted to make sure it was followed up by a high engagement interactive session.</p> \n<p>Additionally, the timing was important. They decided that instead of having 8-hour Zoom meetings, they'd have four hours of virtual sessions a day, broken into 2-hour blocks with a break in between of about 1.5-2 hours.</p> \n<p>The offsite included low energy sessions including a Q&amp;A with the Chief Product Officer, where they prepared questions ahead of time and used a thirty-minute window to go through their questions. But followed up those sessions with interactive activities.</p> \n<p>One session even had team members create a homepage for newcomers based on previous features built by the product team. This had the team actively working in the tool so they could see what features stand out.</p> \n<p>They also had a session with a specialist that was a step-by-step process of the Wikipedia editing process so employees understand the user experience.</p> \n<p>Other fun sessions included friendly games online.</p> \n<p>When planning a virtual offsite, it's important to consider the timing and energy levels of the event. Spending all day on a video conferencing tool isn't going to be effective for most people.</p> \n<p>Hosting a virtual offsite doesn't need to be an overly complicated process. And it doesn't need to be a boring, 8-hour long Zoom meeting. You can host interactive sessions, presentations, and truly engage with your employees.</p> \n<p><a class=\"cta_button\" href=\"https://www.hubspot.com/cs/ci/?pg=57b789cd-3ca2-4d6b-b792-77e5b1163125&amp;pid=53&amp;ecid=&amp;hseid=&amp;hsic=\"><img class=\"hs-cta-img \" style=\"border-width: 0px; /*hs-extra-styles*/; \"
