01:35:38","updatedTime":"2021-04-24 01:35:38","title":"How I Grew the HubSpot Podcast Skill Up Audience by 271% in Two Months","link":"https://blog.hubspot.com/marketing/grew-podcast-skillup-audience","description":"<p><em>This post is a part of Made @ HubSpot, an internal thought leadership series through which we extract lessons from experiments conducted by our very own HubSpotters.</em></p> \n<p>There are <a href=\"https://twitter.com/ChaddHollowed/status/1368756033867325442?s=09&amp;utm_source=podnews.net&amp;utm_medium=email&amp;utm_campaign=podnews.net%3A2021-03-08\">72,000 new podcast episodes each day</a> — which means there are five new podcasts made every six seconds.</p> \n<p>And, as of March 2020, there are a reported <a href=\"https://www.podcastinsights.com/podcast-statistics/\">1.9 million total podcasts, and 47 million total episodes</a>. Depending on when you read this article, these numbers could be drastically different.</p> \n<p>Which is all to say: The podcast industry is <em>rapidly</em>&nbsp;growing.</p> \n<p>In a world of fast-growing competition, how do we — as podcast marketers — compete for listeners' attention, while also expanding reach and growing our audiences?</p> \n<p>I wish that I could tell you that I have it all figured out. However, <em>not</em>&nbsp;having it figured out is what ultimately led to a 271% increase in downloads for season six of HubSpot's podcast, <em><a href=\"https://www.hubspot.com/podcasts/skill-up\">Skill Up</a></em>.</p> \n<p>Here, I'll share my lessons for how I achieved that growth.</p> \n<p><a class=\"cta_button\" href=\"https://www.hubspot.com/cs/ci/?pg=e84f333b-91fb-4c8e-bacd-5c4cd1ebaf9b&amp;pid=53&amp;ecid=&amp;hseid=&amp;hsic=\"><img class=\"hs-cta-img \" style=\"border-width: 0px; /*hs-extra-styles*/; margin: 0 auto; display: block; margin-top: 20px; margin-bottom: 20px\" alt=\"➝ Free Guide: How to Start a Podcast\" src=\"https://no-cache.hubspot.com/cta/default/53/e84f333b-91fb-4c8e-bacd-5c4cd1ebaf9b.png\" align=\"middle\"></a></p> \n<h3 style=\"font-weight: normal;\">Lesson 1: There are a lot&nbsp;of podcast listening platforms.</h3> \n<p>When you think of podcast platforms, Apple Podcasts, Spotify, and Google Podcasts are probably top of mind, right?</p> \n<p>Well, there are many, <em>many</em>&nbsp;more listening platforms beyond those three.</p> \n<p>I downloaded every podcast platform available through the App Store on my iPhone. This included Podcast Addict, Overcast, Castro, PlayerFM, Pandora, Pocket Casts, and about ten others.</p> \n<p>I then cross-referenced the players I downloaded with the audience application report from Megaphone. If there was a small or nonexistent audience on a platform, I highlighted it.</p> \n<p>The first recommendation I can make is to look at <em>where</em>&nbsp;people are listening to your podcasts using the reporting provided by <a href=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/marketing/podcast-tools\">your podcast host</a>. Are the majority of your downloads coming from Apple or Spotify? If your answer is yes, then that's good news. You have untapped audiences on other platforms, including PlayerFM and Podcast Addict.</p> \n<p>Which brings me to my next recommendation …</p> \n<h3 style=\"font-weight: normal;\">Lesson 2: Paid ad placements on podcast platforms pay off.</h3> \n<p>After I had a list of podcast platforms that would allow me to expand the reach of my podcast, I opened each platform and took note of their ad placements. I looked for anything that said \"Sponsored\" or something along those lines. If I liked the ad placement, I included it in my list.</p> \n<p>Next, I focused on gathering data on ad cost, estimated CPM, and estimated downloads for the placements I was interested in. This is relatively easy, since many of the platforms share both the ad placements available and estimated campaign results on their websites.</p> \n<p>If they don't have the information available on their website, you can email the podcast platforms' advertising team, who will provide you with that information.</p> \n<p>After gathering this data, I assessed the best ads for<em>Skill Up</em>. Fortunately, before I joined HubSpot, my manager had already run ads on podcast listening platforms — which meant I had data to reference to make more informed decisions.</p> \n<p>If you haven't run ads on a listening platform previously, I have good news for you: Ad placements range from $165 to $3,000, so even if you don't have a large budget, you can likely still experiment with these types of ads.</p> \n<h3 style=\"font-weight: normal;\">Lesson 3: Episode-specific promotions are incredibly effective.</h3> \n<p>Within my marketing plan for the launch of season six, I focused on promotions that announced the upcoming season.</p> \n<p>The season was comprised of five episodes that were released over the span of three weeks, so it made sense to drive awareness towards the new episodes. The <a href=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/marketing/podcast-advertising-tips\">podcast ad copy</a>&nbsp;read something along the lines of, \"A new season of<em>Skill Up</em>&nbsp;is here!\"</p> \n<p>Towards the end of the season, however, it didn't make sense to announce the season anymore. Instead, I created episode-specific promotions.</p> \n<blockquote> \n <p style=\"font-weight: normal;\">In comparison to the show promotions, the episode highlights resonated better with audiences and increased our conversions through distribution channels, such as email.</p> \n</blockquote> \n<p>Here's an example:</p> \n<p><em>HubSpot's Skill Up podcast presents … “How a Sales Manager at LinkedIn Builds a Buyer-first Selling Strategy”</em></p> \n<p><em>What's the best selling strategy in 2021? Kwesi Graves, Sales Manager at LinkedIn, champions the \"buyer-first selling\" methodology, which prioritizes quality over quantity, emphasizes the importance of the buyer's context, and encourages his team of reps to spend more time researching than reaching out. If you're a manager, sales leader, or rep looking to transform how you sell in 2021, this is a great place to start! </em><em><strong>Listen now:</strong></em></p> \n<div>\n <iframe style=\"border: none; margin: 0px auto; display: block;\" src=\"https://listen.casted.us/player/00907c0c\" width=\"560\" height=\"315\"></iframe>  \n</div> \n<p>Episode-specific advertisements also performed much better than season advertisements. Unfortunately, however, most podcast listening platforms don't allow episode-specific advertisements.</p> \n<p>There is one that does: PlayerFM. Our episode-specific ads on PlayerFM outperformed all our other ad campaigns. Hopefully, more podcast platforms will eventually offer the same.</p> \n<p>While I wouldn't say these initiatives are revolutionary, they were incredibly effective for us. Our team is on an exciting journey where experimentation and innovation are key to success.</p> \n<p>For any podcast marketers in the industry — This is just the beginning.</p> \n<p><a class=\"cta_button\" href=\"https://www.hubspot.com/cs/ci/?pg=97c040a4-1571-4fce-86c1-aa11f2a814f6&amp;pid=53&amp;ecid=&amp;hseid=&amp;hsic=\"><img class=\"hs-cta-img \" style=\"border-width: 0px; /*hs-extra-styles*/; \" alt=\"New Call-to-action\" src=\"https://no-cache.hubspot.com/cta/default/53/97c040a4-1571-4fce-86c1-aa11f2a814f6.png\"></a></p> \n<p></p>  \n<img src=\"https://track.hubspot.com/__ptq.gif?a=53&amp;k=14&amp;r=https%3A%2F%2Fblog.hubspot.com%2Fmarketing%2Fgrew-podcast-skillup-audience&amp;bu=https%253A%252F%252Fblog.hubspot.com%252Fmarketing&amp;bvt=rss\" alt=\"\" width=\"1\" height=\"1\" style=\"min-height:1px!important;width:1px!important;border-width:0!important;margin-top:0!important;margin-bottom:0!important;margin-right:0!important;margin-left:0!important;padding-top:0!important;padding-bottom:0!important;padding-right:0!important;padding-left:0!important; \">","descriptionType":"html","publishedDate":"Mon, 19 Apr 2021 11:00:00 +0000","feedId":54,"bgimg":"https://no-cache.hubspot.com/cta/default/53/e84f333b-91fb-4c8e-bacd-5c4cd1ebaf9b.png","linkMd5":"73b8a435674720f10bf21da7e0de9786","bgimgJsdelivr":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx32/cdn16@2020_6/2021/04/23/17-35-44-459_4f70bc26ad5170f8.webp","destWidth":465,"destHeight":59,"sourceBytes":5600,"destBytes":7594,"author":"Alanah Joseph","articleImgCdnMap":{"https://no-cache.hubspot.com/cta/default/53/e84f333b-91fb-4c8e-bacd-5c4cd1ebaf9b.png":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx32/cdn16@2020_6/2021/04/23/17-35-44-459_4f70bc26ad5170f8.webp","https://no-cache.hubspot.com/cta/default/53/97c040a4-1571-4fce-86c1-aa11f2a814f6.png":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx1/cdn67@2020_6/2021/04/23/17-35-48-747_6113db5ca48c5ff8.webp","https://track.hubspot.com/__ptq.gif?a=53&k=14&r=https%3A%2F%2Fblog.hubspot.com%2Fmarketing%2Fgrew-podcast-skillup-audience&bu=https%253A%252F%252Fblog.hubspot.com%252Fmarketing&bvt=rss":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx2/cdn12@2020_6/2021/04/23/17-35-49-943_c2ce37ee13739ce2.webp"},"publishedOrCreatedDate":1619199338326},{"createdTime":"2021-04-24 01:35:38","updatedTime":"2021-04-24 01:35:38","title":"The Most Annoying Types of Ads & What to Do Instead [New Data]","link":"https://blog.hubspot.com/marketing/worst-ads-poll-survey","description":"<p><a href=\"https://www.edelman.com/research/trust-barometer-special-report-in-brands-we-trust\">A 2019 Edelman study</a> found that three out of four consumers avoid ads. In fact, 47% said they have changed their media habits to see fewer ads while others use ad blockers to prevent them altogether.</p>  \n<p>The reasons why vary.</p> \n<p>Personally, I hate repetitive ads. For about a month straight, every time I would watch a YouTube video, I would see the same ad and it got more irritating every time. Mostly because I wasn't interested in the brand or its services. But the incessant nature of the ad led to me develop a negative association with the company.</p> \n<p><a class=\"cta_button\" href=\"https://www.hubspot.com/cs/ci/?pg=da1bfbbd-7ee9-4bf1-89d1-6d7a833deb08&amp;pid=53&amp;ecid=&amp;hseid=&amp;hsic=\"><img class=\"hs-cta-img \" style=\"border-width: 0px; /*hs-extra-styles*/; \" alt=\"Download Now: Free Ad Campaign Planning Kit\" src=\"https://no-cache.hubspot.com/cta/default/53/da1bfbbd-7ee9-4bf1-89d1-6d7a833deb08.png\"></a></p> \n<p>So, how can brands deliver ads that audiences <em>want</em> to see? To know that, let's first look at what they definitely don't like.</p> \n<h2>The Most Annoying Advertisement Types</h2> \n<p>We surveyed 302 people using <a href=\"http://luc.id\">Lucid</a> to ask them about what ads they're most annoyed by.</p> \n<p>When we asked the random survey pool, \"What's the most annoying type of digital ad?\", a whopping 58% of respondents said pop-up ads that negatively impact the user experience.</p> \n<p style=\"text-align: center;\"><img alt=\"2021 Lucid Survey Most Annoying Ad Types\" src=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/hubfs/Google%20Drive%20Integration/The%20Most%20Annoying%20Advertisement%20Types%20%26%20What%20to%20Do%20Instead%20%5BResearch%5D-1.png\" style=\"margin-left: auto; margin-right: auto; display: block;\" title=\"\"></p> \n<p style=\"text-align: center; font-size: 12px;\"><a href=\"http://luc.id\">Data Source</a></p> \n<p>While advertising can be unavoidable for brands based on their goals, there are ways to produce ads that don't annoy your audience. Below, we dive into the two most annoying ads types and explain how marketers and advertisers can navigate.</p> \n<h3>Pop-Up Ads.</h3> \n<p>When you think about it, this result isn't too shocking. We've all gone through it. You land on a website and before you can even scroll, you're hit with a big pop-up ad that takes up the whole screen. You close it, then get hit with another pop-up on the bottom of your screen, making it harder to navigate the site.</p> \n<p>At this stage, many viewers just drop off.</p> \n<p>This is an issue that affects both publishers and advertisers. The more visitors a publisher has, the higher the rate they will charge for their ad inventory. However, if a site is known to have incessant pop-up ads (looking right at you, recipe websites), visitors may be reluctant to visit that site again. This can lead to lower traffic and eventually less ad revenue.</p> \n<p>This is equally impactful to advertisers who want users to convert on their ads. You know how they say journalists should never become the story? Well, ads should never be noticed for their placement instead of their content.</p> \n<p>Let's say your ads are displayed in ways that hinder the user experience. At worst, consumers will start to build a negative perception of your brand and at best, they'll simply be too distracted by the placement or timing of the ad to care about the content. Either way, it's a lose-lose situation.</p> \n<h3>Pre- or Mid-Roll Video Ads</h3> \n<p>When it comes to video ads, things get tricky.</p> \n<p>Our study found that the second most annoying ad type is the one that plays before or during a video or show. In addition, a <a href=\"https://www.revjet.com/ad-experience-sentiment-report-q319\">2019 study by RevJet </a>found that 100% of consumers will skip the ad whenever possible.</p> \n<p>The solution here isn't to stop producing video ads altogether. It's to leverage the short time you have to capture your audience's attention and encourage them to engage with your video.</p> \n<p>This could be by addressing their pain points or using emotional appeal. Determining what works best for your audience will require a lot of experimentation. It may take time to figure out the right formula but once you do, you can create videos with confidence that your audience will be entertained.</p> \n<p>Now that we know what annoys consumers, let's talk about what consumers actually want to see.</p> \n<h2>What Consumers Want in Ads</h2> \n<h3>Plan your ad with user experience in mind.</h3> \n<p>When deciding on your ad format, placement, and timing, it's important to consider the user experience.</p> \n<p>Take pop-up ads, they are inherently disruptive. In this case, you may want to display them once your user has exhibited a high-engagement behavior on the site. This can be spending X amount of minutes on a page or visiting other pages on the website.</p> \n<p>With this tactic, your user may be less likely to dismiss your ad as they are already highly engaged with the page.</p> \n<h3>Find the right balance in ad frequency.</h3> \n<p>The RevJet study found that over 72% of consumers dislike brands with repetitive messaging in their ads.</p> \n<p>While ad frequency can help you reach your goals, there is a point where it no longer yields positive results.</p> \n<p><a href=\"https://www.facebook.com/business/news/insights/a-data-driven-exploration-of-optimal-ad-frequency?ref=search_new_0#\">A 2020 Facebook IQ study</a> found that for brand lift campaigns, more impressions do lead to better ad recall and action intent. However, after a certain number of impressions, the benefits plateau.</p> \n<p>In 2019, <a href=\"https://www.socialmediatoday.com/news/snapchat-publishes-new-report-on-optimal-ad-frequency-to-drive-recall-and-a/554878/\">Snapchat found</a> that the sweet spot was one to two ads per week. However, this number can vary greatly depending on several factors.</p> \n<p>The key takeaway is that more doesn't always equal better when it comes to users.</p> \n<h3>Don't get too invasive.</h3> \n<p>Yes, <a href=\"https://info.innovid.com/2020-consumer-attitudes\">consumers like personalized ads</a>. But there's a difference between personal and creepy, and that's the balance every brand has to strike.</p> \n<p>We surveyed 300 people and asked them about which ads feel the most invasive. The top answer was ads based on their recent online searches.</p> \n<p style=\"text-align: center;\"><img alt=\"2021 Lucid Survey Most Invasive Ad Types\" src=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/hubfs/Google%20Drive%20Integration/The%20Most%20Annoying%20Advertisement%20Types%20%26%20What%20to%20Do%20Instead%20%5BResearch%5D.png\" style=\"margin-left: auto; margin-right: auto; display: block;\" title=\"\"></p> \n<p style=\"text-align: center; font-size: 12px;\"><a href=\"http://luc.id\">Data Source</a></p> \n<p>The RevJet survey echoed these results, with 60% of consumers stating they do not find retargeting ads helpful.</p> \n<p>What consumers may prefer are contextual and demographical ads, according to a <a href=\"https://info.innovid.com/2020-consumer-attitudes#5\">2020 Innovid Study</a>. For instance, seeing an ad for a blender as you're looking up recipes or seeing an ad for a store located in your area.</p> \n<p>There's no hard-and-fast rule for determining what's helpful or too invasive. Experiment and see what works for your brand, then use that data to inform your future ad strategy.</p> \n<h3>Keep it short and concise.</h3> \n<p>When it comes to video ads, most consumers are not willing to watch them to completion.</p> \n<p>A key finding in the RevJet study was that users are willing to abandon their videos if it means sitting through a long ad.</p> \n<p>Twenty-eight percent of consumers between the ages of 18 to 44 will drop off if the ad exceeds 10 seconds. That rate rises incrementally as video length increases.</p> \n<p>That said, keep your ads short and to the point. If you do opt for a longer ad, have a strong opening that will encourage your audience to keep watching.</p> \n<p>It's important to note that these tips provide insights into consumer perception and can help steer you in the right direction. However, it's only by experimenting that you will determine which strategies yield the best results to achieve your marketing goals.</p> \n<p><a class=\"cta_button\" href=\"https://www.hubspot.com/cs/ci/?pg=46d72524-f4a7-44e9-9af0-935be9bb3891&amp;pid=53&amp;ecid=&amp;hseid=&amp;hsic=\"><img class=\"hs-cta-img \" style=\"border-width: 0px; /*hs-extra-styles*/; \" alt=\"advertising plan\" src=\"https://no-cache.hubspot.com/cta/default/53/46d72524-f4a7-44e9-9af0-935be9bb3891.png\"></a></p> \n<p></p>  \n<img Bretous)","articleImgCdnMap":{"https://no-cache.hubspot.com/cta/default/53/da1bfbbd-7ee9-4bf1-89d1-6d7a833deb08.png":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx30/cdn13@2020_6/2021/04/23/17-35-38-453_91a8856cb36791e3.webp","https://blog.hubspot.com/hubfs/Google%20Drive%20Integration/The%20Most%20Annoying%20Advertisement%20Types%20%26%20What%20to%20Do%20Instead%20%5BResearch%5D-1.png":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx14/cdn44@2020_6/2021/04/23/17-35-48-815_c3019972c6f8fdf4.webp","https://blog.hubspot.com/hubfs/Google%20Drive%20Integration/The%20Most%20Annoying%20Advertisement%20Types%20%26%20What%20to%20Do%20Instead%20%5BResearch%5D.png":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx2/cdn92@2020_6/2021/04/23/17-35-49-020_8dd4568f784c0123.webp","https://no-cache.hubspot.com/cta/default/53/46d72524-f4a7-44e9-9af0-935be9bb3891.png":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx23/cdn83@2020_1/2021/04/23/17-35-49-960_8e21eaa098288b31.webp","https://track.hubspot.com/__ptq.gif?a=53&k=14&r=https%3A%2F%2Fblog.hubspot.com%2Fmarketing%2Fworst-ads-poll-survey&bu=https%253A%252F%252Fblog.hubspot.com%252Fmarketing&bvt=rss":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx6/cdn15@2020_4/2021/04/23/17-35-49-413_d9ef9d1797e600e7.webp"},"publishedOrCreatedDate":1619199338326},{"createdTime":"2021-04-24 01:35:38","updatedTime":"2021-04-24 01:35:38","title":"6 Creative Strategies for Getting Traffic from Pinterest","link":"https://blog.hubspot.com/marketing/get-traffic-pinterest","description":"<p>Pinterest is an undeniably powerful opportunity to reach and convert new audiences.</p> \n<p>If you don't believe me, consider this: The platform has over <a href=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/blog/tabid/6307/bid/31147/the-ultimate-guide-to-mastering-pinterest-for-marketing.aspx\">250 million users</a>. And roughly <a href=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/blog/tabid/6307/bid/31147/the-ultimate-guide-to-mastering-pinterest-for-marketing.aspx\">90% of those Pinterest users say they look at content</a>&nbsp;on the network to make purchasing decisions.</p> \n<p>However, excelling on Pinterest versus using Pinterest as a strong distribution channel are two different things.</p> \n<p>If you're starting to see an uptick in followers on your Pinterest account, you might want to consider how you can turn those followers into real leads and customers for your business.</p> \n<p>Here, let's explore some creative strategies for turning the followers you get on Pinterest into traffic for your website and social channels.</p> \n<p><a class=\"cta_button\" href=\"https://www.hubspot.com/cs/ci/?pg=61ef3959-6721-4b92-8666-48ecb4d2f35c&amp;pid=53&amp;ecid=&amp;hseid=&amp;hsic=\"><img class=\"hs-cta-img \" style=\"border-width: 0px; /*hs-extra-styles*/; margin: 0 auto; display: block; margin-top: 20px; margin-bottom: 20px\" alt=\"Free Resource:&nbsp;12 Pinterest Templates for Business\" src=\"https://no-cache.hubspot.com/cta/default/53/61ef3959-6721-4b92-8666-48ecb4d2f35c.png\" align=\"middle\"></a></p> \n<h3 style=\"font-weight: normal;\">1. Create boards using relevant keywords.</h3> \n<p>A board — or an organized compilation of related pins, for easier discoverability — is a necessary component for a good user experience on Pinterest.</p> \n<p>For instance, <a href=\"https://www.pinterest.com/coschedule/_created/\">CoSchedule</a>, which has almost 17,000 followers on Pinterest, has organized their pins into boards titled \"Content Marketing\", \"Social Media Marketing\", \"Marketing Inspiration\", and more:</p> \n<p><img alt=\"CoSchedule's Pinterest Boards\" src=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/hs-fs/hubfs/Google%20Drive%20Integration/6%20Creative%20Strategies%20for%20Getting%20Traffic%20from%20Pinterest-2.png?width=624&amp;name=6%20Creative%20Strategies%20for%20Getting%20Traffic%20from%20Pinterest-2.png\" style=\"margin-left: 0.00px;\" title=\"\" width=\"624\"></p> \n<p>New followers can easily find the pins they're looking for using these broader categories, which is why it makes sense to use popular keywords when creating your boards, as CoSchedule did.</p> \n<p>Additionally, these keyword-optimized boards can help make your Pinterest content more discoverable on search engines when someone searches for related keywords — particularly on Google Image searches, since Pinterest is primarily a visual channel:</p> \n<p><img alt=\"The image search results page on Google for the search term, &quot;best marketing statistics&quot;\" src=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/hs-fs/hubfs/Google%20Drive%20Integration/6%20Creative%20Strategies%20for%20Getting%20Traffic%20from%20Pinterest.jpeg?width=624&amp;name=6%20Creative%20Strategies%20for%20Getting%20Traffic%20from%20Pinterest.jpeg\" style=\"margin-left: 0.00px;\" title=\"\" width=\"624\"></p> \n<p>As shown above, two images from Pinterest arise on Google's Images search page for the search term, \"Best marketing statistics\". By <a href=\"https://help.pinterest.com/en/business/article/create-a-board\">creating boards</a>&nbsp;with searchable keywords, you're more likely to reach users both on, and off, Pinterest.</p> \n<h3><span style=\"font-weight: normal;\">2. Leverage Rich pins to ensure your Pinterest content is up-to-date.</span></h3> \n<p>Simply put, Rich pins can sync with your website to ensure your content is up-to-date on Pinterest when you make any changes to those pages on your site. &nbsp;</p> \n<p>There are a few reasons you might use Rich pins. If you post your products on Pinterest, Product Rich Pins can ensure availability and pricing are updated automatically as those factors change on your ecommerce site.</p> \n<p>If you post recipes, alternatively, then Recipe Rich pins can add extra information to the recipes you pin to your site — including serving size, diet preference, and ratings — for increased discoverability.</p> \n<p>Finally, Article Rich Pins will add headlines, titles, description, and author byline information of the article or blog post to your Pinterest site when you pin an article.</p> \n<p>These small details go a long way towards ensuring your Pinterest content is always fresh as users find it. Particularly if you're aiming to drive sales for products from Pinterest, it's important to use Product Rich Pins so people aren't frustrated when they find pricing or other information is different between Pinterest and your product pages.</p> \n<h3><span style=\"font-weight: normal;\">3. Pin consistently, and often.</span></h3> \n<p>You can't expect much traffic from Pinterest if you don't regularly pin content on the platform. Pinterest, like any social network, requires dedicated, long-term work to see results.</p> \n<p>You wouldn't expect to write one blog post for your website and see a major, steady flow of traffic as a result — and the same goes for Pinterest.</p> \n<p>Additionally, as your followers grow, you want to provide high-quality, interesting content to increase brand loyalty and <em>keep </em>those followers active on your page. By regularly pinning, you're increasing your odds of converting those followers into fans of your brand — which will ultimately drive them off Pinterest, and onto your website or social pages.</p> \n<h3 style=\"font-weight: normal;\">4. Optimize your pins — and boards — for search.</h3> \n<p>At its core, Pinterest is essentially its own visual search engine. And, similar to other search engines, keyword-optimized content performs best on the network.</p> \n<p>Additionally, keyword optimizing your Pinterest profile increases your chances to rank organically on <em>other</em> search engines, and drive traffic from search engines like Google to your Pinterest site.</p> \n<p>To optimize your Pinterest page, consider inserting brand-related keywords into your bio and profile, pin descriptions, board titles, board descriptions, and even the image alt-text of content you post on Pinterest.</p> \n<p>This can help your images appear on Google's Image search results, as well as improve your chances of ranking on Pinterest for your intended keywords.</p> \n<h3><span style=\"font-weight: normal;\">5. Create pin-worthy images, and use those images to link out to original content on your website or social pages.</span></h3> \n<p>One of the easiest ways to drive traffic back to your website is by creating unique, original content specifically for Pinterest, and then using that pin to link back to your website or blog post.</p> \n<p>For instance, consider the <a href=\"https://www.pinterest.com/pin/23784704271599911/\">infographic below</a>, which I found when searching \"best social media platforms\" on Pinterest:</p> \n<p><img alt=\"an infographic on Pinterest by digichefs titled &quot;which is the best social media platform for your brand?'\" src=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/hubfs/Google%20Drive%20Integration/6%20Creative%20Strategies%20for%20Getting%20Traffic%20from%20Pinterest.png\" style=\"margin-left: auto; margin-right: auto; display: block;\" title=\"\"></p> \n<p>It's a good idea to create unique, standalone value with your images for Pinterest. In this case, I can find my answer to \"best social media platforms\" by looking at the infographic itself without ever leaving Pinterest — which makes for a better user experience.</p> \n<p>However, if I've found unique value in the content, I might want to click the brand's website to learn more about their business or see additional content. When I click on the digichef URL, I'm taken to the <a href=\"https://digichefs.com/which-social-media-platform-is-best-for-your-brand-infographic/\">original page for the infographic, on the business' website</a>:</p> \n<p><img alt=\"A blog post on digichef's website, which includes the original infographic on social media platforms that you can also find on Pinterest. \" src=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/hs-fs/hubfs/Google%20Drive%20Integration/6%20Creative%20Strategies%20for%20Getting%20Traffic%20from%20Pinterest-1.png?width=624&amp;name=6%20Creative%20Strategies%20for%20Getting%20Traffic%20from%20Pinterest-1.png\" style=\"margin-left: 0.00px;\" title=\"\" width=\"624\"></p> \n<p>You might try a similar approach with your own Pinterest strategy. Consider how you can create unique, standalone content that will perform well on Pinterest. Alternatively, perhaps you can post infographics or other visual assets you've already created for your brand on Pinterest, with a link back to your site.</p> \n<h3><span style=\"font-weight: normal;\">6. Follow similar brands for content inspiration, as well as opportunities to re-pin images that align with your brand.</span></h3> \n<p>With Pinterest, each pin you save doesn't have to be original branded content. Instead, one easy opportunity to increase engagement is to re-pin images that align with your brand to share with your own followers.</p> \n<p>Additionally, following other brands can increase traffic to your own Pinterest profile and, ultimately, your website. When you follow someone on Pinterest, Pinterest sends a notification letting them know they have a new follower. Some of those people may then follow you back in return, which is a good way to grow your audience.</p> \n<p>Following similar brands can also help you identify popular or trending content on other profiles, as well as gaps in your own Pinterest content strategy.</p> \n<p>If you work at a home decor ecommerce store, for instance, you might find that many competitors are posting 'Easter Home Decor' images:</p> \n<p><img alt=\"Pinterest's &quot;Shop by Brand&quot; category on the search results page for &quot;easter home decor&quot;\" src=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/hs-fs/hubfs/Google%20Drive%20Integration/6%20Creative%20Strategies%20for%20Getting%20Traffic%20from%20Pinterest-1.jpeg?width=624&amp;height=352&amp;name=6%20Creative%20Strategies%20for%20Getting%20Traffic%20from%20Pinterest-1.jpeg\" style=\"margin-left: 0.00px;\" title=\"\" width=\"624\" height=\"352\"></p> \n<p>This might inspire your team to create your own version of Easter home decor content, as well as other seasonal pins and boards.</p> \n<p>Finally, consider partnering with certain brands that have complementary products or services to your own. For example, Benefit Cosmetics partnered with Shutterfly to create the page, \"<a href=\"https://www.pinterest.com/benefitbeauty/wedding-looks-benefit-cosmetics-x-wedding-paper-di/\">Wedding Looks: benefit cosmetics x Wedding Paper Divas</a>\":</p> \n<p><img src=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/hs-fs/hubfs/pinterest%20partnership.png?width=2784&amp;name=pinterest%20partnership.png\" alt=\"A Pinterest page that showcases a partnership between benefit cosmetics and shutterfly for weddings\" width=\"2784\" style=\"width: 2784px;\"></p> \n<p>The page is filled with pins related to both makeup and stationary for the big day. For expanding your reach and increasing value for your followers, you might try partnering with other popular brands on Pinterest.&nbsp;</p> \n<p>Ultimately, <a href=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/blog/tabid/6307/bid/31147/the-ultimate-guide-to-mastering-pinterest-for-marketing.aspx\">creating a successful Pinterest strategy</a>&nbsp;takes work and dedication, but if you find Pinterest is a popular social platform with your target audience, it's likely worth the time and effort it takes to grow your following, increase brand awareness, and ultimately drive sales. &nbsp;</p> \n<p></p> \n<p><a class=\"cta_button\" href=\"https://www.hubspot.com/cs/ci/?pg=3f71599f-145c-46b7-8160-fa69a69eccf0&amp;pid=53&amp;ecid=&amp;hseid=&amp;hsic=\"><img -085_66e5f0d70d49ffdc.webp","https://no-cache.hubspot.com/cta/default/53/3f71599f-145c-46b7-8160-fa69a69eccf0.png":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx1/cdn79@2020_3/2021/04/23/17-35-49-228_7d79defad72ae096.webp","https://track.hubspot.com/__ptq.gif?a=53&k=14&r=https%3A%2F%2Fblog.hubspot.com%2Fmarketing%2Fget-traffic-pinterest&bu=https%253A%252F%252Fblog.hubspot.com%252Fmarketing&bvt=rss":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx32/cdn88@2020_3/2021/04/23/17-35-50-232_6a48aaa266df250c.webp"},"publishedOrCreatedDate":1619199338326},{"createdTime":"2021-04-24 Instructions]","link":"https://blog.hubspot.com/marketing/facebook-insights","description":"<p>If your brand has a <a href=\"https://www.hubspot.com/facebook-marketing?_ga=2.84760025.1754543653.1615579873-704973595.1615579873\">business Facebook page</a>, you'll want to invest time understanding your Insights dashboard.</p> \n<p>It holds important data that helps you understand how your page is performing and is key to growing your page.</p> \n<p><a class=\"cta_button\" href=\"https://www.hubspot.com/cs/ci/?pg=9f7c45b7-c71b-4797-8d5d-e6b296fb6a83&amp;pid=53&amp;ecid=&amp;hseid=&amp;hsic=\"><img class=\"hs-cta-img \" style=\"border-width: 0px; /*hs-extra-styles*/; \" alt=\"Free Resource: How to Reach &amp; Engage Your Audience on Facebook\" src=\"https://no-cache.hubspot.com/cta/default/53/9f7c45b7-c71b-4797-8d5d-e6b296fb6a83.png\" /></a></p> \n<p>Features like weekly insight summaries and competitive data on other business pages make Facebook Insights a powerful tool that every marketer should leverage.</p> \n<p>Let's dive into what Facebook Insights is, how to access it, and how to interpret the metrics it tracks.</p> \n<h3>Facebook Page Insights vs. Facebook Audience Insights</h3> \n<p>Despite having similar names, Facebook Insights and Facebook Audience Insights have completely different functions.</p> \n<p>Facebook Insights visualizes incoming data from your business page so you can learn how users are behaving on your page, what content they're engaging with, and how your page matches up to competitors.</p> \n<p>Facebook Audience Insights, on the other hand, is used for ad campaigns and helps marketers understand Facebook audiences in general (which can also include those who follow your page).</p> \n<p><img alt=\"Facebook Audience Insights dashboard\" src=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/hubfs/Google%20Drive%20Integration/Facebook%20Insights%20What%20It%20Is%20and%20How%20to%20Use%20IT-Mar-12-2021-08-12-14-94-PM.png\" style=\"margin-left: auto; margin-right: auto; display: block;\" title=\"\" /></p> \n<p>The platform includes information on user demographics, such as location and relationship status as well as user behavior, including average ad clicks and comments.</p> \n<h2>Where is Facebook Insights?</h2> \n<p>To access Facebook Insights, you'll need to have a business page. Then, follow the steps below:</p> \n<ol start=\"1\"> \n <li> <h3>Once you log into Facebook, head to your business page. Then, click on \"Insights,\" located on the sidebar to the left of the page.</h3> <h3 style=\"font-style: normal; font-variant-ligatures: normal; font-variant-caps: normal; font-family: AvenirNext, 'Helvetica Neue', Helvetica, Arial, sans-serif; color: #33475b;\"><img alt=\"Facebook Business Page Insights Tool\" src=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/hubfs/Google%20Drive%20Integration/Facebook%20Insights%20What%20It%20Is%20and%20How%20to%20Use%20IT.png\" title=\"\" style=\"margin-left: auto; margin-right: auto; display: block;\" /></h3> </li> \n <li> <h3>You'll land on the \"Overview\" page which features a dashboard with three main categories. The first is your page summary, which shows key metrics from the last seven days. However, you can also view data from today, yesterday, and the last 28 days. <img alt=\"Facebook Insights Page Summary dashboard\" src=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/hubfs/Google%20Drive%20Integration/Facebook%20Insights%20What%20It%20Is%20and%20How%20to%20Use%20IT-Mar-12-2021-08-12-15-23-PM.png\" style=\"margin-left: auto; margin-right: auto; display: block;\" title=\"\" /></h3> </li> \n <li> <h3>Once you scroll down, you'll see insights on your most recent posts.</h3> <img src=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/hs-fs/hubfs/facebook-insights-most-recent-posts.png?width=1196&amp;name=facebook-insights-most-recent-posts.png\" alt=\"Facebook Insights Most Recent Posts\" width=\"1196\" style=\"width: 1196px; margin-left: auto; margin-right: auto; display: block;\" /></li> \n <li> <h3>The last section features insights from your competitors. In this section, Facebook can recommend pages to watch, but you can also customize which brands' performance you track by clicking \"Add Pages.\"</h3> <img src=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/hs-fs/hubfs/facebook-insights-pages-to-watch.png?width=1196&amp;name=facebook-insights-pages-to-watch.png\" alt=\"facebook insights pages to watch\" width=\"1196\" style=\"width: 1196px; margin-left: auto; margin-right: auto; display: block;\" /></li> \n <li> <h3>To dive deeper into these metrics, you can click each category listed on the sidebar to the left of the dashboard. <img alt=\"\" src=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/hs-fs/hubfs/Google%20Drive%20Integration/Facebook%20Insights%20What%20It%20Is%20and%20How%20to%20Use%20IT-4.png?width=624&amp;name=Facebook%20Insights%20What%20It%20Is%20and%20How%20to%20Use%20IT-4.png\" style=\"margin-left: auto; margin-right: auto; display: block;\" title=\"\" width=\"624\" /></h3> </li> \n</ol> \n<h2>How to Use the Facebook Insights API</h2> \n<p>The Facebook Insights API, also known as the Ads Insights API, allows you to fetch ad data to track your ad performance. The API is particularly useful because it allows marketers to pull the exact data they want to track, no matter how granular.</p> \n<p>To fetch the data from the API, you must determine what data you want to pull and create an access token for that ad, so that only your team can access that information. You'll then need to determine where to import that data, like <a href=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/marketing/google-sheets-templates\">Google Sheets </a>or <a href=\"https://www.hubspot.com/products/marketing/ads\">HubSpot's ads software</a> within the Marketing Hub.</p> \n<p>It allows you to pull your Insights API into the platform and match it against with data already in the CRM. This will provide a better understanding of the customer journey and give you a 360-degree view of how your ads are performing.</p> \n<h2>How to Export Facebook Insights Data</h2> \n<ol start=\"1\"> \n <li> <h3>Start on your dashboard overview. On the top right corner of your \"Page Summary,\" you'll see \"Export Data.\" <img alt=\"Facebook insights page summary\" src=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/hs-fs/hubfs/Google%20Drive%20Integration/Facebook%20Insights%20What%20It%20Is%20and%20How%20to%20Use%20IT-3.png?width=624&amp;name=Facebook%20Insights%20What%20It%20Is%20and%20How%20to%20Use%20IT-3.png\" style=\"margin-left: auto; margin-right: auto; display: block;\" title=\"\" width=\"624\" /></h3> </li> \n <li> <h3>A window will pop up. From there, you'll narrow down what data to export, the data range, file format and layout. <img alt=\"facebook insights export data page\" src=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/hs-fs/hubfs/Google%20Drive%20Integration/Facebook%20Insights%20What%20It%20Is%20and%20How%20to%20Use%20IT-2.png?width=624&amp;name=Facebook%20Insights%20What%20It%20Is%20and%20How%20to%20Use%20IT-2.png\" style=\"margin-left: auto; margin-right: auto; display: block;\" title=\"\" width=\"624\" /></h3> </li> \n <li> <h3>Click \"Export Data\" and you're all set.</h3> </li> \n</ol> \n<h2>Top Facebook Insights Metrics</h2> \n<p>Your Facebook Insights dashboard displays top metrics about your business page. On any given day, you can get a snapshot of your page's performance and adjust your strategy accordingly. Top metrics include:</p> \n<ul> \n <li><strong>Page views</strong> – The number of times your page has been viewed by Facebook and non-Facebook users.</li> \n <li><strong>Page likes </strong>– How many Facebook users like your business page.</li> \n <li><strong>Actions on page</strong> – How many actions users take on your business page, such as to click on a website link or ask for directions to your store.</li> \n <li><strong>Post reach </strong>– The number of users on Facebook who saw your post.</li> \n <li><strong>Post engagement </strong>– How many people liked, shared, reacted, or commented on your post.</li> \n</ul> \n<p>You also have video insights, which can tell you how your videos are performing. Key metrics include:</p> \n<ul> \n <li><strong>Minutes viewed </strong>– The total amount of time users have spent watching your videos.</li> \n <li><strong>Video views </strong>– The number of users who watched your video for three seconds or more.</li> \n <li><strong>Audience retention </strong>– How long you maintained your video's audience in a video.</li> \n</ul> \n<p>For tips on how to interpret your video insights, jump to <a href=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/marketing/facebook-insights#facebook-insights\">this section</a>.</p> \n<h2>How to Interpret Facebook Insights</h2> \n<p>Before you start analyzing your data, make sure you know what questions you want answered. This will help you narrow down which key metrics to focus on.</p> \n<p>Once you know that, start looking through the data to identify patterns.</p> \n<p>For instance, let's say you notice that your how-to posts get shared at a much higher rate than your other content.This may indicate that this type of content resonates more with your audience and adds value to them and their community. As such, you may want to double down on these posts if your goal is to get higher engagement.</p> \n<p>Analyzing the data is one thing, but what's more important is what you do next. As you notice trends, take note of them and conduct experiments to learn more about what your audience wants. This will help you learn more about your audience and develop content that meets their needs.</p> \n<p>If your team wants to focus on video insights, scroll down to the \"Videos\" tab on the left sidebar and click on it. Once there, you'll see your top video metrics, such as watch time and top video performers.</p> \n<a></a> \n<p>For tips on how to understand your video insights, watch the video below. It dives into how to navigate your video insights dashboard and what your insights can tell you broken down by performance, loyalty, audience, and retention.</p> \n<div class=\"hs-responsive-embed-wrapper hs-responsive-embed\" style=\"width: 100%; height: auto; position: relative; overflow: hidden; padding: 0; max-width: 853px; max-height: 480px; min-width: 256px; margin: 0px auto; display: block;\"> \n <div class=\"hs-responsive-embed-inner-wrapper\" style=\"position: relative; overflow: hidden; max-width: 100%; padding-bottom: 56.27%; margin: 0;\"> \n  <iframe class=\"hs-responsive-embed-iframe\" style=\"position: absolute; top: 0; left: 0; width: 100%; height: 100%; border: none;\" src=\"https://www.youtube.com/embed/QRUZ9A282yA\" width=\"853\" height=\"480\" frameborder=\"0\" allowfullscreen=\"\"></iframe> \n </div> \n</div> \n<p>Your Facebook Insights dashboard holds so much information about your page's performance and your audience. If you leverage that data, you can create better content and generate more revenue for your brand.</p> \n<p><a class=\"cta_button\" bspot.com/hs-fs/hubfs/Google%20Drive%20Integration/Facebook%20Insights%20What%20It%20Is%20and%20How%20to%20Use%20IT-2.png?width=624&name=Facebook%20Insights%20What%20It%20Is%20and%20How%20to%20Use%20IT-2.png":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx33/cdn20@2020_4/2021/04/23/17-35-49-682_6a6be1f7bcf12c56.webp","https://no-cache.hubspot.com/cta/default/53/b1ed53ce-abab-413f-b67a-846d53ac1657.png":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx11/cdn95@2020_4/2021/04/23/17-35-48-856_43149526df2d3104.webp","https://track.hubspot.com/__ptq.gif?a=53&k=14&r=https%3A%2F%2Fblog.hubspot.com%2Fmarketing%2Ffacebook-insights&bu=https%253A%252F%252Fblog.hubspot.com%252Fmarketing&bvt=rss":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx18/cdn55@2020_6/2021/04/23/17-35-49-558_f11713633090363c.webp"},"publishedOrCreatedDate":1619199338326},{"createdTime":"2021-04-24 01:35:38","updatedTime":"2021-04-24 01:35:38","title":"How to Use Facebook: A Beginner’s Guide","link":"https://blog.hubspot.com/marketing/how-to-use-facebook","description":"<p>Facebook has changed quite a bit since I first signed up for an account in 2008. Back then, Facebook was still called “The Facebook”, and my bio literally said, “Check out my MySpace, it’s waaaay better than my Facebook.”</p> \n<p>Needless to say, Facebook has evolved at breakneck speed since my middle school years, and it’ll keep adapting at a swift pace for as long as it exists.</p> \n<p>If you need a refresher on how to use <a href=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/blog/tabid/6307/bid/24422/the-ultimate-facebook-marketing-cheat-sheet.aspx?_ga=2.129982540.1566459252.1616458538-1265945322.1616458538\">Facebook for marketing your business</a> or you want to sign up for a personal account, check out this in-depth explanation of how to use the <a href=\"https://www.statista.com/statistics/272014/global-social-networks-ranked-by-number-of-users/\">most popular social media network</a> in the world.</p> \n<a class=\"cta_button\" href=\"https://www.hubspot.com/cs/ci/?pg=71d5a909-34b0-4b5b-aef5-89968e4e8847&amp;pid=53&amp;ecid=&amp;hseid=&amp;hsic=\"><img class=\"hs-cta-img \" style=\"border-width: 0px; /*hs-extra-styles*/; margin: 0 auto; display: block; margin-top: 20px; margin-bottom: 20px\" alt=\"Free Resource: How to Reach &amp; Engage Your Audience on Facebook\" src=\"https://no-cache.hubspot.com/cta/default/53/71d5a909-34b0-4b5b-aef5-89968e4e8847.png\" align=\"middle\"></a> \n<p>In addition to sharing their own ideas, users can engage with the content other people share on Facebook by reacting to it with a like, a laugh, disapproval, and even a hug. Comments and shares are additional ways users can interact with each other’s content.</p> \n<p><img alt=\"\" src=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/hs-fs/hubfs/Google%20Drive%20Integration/How%20to%20Use%20Facebook%20A%20Beginner%E2%80%99s%20Guide-Mar-23-2021-12-16-54-02-AM.png?width=400&amp;name=How%20to%20Use%20Facebook%20A%20Beginner%E2%80%99s%20Guide-Mar-23-2021-12-16-54-02-AM.png\" title=\"\" width=\"400\" style=\"margin-left: auto; margin-right: auto; display: block; width: 400px;\"></p> \n<p>Facebook for businesses works similarly, except businesses have <a href=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/blog/tabid/6307/bid/5492/how-to-create-a-facebook-business-page-in-5-simple-steps-with-video.aspx#:~:text=On%20the%20left%2Dhand%20menu,Page%20in%20under%20255%20characters.\">Facebook Pages</a> not profiles like individual users do. Businesses can <a href=\"https://www.hubspot.com/facebook-marketing\">use their Facebook Pages</a> to engage with existing customers, target new customers, and administer customer support.</p> \n<p>To fully understand Facebook and how it works, you’ll want to become familiar with common terms used on the platform. Here is a list of key Facebook terms and what they mean.</p> \n<h3>Profile</h3> \n<p>The Facebook profile is where your information will live. Your name, photo, hometown, workplace, education history, and so on can all be added to your profile. You can make your profile as public or private as you want by disabling the information you don’t want publicly visible.</p> \n<p><img src=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/hs-fs/hubfs/Facebook-01-jpg.jpeg?width=650&amp;name=Facebook-01-jpg.jpeg\" width=\"650\" style=\"width: 650px; margin-left: auto; margin-right: auto; display: block;\" alt=\"Facebook profile example for a beginner\"></p> \n<h3>Newsfeed</h3> \n<p>This is the place where all of your friends’ posts will appear. You’ll also see updates from business pages that you’ve liked. Your posts will also appear in the newsfeed where your friends can see them.</p> \n<h3>Timeline</h3> \n<p>Often confused with a newsfeed, the timeline is your personal record of all the posts you’ve shared and posts you’ve interacted with. While you won’t usually see friend’s status updates here, there is one exception — if they’ve tagged you in a post or a photo, it’ll appear on your timeline. Your friends can see your timeline by default if they search your name unless you’ve set your privacy settings to do the contrary.</p> \n<h3>Algorithm</h3> \n<p>The algorithm is an elusive concept. Essentially, the algorithm is a series of computations that Facebook’s servers do every second to determine what content you want to see, interact with, and click on next. The algorithm uses dwell time (how long you view a post), engagement, page likes, posts, and more to determine the type of content you might like to see. Over time, the algorithm gets better at determining what content to show you.</p> \n<h3>Status/Post</h3> \n<p>The two terms are often used interchangeably, but “post” is the term Facebook uses to describe something you share on the newsfeed. Text, images, videos, and location are just a few of the types of posts you can share to the newsfeed for your friends to see.</p> \n<p><img alt=\"How to write a status or post for a facebook beginner\" src=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/hs-fs/hubfs/Google%20Drive%20Integration/How%20to%20Use%20Facebook%20A%20Beginner%E2%80%99s%20Guide-2.png?width=300&amp;name=How%20to%20Use%20Facebook%20A%20Beginner%E2%80%99s%20Guide-2.png\" title=\"\" width=\"300\" style=\"width: 300px; margin-left: auto; margin-right: auto; display: block;\"></p> \n<h3>Friends</h3> \n<p>These are people you’ve either sent a request to and they’ve accepted or people who have sent you a request and you’ve accepted. Unlike other social networking sites that allow someone to follow you without you following them back, Facebook’s friend system requires both you and the other person to be friends with each other. A personal account for an individual cannot have more than 5,000 friends (and it’s not a good idea to make a <a href=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/blog/tabid/6307/bid/9134/top-5-things-not-to-do-on-facebook.aspx\">second Facebook profile</a> to get around this rule).<img src=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/hs-fs/hubfs/Facebook-03-png.png?width=650&amp;name=Facebook-03-png.png\" width=\"650\" style=\"width: 650px; margin-left: auto; margin-right: auto; display: block;\" alt=\"How to view Facebook friends for beginners\"></p> \n<h3>Followers</h3> \n<p>Facebook has a follower option as well. When you add new friends, you automatically follow them (and they follow you, too). This is Facebook’s way of adding this new friend to your newsfeed and making sure you see their posts (at least for a little while unless you stop engaging with them). For individuals who exceed 5,000 friends on their personal Facebook profiles, people can opt to follow them instead to stay up to date on their posts. Keep in mind, while Facebook automatically follows your friends for you, you can manually unfollow them without unfriending them. This action removes these individuals’ posts from your newsfeed. If you do this, you’ll need to search your friends individually and surge their timelines to catch up on their latest posts.</p> \n<p><img alt=\"How to follow and unfollow a friend on Facebook\" src=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/hs-fs/hubfs/Google%20Drive%20Integration/How%20to%20Use%20Facebook%20A%20Beginner%E2%80%99s%20Guide-Mar-23-2021-12-16-52-78-AM.png?width=400&amp;name=How%20to%20Use%20Facebook%20A%20Beginner%E2%80%99s%20Guide-Mar-23-2021-12-16-52-78-AM.png\" title=\"\" width=\"400\" style=\"margin-left: auto; margin-right: auto; display: block; width: 400px;\"></p> \n<h3>Groups</h3> \n<p>Facebook users with similar interests might find it helpful to create a group on the platform. A group is a community of users who interact with each other based on various topics set by the group’s admins and other users. Only individual users can be added to groups — pages cannot be part of Facebook groups. Admins have a wide range of permissions they can enable or disable to have the group function in a particular way.</p> \n<p><img src=\"https://lh6.googleusercontent.com/E6g70izSajTgsnQWPFou1_bhObljb9ju2_fqEK5SFUzF1WsD1Dcjkuk7W1_7YavjnWjVxiTBvckVMY60iRhV_ngfm1Ki8pMYoN1IQvUgqbkds8JvRUCTlGrK7WLjuXOyxqPBlbB6\" width=\"400\" style=\"margin-left: auto; margin-right: auto; display: block; width: 400px;\" alt=\"Example of a Facebook private group called the millennial check in\"></p> \n<h3>Pages</h3> \n<p>Businesses use Facebook Pages to create a presence on the social network. Pages are not individual Facebook users — think of them as profiles for businesses. They can post updates, images, videos, and all the other types of content that profiles can. However, they have an advantage — Facebook Pages have the ability to connect to <a href=\"https://www.facebook.com/business\">Facebook for Business</a> and <a href=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/marketing/facebook-paid-ad-checklist\">run ad campaigns</a>.</p> \n<p><img alt=\"Example of a Facebook page featuring GoFundme\" src=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/hs-fs/hubfs/Google%20Drive%20Integration/How%20to%20Use%20Facebook%20A%20Beginner%E2%80%99s%20Guide-Mar-23-2021-12-16-55-16-AM.png?width=650&amp;name=How%20to%20Use%20Facebook%20A%20Beginner%E2%80%99s%20Guide-Mar-23-2021-12-16-55-16-AM.png\" title=\"\" width=\"650\" style=\"margin-left: auto; margin-right: auto; display: block; width: 650px;\"></p> \n<h3>Events</h3> \n<p>With so much community happening on Facebook, individual users and businesses have the option to advertise events. The events can accept RSVPs, create a guest list, and share the date time, and location of the event. Events can be virtual through a video platform or they can be in person with a physical location.</p> \n<p><img alt=\"Example of a Facebook event featuring a few dozen people in small boats at the 4th annual mega tube float\" src=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/hs-fs/hubfs/Google%20Drive%20Integration/How%20to%20Use%20Facebook%20A%20Beginner%E2%80%99s%20Guide-Mar-23-2021-12-16-56-80-AM.png?width=300&amp;name=How%20to%20Use%20Facebook%20A%20Beginner%E2%80%99s%20Guide-Mar-23-2021-12-16-56-80-AM.png\" title=\"\" width=\"300\" style=\"margin-left: auto; margin-right: auto; display: block; width: 300px;\"></p> \n<h3>Messenger</h3> \n<p>Instead of a direct messaging platform in the native Facebook app, Facebook Messenger exists as a separate application so users can chat one-on-one or in a private group setting. When using Facebook.com on a desktop computer, the messenger is accessible through the native Facebook website.</p> \n<p><img src=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/hs-fs/hubfs/Screen%20Shot%202021-03-22%20at%207-33-46%20PM-png.png?width=300&amp;name=Screen%20Shot%202021-03-22%20at%207-33-46%20PM-png.png\" style=\"margin-left: auto; margin-right: auto; display: block; width: 300px;\" width=\"300\" alt=\"Facebook messenger button for beginners\"></p> \n<h3>Story</h3> \n<p>Like Instagram stories, Facebook stories are another way individual users and business pages can connect with their friends and followers. Stories are short pieces of content that are visible for just 24 hours. After 24 hours, the stories disappear from the newsfeed.</p> \n<p><img alt=\"Facebook stories for beginners\" src=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/hs-fs/hubfs/Google%20Drive%20Integration/How%20to%20Use%20Facebook%20A%20Beginner%E2%80%99s%20Guide-Mar-23-2021-12-16-53-52-AM.png?width=400&amp;name=How%20to%20Use%20Facebook%20A%20Beginner%E2%80%99s%20Guide-Mar-23-2021-12-16-53-52-AM.png\" title=\"\" width=\"400\" style=\"margin-left: auto; margin-right: auto; display: block; width: 400px;\"></p> \n<h3>Notification</h3> \n<p>Represented by the bell icon in the third circle below, a notification informs you when a friend engages with your posts, photos, videos, or timeline, you’ll receive a notification that explains what they engaged with and when. Friend requests will also appear here.<img src=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/hs-fs/hubfs/Facebook-04-png.png?width=300&amp;name=Facebook-04-png.png\" width=\"300\" style=\"width: 300px; margin-left: auto; margin-right: auto; display: block;\" alt=\"Facebook notifications for beginners\"></p> \n<p>Now that you have an idea of what Facebook is and how it works, here’s a handy guide to using Facebook.</p> \n<h3>How does Facebook Work?</h3> \n<p>Facebook is powered by an algorithm that is able to learn each user's preferences and interests. Then, the algorithm displays content like images, status updates, and videos posted by friends and businesses that the user might be interested in. The goal for Facebook is to get users to engage with, consume, and share content.</p> \n<p>Along with this, Facebook runs advertisements for businesses and these ads are sprinkled in between organic content shared by your friends on the news feed. The ads are tailored to your interests so you see what the algorithm thinks you might be interested in based on content you’ve interacted with in the past. This is called <a href=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/marketing/behavioral-targeting\">behavioral targeting</a>.</p> \n<h3>How the Facebook Algorithm Works</h3> \n<p>In the past, Facebook used a chronological timeline. This means that the posts on your newsfeed were listed in the order in which they were most recently shared by your friends on the platform. If your mom posted three hours ago and your best friend posted five minutes ago, you’d see your best friend’s post first, then your mom’s. However, that all changed in September 2011 when <a href=\"https://mashable.com/2013/03/12/facebook-news-feed-evolution/\">Facebook officially announced</a> that it was doing away with the chronological newsfeed and replacing it with a more personalized experience. Rather than seeing your friends’ posts in the order they were shared, you now see the content Facebook’s algorithm thinks you’ll enjoy the most. This newsfeed is still around today.</p> \n<p></p> \n<h3>1. Sign up for a Facebook account.</h3> \n<p>To sign up for a Facebook account, follow these three easy steps.</p> \n<ul> \n <li>Visit <a href=\"https://www.facebook.com/\">Facebook’s website</a>.</li> \n <li>On the homepage, enter your <strong>first name</strong>, <strong>last name</strong>, <strong>mobile number or email</strong>, <strong>new password</strong>, <strong>birthday</strong>, and <strong>gender</strong>.</li> \n <li>Click <strong>Sign Up</strong>.</li> \n</ul> \n<p><img alt=\"Facebook sign up screen that shows new users how to sign up for Facebook\" src=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/hs-fs/hubfs/Google%20Drive%20Integration/How%20to%20Use%20Facebook%20A%20Beginner%E2%80%99s%20Guide-Mar-23-2021-12-16-53-18-AM.png?width=400&amp;name=How%20to%20Use%20Facebook%20A%20Beginner%E2%80%99s%20Guide-Mar-23-2021-12-16-53-18-AM.png\" title=\"\" width=\"400\" style=\"margin-left: auto; margin-right: auto; display: block; width: 400px;\"></p> \n<h3>2. Set up your privacy settings.</h3> \n<p>After you’ve signed up for a Facebook account, you can adjust your privacy settings to control who can see your profile and information. Follow these four simple steps to change your privacy settings.</p> \n<ul> \n <li>Click on the downward pointing <strong>arrow</strong> that’s located on the top right corner of any Facebook page.</li> \n <li>Click <strong>Settings</strong>.</li> \n <li>In the left sidebar, select <strong>Privacy</strong>.</li> \n <li>Set who is allowed to see your past and future posts. You can also control how people can find and contact you.</li> \n</ul> \n<p><img src=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/hs-fs/hubfs/Facebook-06-png.png?width=300&amp;name=Facebook-06-png.png\" width=\"300\" style=\"width: 300px; margin-left: auto; margin-right: auto; display: block;\" alt=\"How to change Facebook privacy settings for new users\"></p> \n<p>Odds are, there’s probably someone on Facebook who has the same name as you. To differentiate yourself from these people and help your friends and family find you on Facebook, personalize your profile by adding a profile picture, cover photo, and some personal information.</p> \n<h3>3. Personalize your profile.</h3> \n<h4>Picking a Profile Picture</h4> \n<ul> \n <li>Go to your <strong>profile</strong> and click on your <strong>profile picture</strong>.</li> \n <li>To pick your profile picture, choose a photo that you’re already tagged in on Facebook, one that you’ve uploaded to Facebook, or a photo from your computer. You can also add a frame to your profile picture.</li> \n</ul> \n<p><img alt=\"How to update your profile picture on Facebook\" src=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/hs-fs/hubfs/Google%20Drive%20Integration/How%20to%20Use%20Facebook%20A%20Beginner%E2%80%99s%20Guide-Mar-23-2021-12-16-54-42-AM.png?width=650&amp;name=How%20to%20Use%20Facebook%20A%20Beginner%E2%80%99s%20Guide-Mar-23-2021-12-16-54-42-AM.png\" title=\"\" width=\"650\" style=\"margin-left: auto; margin-right: auto; display: block; width: 650px;\"></p> \n<h4>Choosing a Cover Photo</h4> \n<ul> \n <li>Click the <strong>camera</strong> button on your cover photo, which is on your profile.</li> \n <li>To choose your cover photo, you can pick a photo from your Facebook profile, a selection of Facebook’s own cover artwork, create a collage, or upload a photo from your computer. You can also reposition or delete your current cover photo.</li> \n</ul> \n<p><img alt=\"How to choose and change a cover photo for Facebook beginners\" src=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/hs-fs/hubfs/Google%20Drive%20Integration/How%20to%20Use%20Facebook%20A%20Beginner%E2%80%99s%20Guide-Mar-23-2021-12-16-53-83-AM.png?width=300&amp;name=How%20to%20Use%20Facebook%20A%20Beginner%E2%80%99s%20Guide-Mar-23-2021-12-16-53-83-AM.png\" title=\"\" width=\"300\" style=\"margin-left: auto; margin-right: auto; display: block; width: 300px;\"></p> \n<h4>Updating Your Profile</h4> \n<ul> \n <li>Click the <strong>About</strong> section on your profile page.</li> \n <li>In this section, you can fill in information about your work and education, the places you’ve lived, contact and basic info, family and relationships, details about you, and life events.<img alt=\"How to update your profile and about sections on Facebook\" src=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/hs-fs/hubfs/Google%20Drive%20Integration/How%20to%20Use%20Facebook%20A%20Beginner%E2%80%99s%20Guide-Mar-23-2021-12-16-56-44-AM.png?width=300&amp;name=How%20to%20Use%20Facebook%20A%20Beginner%E2%80%99s%20Guide-Mar-23-2021-12-16-56-44-AM.png\" title=\"\" width=\"300\" style=\"margin-left: auto; margin-right: auto; display: block; width: 300px;\"></li> \n</ul> \n<h3>4. Like and follow public pages.</h3> \n<p>On Facebook, you can follow and get updates from your favorite brands, celebrities, sports teams, and publications. The best way to do this is by searching for them on Facebook and liking or following their public page, which will have a blue verified check mark next to their name. After you like or follow their page, you’ll start to see their updates in your news feed.</p> \n<p><img src=\"https://lh6.googleusercontent.com/g433lxxFIkqR1c98eqMjxH6lw3LmcRHdH5k2-CId5d7gjkTrOgYosNqNRN4VRdFOmiw5NsN34qWz--ByFk9C78BVKy8-voQPOBXk76lcchwGmf-AN12Lu_15hOcFkN2LKeL1SiT-\" width=\"400\" style=\"margin-left: auto; margin-right: auto; display: block; width: 400px;\" alt=\"How to find like and follow public pages like HubSpot on Facebook\"></p> \n<h3>5. Review your timeline.</h3> \n<p>Your timeline is a digital log of your Facebook activity in reverse-chronological order. Your status updates, uploaded photos and videos, and the photos you’re tagged in will appear on your timeline.</p> \n<p><img src=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/hs-fs/hubfs/Facebook-07-jpg.jpeg?width=650&amp;name=Facebook-07-jpg.jpeg\" style=\"margin-left: auto; margin-right: auto; display: block; width: 650px;\" width=\"650\" alt=\"How to find and view your Facebook timeline\"></p> \n<h3>6. Add friends on Facebook.</h3> \n<p>There are three ways you can add friends on Facebook. You can either search for them, find them in the Find Friends tab, or import a list of contacts from your email, iCloud, or phone.</p> \n<p>To find friends on Facebook, go to your profile, select the <strong>Friends tab</strong>, and tap the Find Friends button. You’ll see a list of friend requests from other people and a list of people you may know that you can add as a friend on Facebook.</p> \n<p>If you upload a list of contacts onto Facebook, you can add your friends as you sort through each of your contacts.</p> \n<p><img src=\"https://lh3.googleusercontent.com/vKkb5sbpRUY9Bndx9nPcxf0SulRAdrCl1F2kWyWJ9w08LYk30JVS4Ru9CJpp_l4EXWrF-O5AFAgsFyM9Cfj7VAcAI_TJtAK91YRLhT2WID-ZsTjlhmxFF45TZSqxWpwq5HO_L6aR\" width=\"650\" style=\"margin-left: auto; margin-right: auto; display: block; width: 650px;\" alt=\"How to add friends on Facebook for beginners\"></p> \n<h3>7. Post on Facebook.</h3> \n<p>The main purpose of Facebook is to help friends and family connect with each other. And the best way to connect with your friends and family is by updating them about your life with status updates. To share a Facebook status, go to the text box at the top of your news feed page or on your profile page.</p> \n<p>With status updates, you can share text with 15 different colored backgrounds, photos, videos, GIFs, stickers, and links.</p> \n<p>You can also share other types of posts, like:</p> \n<ul> \n <li><strong>Feeling/Activity:</strong> Share how you’re currently feeling or what you’re currently doing.</li> \n <li><strong>Check In:</strong> When you visit a city, location, or place, check in and let your friends know where you’re at.</li> \n <li><strong>Tag Friends:</strong> If you’re hanging out with your friends, tag them in your status and share what you’re doing.</li> \n <li><strong>Tag Event:</strong> If you’re at an event, you can tag it in your status and share what event you’re attending.</li> \n <li><strong>Ask for Recommendations:</strong> If you just moved somewhere or you’re about to visit a location, you can ask your Facebook friends for recommendations on where to go.</li> \n <li><strong>Poll:</strong> Ask your Facebook friends what their opinion is on a certain topic.</li> \n <li><strong>Support Nonprofit:</strong> Choose a nonprofit organization of your choice and share it through your status. Your Facebook Friends can then select the <strong>donate button</strong> to support the chosen organization.</li> \n <li><strong>Answer a Question:</strong> Choose a predetermined question to answer or create your own question to answer and share it with your Facebook friends.</li> \n <li><strong>Lists:</strong> Choose a predetermined topic to make a list for or create your own topic and share it with your Facebook friends.</li> \n <li><strong>Facebook Stories:</strong> All the content that you can share through a status update is shareable through your Facebook story. You can also upload content to your stories by clicking the Add to Your Story button on the right sidebar. Additionally, you can watch all your friends’ Facebook Stories by clicking on their picture in the Stories section, which is also located on the right sidebar on your home page.</li> \n</ul> \n<h3>8. Add photos and videos.</h3> \n<p>On Facebook, you can add photos, videos, albums, and live video broadcasts to your profile for all your friends to see.</p> \n<h4>Uploading photos or videos</h4> \n<p>To upload photos or videos to your profile, follow these four simple steps:</p> \n<ul> \n <li>Go to your <strong>Profile</strong>.</li> \n <li style=\"background-color: #ffff64;\">Select the <strong>Photos</strong> tab.</li> \n <li style=\"background-color: #ffff64;\">Select <strong>Add Photos/Video</strong>.</li> \n</ul> Upload pictures or videos from your computer.\n<img alt=\"How to upload new photos and videos to Facebook\" src=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/hs-fs/hubfs/Google%20Drive%20Integration/How%20to%20Use%20Facebook%20A%20Beginner%E2%80%99s%20Guide-Mar-23-2021-12-16-55-01-AM.png?width=650&amp;name=How%20to%20Use%20Facebook%20A%20Beginner%E2%80%99s%20Guide-Mar-23-2021-12-16-55-01-AM.png\" title=\"\" width=\"650\" style=\"width: 650px; margin-left: auto; margin-right: auto; display: block;\"> \n<h4>Creating photo or video albums</h4> \n<p>To create a photo or video album, follow these four simple steps:</p> \n<ul> \n <li>Go to your <strong>Profile</strong>.</li> \n <li>Tap the <strong>Photos</strong> tab.</li> \n <li>Tap <strong>Create Album</strong>.</li> \n</ul> Upload pictures or videos from your computer.\n<img src=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/hs-fs/hubfs/Facebook-08-png.png?width=500&amp;name=Facebook-08-png.png\" style=\"margin-left: auto; margin-right: auto; display: block; width: 500px;\" width=\"500\" alt=\"How to create a new photo or video album in Facebook\"> \n<h4>Facebook Live</h4> \n<p>To do a <a href=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/marketing/facebook-live-guide\">live broadcast on your Facebook account</a>, follow these three simple steps.</p> \n<ul> \n <li>In the box that says <strong>What’s on your mind?</strong>, select <strong>Live Video</strong>.</li> \n <li>Once you select <strong>Live Video</strong>, you can write a description about your broadcast, tag people in it, add a feeling or activity, check in to an event, support a non-profit, or add a poll. You can also title your live broadcast or tag a video game if you’re live streaming someone or yourself playing a video game.</li> \n <li style=\"background-color: #ffff64;\">Select <strong>Go Live</strong> when you’ve finished describing your live broadcast.</li> \n</ul> \n<p><img src=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/hs-fs/hubfs/Facebook-09-jpg.jpeg?width=650&amp;name=Facebook-09-jpg.jpeg\" style=\"margin-left: auto; margin-right: auto; display: block; width: 650px;\" width=\"650\" alt=\"How to go live on Facebook for beginners\"></p> \n<h3>9. Connect with friends.</h3> \n<p>On your news feed, you’ll see updates from your friends, family, or public pages you follow. To interact with them, you can like and react to their posts, share content on their timelines, and communicate with them through text or video chat.</p> \n<h4>Like, Comment, Or Share</h4> \n<p>If you like someone's post, give them a thumbs up, comment on their post, or share it.</p> \n<p><img src=\"https://lh4.googleusercontent.com/pT7_isjuQ4qwxXJGHBiAiBqKjHGtlD-lWlKtQIrknqAuyWKCMHp_DYCpB-7zjDelpMG49fhHpEzq0ioJjvgccTj5I2g6EfnNSiWTqCLjWLNw0mPPqHxR3NlOw5K4F-JHa0HMpp7D\" width=\"650\" style=\"margin-left: auto; margin-right: auto; display: block; width: 650px;\"></p> \n<h4>Other Reactions</h4> \n<p>If your Facebook friend’s post evokes a stronger reaction in you than a like, you can also express that you love, laughed, are amazed, sad, or angry at their post by holding down the Like button.</p> \n<p><img alt=\"Facebook emoji reactions\" src=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/hs-fs/hubfs/Google%20Drive%20Integration/How%20to%20Use%20Facebook%20A%20Beginner%E2%80%99s%20Guide-Mar-23-2021-12-16-53-38-AM.png?width=400&amp;name=How%20to%20Use%20Facebook%20A%20Beginner%E2%80%99s%20Guide-Mar-23-2021-12-16-53-38-AM.png\" title=\"\" width=\"400\" style=\"margin-left: auto; margin-right: auto; display: block; width: 400px;\"></p> \n<h4>Sharing Content on Your Friends’ Timelines</h4> \n<p>Anything you can post on your status, you can also post on your friend’s timeline.</p> \n<h4>Facebook Messenger</h4> \n<p>To chat with your friends or public pages on Facebook, use Facebook Messenger. You can access it by tapping the Messages button at the top right corner of any Facebook page or selecting the Messages button on the left sidebar of the home page.</p> \n<p><img src=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/hs-fs/hubfs/Facebook-10-10-png.png?width=300&amp;name=Facebook-10-10-png.png\" style=\"margin-left: auto; margin-right: auto; display: block; width: 300px;\" width=\"300\" alt=\"How to use Facebook messenger \"></p> \n<p>Next, select New Message and type in your friend or brand’s name that you want to connect with. Facebook Messenger also lets you create group chats by clicking on New Group. After that, all you have to do is name your group and add the friends you want to include in the group.</p> \n<p><img alt=\"How to send a new message in Facebook messenger\" src=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/hs-fs/hubfs/Google%20Drive%20Integration/How%20to%20Use%20Facebook%20A%20Beginner%E2%80%99s%20Guide.png?width=300&amp;name=How%20to%20Use%20Facebook%20A%20Beginner%E2%80%99s%20Guide.png\" title=\"\" width=\"300\" style=\"margin-left: auto; margin-right: auto; display: block; width: 300px;\"></p> \n<p>When you message your friends or group on Facebook Messenger, you can upload pictures, videos, and files from your computer, as well as stickers, GIFs, emojis, and take pictures and videos from your computer’s or phone’s camera.</p> \n<p>You can also view Messenger on its own page, where you can search for past conversations and manage your settings. To view Messenger on its own page tap the Messages button in the top right corner of any Facebook page and then tap the See All in Messenger button.</p> \n<p><img alt=\"How to find Facebook messenger\" src=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/hs-fs/hubfs/Google%20Drive%20Integration/How%20to%20Use%20Facebook%20A%20Beginner%E2%80%99s%20Guide-Mar-23-2021-12-16-52-42-AM.png?width=400&amp;name=How%20to%20Use%20Facebook%20A%20Beginner%E2%80%99s%20Guide-Mar-23-2021-12-16-52-42-AM.png\" title=\"\" width=\"400\" style=\"margin-left: auto; margin-right: auto; display: block; width: 400px;\"></p> \n<p>To instant message your friends' who are logged onto Facebook at the same time as you, tap the Chat button on the bottom of any Facebook page and strike up a conversation with your friends who are online.<img src=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/hs-fs/hubfs/Facebook-11-png.png?width=300&amp;name=Facebook-11-png.png\" style=\"margin-left: auto; margin-right: auto; display: block; width: 300px;\" width=\"300\" alt=\"How to view messenger conversations on the main Facebook screen\"></p> \n<h4>Phone and Video Calling</h4> \n<p>When you have Messenger open on its own page, you can search for any of your friends or groups, click on their name, and tap the phone or video chat button to call them.</p> \n<p><img alt=\"How to chat through Facebook messenger\" src=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/hs-fs/hubfs/Google%20Drive%20Integration/How%20to%20Use%20Facebook%20A%20Beginner%E2%80%99s%20Guide-Mar-23-2021-12-16-52-22-AM.png?width=300&amp;name=How%20to%20Use%20Facebook%20A%20Beginner%E2%80%99s%20Guide-Mar-23-2021-12-16-52-22-AM.png\" title=\"\" width=\"300\" style=\"margin-left: auto; margin-right: auto; display: block; width: 300px;\"></p> \n<h3>10. Review your newsfeed.</h3> \n<p>Your news feed is a curated feed of posts from your friends, family, and public pages you follow that <a href=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/marketing/facebook-organic-reach-declining\">Facebook’s algorithm</a> thinks you’ll be interested in. You’ll also see ads from brands who think you’ll enjoy consuming their content or products.</p> \n<p>To customize your news feed, tap the downward pointing <strong>arrow</strong> in the upper right corner of any Facebook page and tap <strong>News Feed Preference</strong>.</p> \n<p>From there, you can prioritize whose posts you’ll see first, unfollow people and groups to hide their posts, reconnect with people and groups you unfollowed, discover public pages that match your interests, and hide apps from your news feed.</p> \n<h3>11. Discover additional Facebook features.</h3> \n<p>Facebook isn’t just a platform for viral content and connection. It’s also a hub for community communications, video streaming, marketplaces, and games.</p> \n<h4>Events</h4> \n<p>The Events page on Facebook will show you any upcoming events that are popular with your Facebook friends or have been set up by the groups you belong to. You can also find events based on their date, location, and category.</p> \n<p>To find the Events page, select the <strong>Home</strong> button. Then, on the left sidebar, you’ll see the Explore section, where you can select <strong>Events</strong></p> \n<p><img src=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/hs-fs/hubfs/Facebook-13-jpg.jpeg?width=300&amp;name=Facebook-13-jpg.jpeg\" width=\"300\" style=\"width: 300px; margin-left: auto; margin-right: auto; display: block;\" alt=\"Facebook event in Bartlett, TN for an outdoor spring crafts fair\"></p> \n<h4>Groups</h4> \n<p>The Groups page on Facebook will show you which groups you manage and belong to. You can also discover groups to join based on Facebook’s suggestions and a ton of other categories.</p> \n<p>To access the Groups page, tap the Home button and then on the left sidebar, you’ll see the Explore section, where you can click Groups.</p> \n<p><img src=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/hs-fs/hubfs/Screen%20Shot%202021-03-17%20at%2012-35-20%20AM-14-png.png?width=300&amp;name=Screen%20Shot%202021-03-17%20at%2012-35-20%20AM-14-png.png\" width=\"300\" style=\"width: 300px; margin-left: auto; margin-right: auto; display: block;\" alt=\"How to find and see a group on Facebook\"></p> \n<h4>Facebook Watch</h4> \n<p>On the Facebook Watch platform, you can watch videos from the shows you’re following and search for other shows and videos.</p> \n<p>To access Facebook Watch, select the Home button. Then, on the left sidebar, you’ll see the Watch button right under the Marketplace button.</p> \n<p><img alt=\"How to view groups in one page on Facebook\" src=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/hs-fs/hubfs/Google%20Drive%20Integration/How%20to%20Use%20Facebook%20A%20Beginner%E2%80%99s%20Guide-Mar-23-2021-12-16-54-57-AM.png?width=650&amp;name=How%20to%20Use%20Facebook%20A%20Beginner%E2%80%99s%20Guide-Mar-23-2021-12-16-54-57-AM.png\" title=\"\" width=\"650\" style=\"width: 650px; margin-left: auto; margin-right: auto; display: block;\"></p> \n<h4>Marketplace</h4> \n<p>Not only does Facebook compete with Netflix in the streaming industry, but they also compete with eBay in the marketplace industry. With Facebook Marketplace, you can browse for all kinds of products, join groups to buy and sell products with people in your area or who share similar interests, shop for products sold from different shops, shop by category, and sell your own products.</p> \n<p>To access Facebook Marketplace, select the <strong>Home</strong> button. Then on the left sidebar, you’ll see the <strong>Marketplace</strong> button right under the <strong>Watch</strong> button.</p> \n<p><img alt=\"Facebook marketplace for beginners featuring a table, a house, and a studio apartment for sale\" src=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/hs-fs/hubfs/Google%20Drive%20Integration/How%20to%20Use%20Facebook%20A%20Beginner%E2%80%99s%20Guide-Mar-23-2021-12-16-52-95-AM.png?width=650&amp;name=How%20to%20Use%20Facebook%20A%20Beginner%E2%80%99s%20Guide-Mar-23-2021-12-16-52-95-AM.png\" title=\"\" width=\"650\" style=\"margin-left: auto; margin-right: auto; display: block; width: 650px;\"></p> \n<h4>Games</h4> \n<p>Facebook Games is one of Facebook’s best features. They host a huge collection of massively popular games, and you can browse the most popular games on the platform by top charts and categories. You can even play most of the games with your friends, too.</p> \n<p><img alt=\"Facebook games for beginners\" src=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/hs-fs/hubfs/Google%20Drive%20Integration/How%20to%20Use%20Facebook%20A%20Beginner%E2%80%99s%20Guide-3.png?width=650&amp;name=How%20to%20Use%20Facebook%20A%20Beginner%E2%80%99s%20Guide-3.png\"
