tps://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx5oss/cdn60@2020_5/2021/04/23/17-35-48-465_feabeda4133c956a.webp","https://no-cache.hubspot.com/cta/default/53/b1ed53ce-abab-413f-b67a-846d53ac1657.png":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx11/cdn95@2020_4/2021/04/23/17-35-48-856_43149526df2d3104.webp","https://track.hubspot.com/__ptq.gif?a=53&k=14&r=https%3A%2F%2Fblog.hubspot.com%2Fmarketing%2Fhow-to-use-facebook&bu=https%253A%252F%252Fblog.hubspot.com%252Fmarketing&bvt=rss":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx4/cdn16@2020_5/2021/04/23/17-35-48-836_159c4ea272170243.webp"},"publishedOrCreatedDate":1619199338326},{"createdTime":"2021-04-24 01:35:38","updatedTime":"2021-04-24 01:35:38","title":"How to Create a Pie Chart in Excel in 60 Seconds or Less","link":"https://blog.hubspot.com/marketing/make-pie-chart-excel","description":"<p>At the beginning of 2021, I was tasked with an assignment: Create a pie chart showcasing which types of content performed best on the Marketing Blog in 2020.</p> \n<p>The question was an undeniably important one, as it would influence what types of content we wrote in 2021, along with identifying new opportunities for growth.</p> \n<p>But once I'd compiled all relevant data, I was stuck — How could I easily create a pie chart to showcase my results?</p> \n<p>Fortunately, I've since figured it out. Here, let's dive into how you can create your own excel pie chart for impressive marketing reports and presentations. Plus, how to rotate a pie chart in excel, explode a pie chart, and even how to create a 3-dimensional version.</p> \n<p>Let's dive in.</p> \n<p><a class=\"cta_button\" href=\"https://www.hubspot.com/cs/ci/?pg=9ff7a4fe-5293-496c-acca-566bc6e73f42&amp;pid=53&amp;ecid=&amp;hseid=&amp;hsic=\"><img class=\"hs-cta-img \" style=\"border-width: 0px; /*hs-extra-styles*/; margin: 0 auto; display: block; margin-top: 20px; margin-bottom: 20px\" alt=\"Download 9 Excel Templates for Marketers [Free Kit]\" src=\"https://no-cache.hubspot.com/cta/default/53/9ff7a4fe-5293-496c-acca-566bc6e73f42.png\" align=\"middle\"></a></p> \n<h2 style=\"font-weight: normal;\">How to Make a Pie Chart in Excel</h2> \n<p><strong>1. Create your columns and/or rows of data. Feel free to label each column of data — excel will use those labels as titles for your pie chart. Then, highlight the data you want to display in pie chart form.</strong></p> \n<p><img alt=\"Highlighted columns of data in excel to create a pie chart.\" src=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/hubfs/Google%20Drive%20Integration/How%20to%20Create%20a%20Pie%20Chart%20in%20Excel%20in%2060%20Seconds%20or%20Less-1.png\" style=\"margin-left: auto; margin-right: auto; display: block;\" title=\"\"></p> \n<p><strong>2. Now, click \"Insert\" and then click on the \"Pie\" logo at the top of excel. </strong></p> \n<p><img alt=\"The pie chart tool in excel. \" src=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/hs-fs/hubfs/Google%20Drive%20Integration/How%20to%20Create%20a%20Pie%20Chart%20in%20Excel%20in%2060%20Seconds%20or%20Less-3.jpeg?width=624&amp;name=How%20to%20Create%20a%20Pie%20Chart%20in%20Excel%20in%2060%20Seconds%20or%20Less-3.jpeg\" style=\"margin-left: 0.00px;\" title=\"\" width=\"624\"></p> \n<p><strong>3. You'll see a few pie options here, including 2-dimensional and 3-dimensional. For our purposes, let's click on the first image of a 2-dimensional pie chart. </strong></p> \n<p><img alt=\"Various pie chart design options, including 2-D and 3-D pies, in excel.\" src=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/hs-fs/hubfs/Google%20Drive%20Integration/How%20to%20Create%20a%20Pie%20Chart%20in%20Excel%20in%2060%20Seconds%20or%20Less.jpeg?width=624&amp;name=How%20to%20Create%20a%20Pie%20Chart%20in%20Excel%20in%2060%20Seconds%20or%20Less.jpeg\" style=\"margin-left: 0.00px;\" title=\"\" width=\"624\"></p> \n<p><strong>4. And there you have it! A pie chart will appear with the data and labels you've highlighted. </strong></p> \n<p><img alt=\"A complete pie chart created in excel.\" src=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/hs-fs/hubfs/Google%20Drive%20Integration/How%20to%20Create%20a%20Pie%20Chart%20in%20Excel%20in%2060%20Seconds%20or%20Less-Apr-13-2021-10-58-39-63-PM.png?width=496&amp;height=329&amp;name=How%20to%20Create%20a%20Pie%20Chart%20in%20Excel%20in%2060%20Seconds%20or%20Less-Apr-13-2021-10-58-39-63-PM.png\" style=\"margin-left: auto; margin-right: auto; display: block;\" title=\"\" width=\"496\" height=\"329\"></p> \n<p><strong>If you're not happy with the pie chart colors or design, however, you also have plenty of editing options. </strong></p> \n<p><strong>Let's dive into those, next. </strong></p> \n<h2 style=\"font-weight: normal;\">How to Edit a Pie Chart in Excel</h2> \n<h3>Background Color</h3> \n<p><strong>1. You can change the background color by clicking on the paint bucket icon under the \"Format Chart Area\" sidebar.</strong></p> \n<p><strong>Then, choose the fill type (whether you want a solid color as your pie chart background, or whether you want the fill to be gradient or patterned), and the background color.</strong></p> \n<p><img alt=\"The background color tool for pie charts in excel.\" src=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/hs-fs/hubfs/Google%20Drive%20Integration/How%20to%20Create%20a%20Pie%20Chart%20in%20Excel%20in%2060%20Seconds%20or%20Less-Apr-13-2021-10-58-39-83-PM.png?width=624&amp;height=388&amp;name=How%20to%20Create%20a%20Pie%20Chart%20in%20Excel%20in%2060%20Seconds%20or%20Less-Apr-13-2021-10-58-39-83-PM.png\" style=\"margin-left: 0.00px;\" title=\"\" width=\"624\" height=\"388\"></p> \n<h3>Pie Chart Text</h3> \n<p><strong>2. Next, click on the text within the pie chart itself if you want to rewrite anything, expand the text, or move the text to a new area of your pie chart. </strong></p> \n<p><img alt=\"The text editor tool for pie charts in excel.\" src=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/hs-fs/hubfs/Google%20Drive%20Integration/How%20to%20Create%20a%20Pie%20Chart%20in%20Excel%20in%2060%20Seconds%20or%20Less.png?width=624&amp;height=404&amp;name=How%20to%20Create%20a%20Pie%20Chart%20in%20Excel%20in%2060%20Seconds%20or%20Less.png\" style=\"margin-left: 0.00px;\" title=\"\" width=\"624\" height=\"404\"></p> \n<h3>Pie Chart Border</h3> \n<p><strong>3. Within the Format Chart Area, you can edit the border of your pie chart as well — including the border transparency, width, and color. </strong></p> \n<p><img alt=\"The border tool for pie charts in excel in the Format Chart Area sidebar.\" src=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/hubfs/Google%20Drive%20Integration/How%20to%20Create%20a%20Pie%20Chart%20in%20Excel%20in%2060%20Seconds%20or%20Less-Apr-13-2021-10-58-40-18-PM.png\" style=\"margin-left: auto; margin-right: auto; display: block;\" title=\"\"></p> \n<h3>Pie Chart Shadows</h3> \n<p><strong>4. To change the pie chart box itself (including the box's shadow, edges, and glow), click on the pentagon shape in the Format Chart Area sidebar. </strong></p> \n<p><strong>Then, toggle the bar across \"Transparency\", \"Size\", \"Blur\", and \"Angle\" until you're happy with the shadow of your pie chart box. </strong></p> \n<p><img alt=\"The shadow, glow, soft edges, or 3-d format options for pie charts in excel.\" src=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/hs-fs/hubfs/Google%20Drive%20Integration/How%20to%20Create%20a%20Pie%20Chart%20in%20Excel%20in%2060%20Seconds%20or%20Less-Apr-13-2021-10-58-40-40-PM.png?width=624&amp;name=How%20to%20Create%20a%20Pie%20Chart%20in%20Excel%20in%2060%20Seconds%20or%20Less-Apr-13-2021-10-58-40-40-PM.png\" style=\"margin-left: 0.00px;\" title=\"\" width=\"624\"></p> \n<h3>Pie Chart Colors</h3> \n<p><strong>5. Click the color paint palette, at the top left of excel, to change the colors of your pie chart. </strong></p> \n<p><strong>Excel offers a range of complementary colors — including a few presets under \"Colorful\", and a few presets under \"Monochromatic\". You can click between the options until you find a color palette you're happy with. </strong></p> \n<p><strong>(Alternatively, if you want to change the colors of your pie chart pieces individually, simply double click on the pie chart piece, toggle onto the paint section of the Format Chart Area, and choose a new color.)</strong></p> \n<p><img alt=\"The color options for your pie chart in excel as pre-set by excel.\" src=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/hs-fs/hubfs/Google%20Drive%20Integration/How%20to%20Create%20a%20Pie%20Chart%20in%20Excel%20in%2060%20Seconds%20or%20Less-2.png?width=624&amp;name=How%20to%20Create%20a%20Pie%20Chart%20in%20Excel%20in%2060%20Seconds%20or%20Less-2.png\" style=\"margin-left: 0.00px;\" title=\"\" width=\"624\"></p> \n<p><img src=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/hs-fs/hubfs/change%20color%20of%20pie%20chart%20pieces.gif?width=1814&amp;name=change%20color%20of%20pie%20chart%20pieces.gif\" alt=\"how to change the color of an individual pie chart piece in excel.\" width=\"1814\" style=\"width: 1814px;\"></p> \n<h3>Chart Title</h3> \n<p><strong>6. Change the chart title by clicking on the three bars graph icon in the top left of excel, and then toggling to \"Chart Title &gt; None\", \"Chart Title &gt; Above Chart\", or \"Chart Title &gt; Centered Overlay\". </strong></p> \n<p><img alt=\"The chart title tool in excel to edit the placement of your title for your pie chart.\" src=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/hubfs/Google%20Drive%20Integration/How%20to%20Create%20a%20Pie%20Chart%20in%20Excel%20in%2060%20Seconds%20or%20Less-4.png\" style=\"margin-left: auto; margin-right: auto; display: block;\" title=\"\"></p> \n<h3>Change Location of Data Labels</h3> \n<p><strong>7. On the same three bar graph icon, click \"Data Labels\" to modify where your labels appear on the pie chart. (For instance, do you want the pie chart pieces labelled in the middle of each pie chart portion, or on the outside?)</strong></p> \n<p><img alt=\"\" src=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/hubfs/Google%20Drive%20Integration/How%20to%20Create%20a%20Pie%20Chart%20in%20Excel%20in%2060%20Seconds%20or%20Less-Apr-13-2021-10-58-39-28-PM.png\" style=\"margin-left: auto; margin-right: auto; display: block;\" title=\"\"></p> \n<h3>Switch Row/Column</h3> \n<p><strong>8. If you'd prefer to switch which data appears in the pie chart, click \"Switch Row/Column\" to see alternate information aligned from your original data set. </strong></p> \n<p><img alt=\"The switch row/column button in excel.\" src=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/hs-fs/hubfs/Google%20Drive%20Integration/How%20to%20Create%20a%20Pie%20Chart%20in%20Excel%20in%2060%20Seconds%20or%20Less-1.jpeg?width=624&amp;name=How%20to%20Create%20a%20Pie%20Chart%20in%20Excel%20in%2060%20Seconds%20or%20Less-1.jpeg\" style=\"margin-left: 0.00px;\" title=\"\" width=\"624\"></p> \n<h2 style=\"font-weight: normal;\">How to Explode a Pie Chart in Excel</h2> \n<p><strong>1. To explode a piece of your pie chart (which can help you emphasize or draw attention to a specific section of your pie chart), simply double-click on the piece you want to pull away. </strong></p> \n<p><strong>Then, drag your cursor until it's the distance you want it, and you're all set! </strong></p> \n<p><img alt=\"The tool to drag a piece of your pie chart away from the whole in excel.\" src=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/hs-fs/hubfs/Google%20Drive%20Integration/How%20to%20Create%20a%20Pie%20Chart%20in%20Excel%20in%2060%20Seconds%20or%20Less.gif?width=624&amp;name=How%20to%20Create%20a%20Pie%20Chart%20in%20Excel%20in%2060%20Seconds%20or%20Less.gif\" style=\"margin-left: 0.00px;\" title=\"\" width=\"624\"></p> \n<h2 style=\"font-weight: normal;\">How to Create a 3D Pie Chart in Excel</h2> \n<p><strong>1. To create a 3-dimensional pie chart in excel, simply highlight your data and then click the \"Pie\" logo. </strong></p> \n<p><img alt=\"The pie chart button in excel\" src=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/hs-fs/hubfs/Google%20Drive%20Integration/How%20to%20Create%20a%20Pie%20Chart%20in%20Excel%20in%2060%20Seconds%20or%20Less-2.jpeg?width=624&amp;name=How%20to%20Create%20a%20Pie%20Chart%20in%20Excel%20in%2060%20Seconds%20or%20Less-2.jpeg\" style=\"margin-left: 0.00px;\" title=\"\" width=\"624\"></p> \n<p><strong>2. Then, choose the \"3-D Pie\" option.</strong></p> \n<p><img alt=\"The 3-D option for pie charts in excel to create a 3-dimensional version.\" src=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/hs-fs/hubfs/Google%20Drive%20Integration/How%20to%20Create%20a%20Pie%20Chart%20in%20Excel%20in%2060%20Seconds%20or%20Less-4.jpeg?width=624&amp;name=How%20to%20Create%20a%20Pie%20Chart%20in%20Excel%20in%2060%20Seconds%20or%20Less-4.jpeg\" style=\"margin-left: 0.00px;\" title=\"\" width=\"624\"></p> \n<p><strong>3. Finally, choose the design option you like at the top of your screen. </strong></p> \n<p><img alt=\"The design options for pie charts in excel. \" src=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/hs-fs/hubfs/Google%20Drive%20Integration/How%20to%20Create%20a%20Pie%20Chart%20in%20Excel%20in%2060%20Seconds%20or%20Less-3.png?width=624&amp;height=328&amp;name=How%20to%20Create%20a%20Pie%20Chart%20in%20Excel%20in%2060%20Seconds%20or%20Less-3.png\" style=\"margin-left: 0.00px;\" title=\"\" width=\"624\" height=\"328\"></p> \n<h2 style=\"font-weight: normal;\">How to Rotate a Pie Chart in Excel</h2> \n<p><strong>Finally, to rotate your pie chart, double-click on the chart and then click on the three-bar icon under \"Format Data Point\". </strong></p> \n<p><strong>Then, toggle the \"Angle of first slice\" until you've rotated the pie chart to the degree you want. </strong></p> \n<p><img alt=\"How to rotate a pie chart in excel using format data point.\" src=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/hs-fs/hubfs/Google%20Drive%20Integration/How%20to%20Create%20a%20Pie%20Chart%20in%20Excel%20in%2060%20Seconds%20or%20Less-Apr-13-2021-10-58-41-00-PM.jpeg?width=624&amp;name=How%20to%20Create%20a%20Pie%20Chart%20in%20Excel%20in%2060%20Seconds%20or%20Less-Apr-13-2021-10-58-41-00-PM.jpeg\" style=\"margin-left: 0.00px;\" title=\"\" width=\"624\"></p> \n<p>And there you have it! You're well on your way to creating clean, impressive pie charts for your marketing materials to highlight important data and move stakeholders to take action.</p> \n<p>Ultimately, you'll want to experiment with all of excel's unique formatting features until you figure out the pie chart that works best for your needs. Good luck!</p> \n<p></p> \n<p><a class=\"cta_button\" href=\"https://www.hubspot.com/cs/ci/?pg=7912de6f-792e-4100-8215-1f2bf712a3e5&amp;pid=53&amp;ecid=&amp;hseid=&amp;hsic=\"><img class=\"hs-cta-img ng":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx24/cdn67@2020_3/2021/04/23/17-35-49-322_ea9a3240e263c48b.webp","https://blog.hubspot.com/hs-fs/hubfs/Google%20Drive%20Integration/How%20to%20Create%20a%20Pie%20Chart%20in%20Excel%20in%2060%20Seconds%20or%20Less-1.jpeg?width=624&name=How%20to%20Create%20a%20Pie%20Chart%20in%20Excel%20in%2060%20Seconds%20or%20Less-1.jpeg":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx6/cdn3@2020_4/2021/04/23/17-35-49-008_b53dde64301f68af.webp","https://blog.hubspot.com/hs-fs/hubfs/Google%20Drive%20Integration/How%20to%20Create%20a%20Pie%20Chart%20in%20Excel%20in%2060%20Seconds%20or%20Less.gif?width=624&name=How%20to%20Create%20a%20Pie%20Chart%20in%20Excel%20in%2060%20Seconds%20or%20Less.gif":null,"https://blog.hubspot.com/hs-fs/hubfs/Google%20Drive%20Integration/How%20to%20Create%20a%20Pie%20Chart%20in%20Excel%20in%2060%20Seconds%20or%20Less-2.jpeg?width=624&name=How%20to%20Create%20a%20Pie%20Chart%20in%20Excel%20in%2060%20Seconds%20or%20Less-2.jpeg":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx8/cdn44@2020_6/2021/04/23/17-35-49-705_ed10cdca85e3a82f.webp","https://blog.hubspot.com/hs-fs/hubfs/Google%20Drive%20Integration/How%20to%20Create%20a%20Pie%20Chart%20in%20Excel%20in%2060%20Seconds%20or%20Less-4.jpeg?width=624&name=How%20to%20Create%20a%20Pie%20Chart%20in%20Excel%20in%2060%20Seconds%20or%20Less-4.jpeg":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx25/cdn47@2020_1/2021/04/23/17-35-49-113_c34f1efa71492637.webp","https://blog.hubspot.com/hs-fs/hubfs/Google%20Drive%20Integration/How%20to%20Create%20a%20Pie%20Chart%20in%20Excel%20in%2060%20Seconds%20or%20Less-3.png?width=624&height=328&name=How%20to%20Create%20a%20Pie%20Chart%20in%20Excel%20in%2060%20Seconds%20or%20Less-3.png":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx19/cdn59@2020_2/2021/04/23/17-35-50-279_165440a89b17eb53.webp","https://blog.hubspot.com/hs-fs/hubfs/Google%20Drive%20Integration/How%20to%20Create%20a%20Pie%20Chart%20in%20Excel%20in%2060%20Seconds%20or%20Less-Apr-13-2021-10-58-41-00-PM.jpeg?width=624&name=How%20to%20Create%20a%20Pie%20Chart%20in%20Excel%20in%2060%20Seconds%20or%20Less-Apr-13-2021-10-58-41-00-PM.jpeg":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx32/cdn40@2020_6/2021/04/23/17-35-48-421_3064d2feeeb1f204.webp","https://no-cache.hubspot.com/cta/default/53/7912de6f-792e-4100-8215-1f2bf712a3e5.png":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx3/cdn39@2020_3/2021/04/23/17-35-49-643_5cfe01436a49f100.webp","https://track.hubspot.com/__ptq.gif?a=53&k=14&r=https%3A%2F%2Fblog.hubspot.com%2Fmarketing%2Fmake-pie-chart-excel&bu=https%253A%252F%252Fblog.hubspot.com%252Fmarketing&bvt=rss":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx11/cdn3@2020_6/2021/04/23/17-35-49-467_1f0d8c1d0b751ea2.webp"},"publishedOrCreatedDate":1619199338326},{"createdTime":"2021-04-24 01:35:38","updatedTime":"2021-04-24 01:35:38","title":"Arise RevOps, the New Orchestrators of Customer Experience","link":"https://blog.hubspot.com/marketing/arise-revops-new-orchestrators-customer-experience","description":"<p>I care about customers. Whether they're your customers, my customers, or my customers'&nbsp;customers, I want every one of them to have a good experience every time they pick up the phone to call a&nbsp;business, open a marketing email, or visit a website.</p>  \n<p>It's what gets me going every morning. That's why I was thrilled in 2019 when I had&nbsp;the opportunity&nbsp;to launch HubSpot's first-ever 'voice of the customer' team.</p> \n<p>I assembled a group of passionate people, each more dedicated than the last to improving customer experience. We met weekly, talked about our customers, forensically analyzed feedback, and dug deep into the weeds to see where we could root out friction.</p> \n<p>And then one day it hit us. The answers to most of our questions didn't lie in more cross-functional meetings, increased headcount, or longer hours for support staff. The answers to our questions lay in operations.</p> \n<p>Operations teams carry the responsibility for making sure that, well, <em>everything</em>&nbsp;works. If a marketer is having trouble segmenting a contact list, they reach out to operations. If a salesperson's automated emails are misfiring, operations gets&nbsp;tagged in. If a service professional can't access a customer's communication history, it's operations to the rescue again.</p> \n<p>They're the people who set every customer-facing team up for success. As such, they are the orchestrators of the customer experience. And yet, most companies view operations as a reactive function whose sole purpose is to frantically find fixes to issues as they arise.</p> \n<p>It's time for us as an industry to re-imagine operations and transform these teams from reactive fire-fighters into proactive friction-fighters. How can we do this? With revenue operations (RevOps).</p> \n<p>It's my firm belief that operations teams can only fulfill their potential when they work together under a unified RevOps strategy and are equipped with the right tools to execute that strategy.</p> \n<p><span style=\"font-weight: bold;\">Today, HubSpot is spearheading the onrushing RevOps revolution with the launch of Operations Hub</span> — a new product specifically designed to empower operations teams to play an influential role in helping their companies delight customers at scale.</p> \n<p>Because when a company scales, friction inevitably emerges, and customer experience is often the first thing to suffer.</p> \n<p><a class=\"cta_button\" href=\"https://www.hubspot.com/cs/ci/?pg=2aedeaf3-d822-4747-8d62-f478a5445b75&amp;pid=53&amp;ecid=&amp;hseid=&amp;hsic=\"><img class=\"hs-cta-img \" style=\"border-width: 0px; /*hs-extra-styles*/; margin: 0 auto; display: block; margin-top: 20px; margin-bottom: 20px\" alt=\"Learn More About HubSpot's Operations Hub Software\" src=\"https://no-cache.hubspot.com/cta/default/53/2aedeaf3-d822-4747-8d62-f478a5445b75.png\" align=\"middle\"></a></p> \n<h2 style=\"font-weight: normal;\">Three&nbsp;Reasons Why Customer Experience Often Suffers When a Company Scales</h2> \n<p>There are few companies out there that impress me so much, I feel compelled to tweet about my experience, tell my friends, or write a positive review. These days, customers like me <em>expect </em>their interactions with every company to be quick, convenient, and contextual.</p> \n<p>When a company scales and begins to achieve exponential growth, the challenge of keeping pace with customer expectations grows exponentially, too. There are three key reasons why:</p> \n<h3 style=\"font-weight: normal;\">1. More customers to support.</h3> \n<p>When a company is in startup mode, it will usually keep up with the growth of its customer base by increasing investments in staff. When customer growth starts to outpace the company's ability to maintain a high standard of customer experience, it will likely raise capital and hire new employees to support the expanding demand. This works … for a while.</p> \n<p>When that company is ready to scale – that is, to grow its business faster than its investments – it needs to support a growing customer base <em>without</em>&nbsp;simply hiring more employees and <em>without</em>&nbsp;letting the quality of the customer experience drop. To do this, it has to reinvent its approach to delighting customers or risk losing the trust of its user base – and its market share.</p> \n<h3 style=\"font-weight: normal;\">2. More tools to manage.</h3> \n<p>As a company grows, it will inevitably encounter new challenges. And in a world of <a href=\"https://chiefmartec.com/2020/04/marketing-technology-landscape-2020-martech-5000/\">over 8,000 martech solutions</a>, there is no shortage of tools out there that could be brought in to help solve a problem quickly. So, it's common for different teams to adopt different tools to help them solve different problems.</p> \n<p>Over time, this approach results in a brutally bloated tech stack that takes so much time and energy to manage, there's little left to dedicate to customers. What's more, when tech stacks are unnecessarily complex, it becomes increasingly difficult for customer-facing teams to access reliable data, making it nearly impossible to deliver the type of contextual experience customers expect.</p> \n<h3 style=\"font-weight: normal;\">3. More touchpoints to maintain.</h3> \n<p>When a company is getting off the ground, it will tend to focus on a small number of high-impact channels. For example, its early social media marketing strategy may focus exclusively on, say, Facebook and Twitter, and it might only take customer queries over the phone.</p> \n<p>As that company seeks to scale, however, it will add new channels to its marketing mix and offer its customers more ways to get in touch. Pretty soon, it'll find itself interacting with its audience not only on Facebook, Twitter, and over the phone, but on Instagram, LinkedIn, YouTube, and via 24/7 web chat, too.</p> \n<p>To manage this multitude of touchpoints, that company will need a new strategy to ensure it maintains the quality of experience it offered to customers when there were only a few channels in play.</p> \n<p>These three issues are a by-product of scale. They are challenges a company <em>wants</em>&nbsp;to have … and solve. Yet, most businesses fall short. They naturally fall back on the methods that have helped them reach this critical moment in their journey — many continue to frantically hire staff long after it's sustainable to do so, some rush to tack more tools onto their tech stacks without the infrastructure to make them all work together, and others simply leave certain touchpoints unattended, leaving customers unimpressed.</p> \n<p>Operations professionals are uniquely positioned to help a company solve challenges like these. But historically, companies across our industry have failed to recognize the potential of their operations teams, leaving them stuck in silos and asking them to solve issues without the right tools or team structure to do so effectively.</p> \n<h3 style=\"font-weight: normal;\">Moving From Function-Out To Customer-In</h3> \n<p>Operations professionals are rarely among the first hires a company makes. They tend to be brought in only when systems start to creak and the friction between teams becomes unbearable. A company's marketing leader might hire an operations professional onto their team to help improve its lead scoring system, while its head of sales brings in their own operations hire to&nbsp;work on reporting.</p> \n<p>Before long, there are multiple operations teams working in different departmental silos, often out of different operating systems. In this setup, even if each operations team does an exceptionally good job at fighting friction <em>within</em>&nbsp;their department, friction can still be rife <em>between </em>their departments.</p> \n<p>For example, the sales team might be having difficulty accessing and understanding the marketing team's data, hurting their ability to personalize their outreach based on a prospect's recent engagement.</p> \n<p>With no team accountable for overseeing this critical cross-departmental touchpoint, prospects will continue to receive impersonal emails, the marketing team will continue to receive exasperated messages from their sales colleagues, and the sales team will continue to struggle to win over prospects.</p> \n<p>I call this a \"function-out\" perspective, where each customer-facing team is only focused on the portion of the customer experience they're directly responsible for, and each operations professional is tasked with supporting their designated function.</p> \n<p>What companies need instead is a “customer-in” perspective, where all teams work in unison, informed by a holistic view of the customer, to deliver a unified experience. Operations professionals have a critical role to play in driving this shift in perspective. But to be successful, they too need to be unified.</p> \n<h3><span style=\"font-weight: normal;\">How RevOps Helps Companies Scale Customer Experience</span></h3> \n<p>One of the most powerful things a company can do to scale its customer experience is to unify its functional operations professionals under one centralized revenue operations (RevOps) strategy.</p> \n<blockquote>\n When operations teams are unified, they are not serving their separate teams' goals, they are serving the customer. They work with the same data, which gives them a single source of truth on what's really going on with customers at a holistic level.\n</blockquote> \n<p>They collaborate on cross-functional processes that allow them to bridge the gaps between teams where friction frequently festers. And perhaps most importantly, they work together to proactively identify issues <em>before</em>&nbsp;they have a chance to hurt the customer experience.</p> \n<p>Companies that don't yet have a large number of operations professionals among their ranks don't have to wait until they do to start adopting a \"customer-in\" perspective. If they haven't hired an operations professional yet, they should consider bringing one in as a priority and giving them a meaningful say in how <em>all</em>&nbsp;customer-facing teams work together, not just one.</p> \n<p>They should also examine the ways their internal teams are set up within their current operating model, assess whether the systems they're using are contributing to silos, and begin to instill a culture of alignment around the customer.</p> \n<p>After all, RevOps is not just the name of a team, it's a philosophy by which to run a company — one that thrives when operations teams are equipped with the right tools.</p> \n<h3 style=\"font-weight: normal;\">Introducing Operations Hub</h3> \n<p>Today with the launch of Operations Hub, we are giving operations teams a suite of tools that allow them to assume their rightful place at the forefront of the customer experience and empower them to guide their companies through the customer experience challenges that come with scale.</p> \n<blockquote> \n <p>With Operations Hub, teams can sync data across their business apps bi-directionally and in real-time, allowing them to manage a tech stack with ease, no matter how complex it is.</p> \n</blockquote> \n<p>They can roll out workflows that automatically keep their database clean and up to date, helping them to maintain a reliable view of the customer, no matter how many touchpoints they manage. And they can design sophisticated custom automation actions to deliver a deeply personalized and contextual experience to customers, no matter how large their customer base grows.</p> \n<p>Together, these tools free up operations teams to conduct bold ambitious experiments, test big innovative ideas, and launch ground-breaking new strategies, all in the name of delivering an exceptional customer experience. For too long our industry has put a limit on the potential of operations professionals. That changes today.</p> \n<p>Back in 2019, I had the opportunity to launch HubSpot's 'voice of the customer' team. That experience opened my eyes to the vital role operations teams have to play in scaling customer experience.</p> \n<p>At the beginning of 2021, I had the opportunity to launch another team at HubSpot: the revenue operations team. With Operations Hub at our fingertips and our operations professionals unified as one, we are on a mission to elevate the role of operations teams not only at our company, but across the entire industry.</p> \n<p>If you work in operations like me, you have a right to feel excited. Where you were once reactive, you can now be proactive. Where you were once siloed, you can now be in sync with your operations teammates. And where you were once an afterthought of the customer-facing teams you support, you can now be the orchestrator of your company's customer experience strategy.</p> \n<p><a class=\"cta_button\" href=\"https://www.hubspot.com/cs/ci/?pg=3a26e52f-36cb-47a5-a280-05e034358de2&amp;pid=53&amp;ecid=&amp;hseid=&amp;hsic=\"><img class=\"hs-cta-img \" style=\"border-width: 0px; /*hs-extra-styles*/; \" alt=\"New Call-to-action\" src=\"https://no-cache.hubspot.com/cta/default/53/3a26e52f-36cb-47a5-a280-05e034358de2.png\"></a></p> \n<p></p>  \n<img src=\"https://track.hubspot.com/__ptq.gif?a=53&amp;k=14&amp;r=https%3A%2F%2Fblog.hubspot.com%2Fmarketing%2Farise-revops-new-orchestrators-customer-experience&amp;bu=https%253A%252F%252Fblog.hubspot.com%252Fmarketing&amp;bvt=rss\" alt=\"\" width=\"1\" height=\"1\" style=\"min-height:1px!important;width:1px!important;border-width:0!important;margin-top:0!important;margin-bottom:0!important;margin-right:0!important;margin-left:0!important;padding-top:0!important;padding-bottom:0!important;padding-right:0!important;padding-left:0!important; \">","descriptionType":"html","publishedDate":"Wed, 21 Apr 2021 12:30:00 +0000","feedId":54,"bgimg":"https://no-cache.hubspot.com/cta/default/53/2aedeaf3-d822-4747-8d62-f478a5445b75.png","linkMd5":"5d900f01a940fa833d82bd585151340a","bgimgJsdelivr":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx29/cdn21@2020_4/2021/04/23/17-35-38-440_2d74bc1ab1fe97d5.webp","destWidth":487,"destHeight":59,"sourceBytes":5441,"destBytes":7616,"author":"aelworthy@hubspot.com (Alison Elworthy)","articleImgCdnMap":{"https://no-cache.hubspot.com/cta/default/53/2aedeaf3-d822-4747-8d62-f478a5445b75.png":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx29/cdn21@2020_4/2021/04/23/17-35-38-440_2d74bc1ab1fe97d5.webp","https://no-cache.hubspot.com/cta/default/53/3a26e52f-36cb-47a5-a280-05e034358de2.png":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx22/cdn35@2020_4/2021/04/23/17-35-49-470_a44c8ab4e5aed43a.webp","https://track.hubspot.com/__ptq.gif?a=53&k=14&r=https%3A%2F%2Fblog.hubspot.com%2Fmarketing%2Farise-revops-new-orchestrators-customer-experience&bu=https%253A%252F%252Fblog.hubspot.com%252Fmarketing&bvt=rss":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx22/cdn9@2020_2/2021/04/23/17-35-48-329_bce9603d46fa4aab.webp"},"publishedOrCreatedDate":1619199338326},{"createdTime":"2021-04-24 01:35:38","updatedTime":"2021-04-24 01:35:38","title":"YouTube Algorithm: The Constantly Updated Guide to YouTube's Updates & Changes","link":"https://blog.hubspot.com/marketing/youtube-algorithm","description":"<p>Since marketers are at the mercy of algorithms on nearly every publishing channel, knowing how each of these unique algorithms work is crucial to attracting and maintaining an audience.</p> \n<p>Luckily, while some channels are rather reserved about the secrets of their algorithms, YouTube, which boasts over <a href=\"https://www.youtube.com/intl/en-GB/about/press/\">2 billion</a> users, has been remarkably transparent. It launched a <a href=\"https://creatoracademy.youtube.com/page/lesson/discovery\">course for creators about getting discovered</a>, walking them through the nitty-gritty details of increasing their visibility on the platform.</p> \n<p>Naturally, we took the course to help you understand exactly how to boost your rankings on the video platform. Read on to learn what we discovered and how you can <a href=\"https://academy.hubspot.com/courses/youtube-marketing\">grow your audience on YouTube</a>.</p> \n<p><a class=\"cta_button\" href=\"https://www.hubspot.com/cs/ci/?pg=b33cfd44-133a-49e3-a943-086c5679d485&amp;pid=53&amp;ecid=&amp;hseid=&amp;hsic=\"><img class=\"hs-cta-img \" style=\"border-width: 0px; /*hs-extra-styles*/; margin: 0 auto; display: block; margin-top: 20px; margin-bottom: 20px\" alt=\"→ Free Templates: How to Use YouTube for Business [Download Now]\" src=\"https://no-cache.hubspot.com/cta/default/53/b33cfd44-133a-49e3-a943-086c5679d485.png\" align=\"middle\" /></a></p> \n<h2>How does the YouTube algorithm work?</h2> \n<p>YouTube’s algorithm serves the most relevant, personalized videos to their users on five different sections of their platform: Search, Home, Suggested Videos, Trending, Subscriptions, and Notifications.</p> \n<p>By helping users find the videos they’re most likely to watch and enjoy, YouTube can keep viewers on the platform for as long as possible and get them to visit their site regularly.</p> \n<p>To figure out which videos and channels users are most likely to enjoy watching, YouTube “follows” their audience, which means they track their users’ engagement with each video they watch. More specifically, they pay attention to which videos each user watches and doesn’t watch, how much time they spend watching each video, which videos they like and dislike, and which videos they’re not interested in based on <a href=\"https://support.google.com/youtube/answer/6342839?hl=en&amp;ref_topic=9257501\">the user’s feedback</a>.</p> \n<p>Since their algorithm rewards engagement instead of vanity metrics like views and clicks, YouTube incentivizes creators to produce videos that their audience actually enjoys watching, discouraging them from trying to game the system.</p> \n<p>But YouTube’s algorithm also uses different signals and metrics to rank and recommend videos on each section of their platform. With this in mind, let's go over how the algorithm serves content via YouTube's six main user categories: Search, Home, Suggested Videos, Trending, Subscriptions, and Notifications.</p> \n<h3>Search</h3> \n<p>The two biggest factors that affect your videos’ search rankings are <a href=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/marketing/youtube-algorithm#how-to-optimize-videos-on-youtube\">keyword relevance and engagement metrics</a>. When ranking videos in search, YouTube will consider how well your titles, descriptions, and content match each user’s queries. They’ll also consider how many videos users have watched from your channel and the last time they watched other videos surrounding the same topic as your video.<img src=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/hs-fs/hubfs/youtube-search-results.jpeg?width=650&amp;name=youtube-search-results.jpeg\" alt=\"YouTube search results page\" width=\"650\" style=\"width: 650px; margin-left: auto; margin-right: auto; display: block;\" /></p> \n<p>Although the user’s history is important, YouTube also <a href=\"https://creatoracademy.youtube.com/page/lesson/discovery\">looks at</a> “which videos have driven the most engagement for a query.” The Search section also offers sponsored ads related to the query.</p> \n<h3>Home</h3> \n<p>When users access the home page, they first see videos from their subscriptions, then suggested videos based on their previous watch history and the videos’ performance. While you may be tempted to try to snag a coveted spot on the page, YouTube encourages creators to simply create good content that people want to watch and click on.</p> \n<p><img src=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/hs-fs/hubfs/youtube-home-page.jpeg?width=650&amp;name=youtube-home-page.jpeg\" alt=\"YouTube home page with recommended videos\" width=\"650\" style=\"width: 650px; margin-left: auto; margin-right: auto; display: block;\" /></p> \n<h3>Suggested Videos</h3> \n<p>No two users will have the same experience on YouTube — they want to serve the most relevant, personalized recommendations to each of their viewers. To do this, they analyze users’ activity history and find hundreds of videos that could be relevant to them.</p> \n<p>Then, they rank these videos based on 1) how well each video has engaged and satisfied similar users, 2) how often each viewer watches videos from each channel or other videos surrounding the same topic, and 3) how many times YouTube has already shown each video to users.</p> \n<p>YouTube has also noticed users tend to watch more content when they receive recommendations from a variety of channels, so they like to diversify their suggested videos feed.</p> \n<h3>Trending</h3> \n<p>The trending page is a feed of new and popular videos in a user’s specific country. You’ll find it by heading to Explore on the sidebar, then clicking on Trending.</p> \n<p>YouTube wants to balance popularity with novelty when they rank videos in this section, so they heavily consider view count and rate of view growth for each video they rank. They also split trending videos into four categories: “Now,” “Music,” “Gaming,” and “Movies.”</p> \n<p><img src=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/hs-fs/hubfs/youtube-trending-page.jpeg?width=650&amp;name=youtube-trending-page.jpeg\" alt=\"YouTube trending page with videos released 1 day ago\" width=\"650\" style=\"width: 650px; margin-left: auto; margin-right: auto; display: block;\" /></p> \n<h3>Subscriptions</h3> \n<p>YouTube has a subscriptions page where users can view all the recently uploaded videos from the channels they subscribe to. But this page isn’t the only benefit channels get when they acquire a ton of subscribers.</p> \n<p>To determine rankings on their platform, YouTube uses a metric called view velocity, which measures the number of subscribers who watch your video right after it's published. And the higher your video’s view velocity, the higher your videos will rank. YouTube also accounts for the number of active subscribers you have when they rank your videos.</p> \n<p><img src=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/hs-fs/hubfs/youtube-subscription-page.jpeg?width=650&amp;name=youtube-subscription-page.jpeg\" alt=\"YouTube subscriptions page with new videos from subscribed channels\" width=\"650\" style=\"width: 650px; margin-left: auto; margin-right: auto; display: block;\" /></p> \n<h3>Notifications</h3> \n<p>YouTube also delivers tailored videos to users through notifications. Users can opt to either receive no notifications from a channel, receive some notifications, or receive all notifications.</p> \n<p>The only way to optimize for showing up in users’ notifications is to ask your subscribers to tap the bell button next to the subscribe button.</p> \n<p><img src=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/hs-fs/hubfs/youtube-subscribe-to-notifications-bell.png?width=650&amp;name=youtube-subscribe-to-notifications-bell.png\" alt=\"YouTube subscribe to notifications bell underneath a video\" width=\"650\" style=\"width: 650px; margin-left: auto; margin-right: auto; display: block;\" /></p> \n<p>But how can you ask anyone to do that if you don’t yet have enough viewers and subscribers? By optimizing your videos for YouTube’s algorithm, you can grow your audience. Remember: it all comes down to creating good content that people want to watch.</p> \n<a></a> \n<h2>How to Optimize Your Videos for YouTube’s Algorithm</h2> \n<p>YouTube ranks videos based on two qualities: <strong>keyword</strong> <strong>relevance</strong> and <strong>engagement</strong> <strong>metrics </strong>(which are used to measure a video’s performance).</p> \n<p>Let’s take a look at both of these in more detail.</p> \n<h3>1. Keyword Relevance</h3> \n<p>To rank on YouTube, the first thing to consider is optimizing your videos and channel for popular search queries. To do this, place relevant keywords in your videos’ titles, tags, descriptions, SRT files (which are transcriptions), video files, and thumbnail files.</p> \n<p>You should also check out the most popular queries guiding viewers to your videos, which you can find in YouTube’s Search Report. If these queries are slightly different from your video’s topic, consider updating your video to fill these content gaps and add the keywords to your metadata. If there’s a stark difference, consider making new videos about these popular queries.</p> \n<h3>2. Engagement Metrics</h3> \n<p>The next thing to consider when ranking on YouTube is optimizing your videos and channel for engagement. The key metric to consider here is <strong>watch time</strong>, or the aggregate amount of time users spend watching your videos.</p> \n<p>To get people to watch in the first place, you need to attract users’ attention. And one of the best ways to instantly grab users’ attention is by creating vibrant thumbnails for each of your videos.</p> \n<p>Thumbnails — the small, clickable snapshots that viewers see when they search for videos on YouTube — are just as important as a video’s title. They provide a preview of your video and entice viewers to click through. This can help you differentiate yourself on a platform clogged with standard thumbnails all screaming for attention.</p> \n<p>To create a striking thumbnail, consider including a talking head because people are naturally drawn to human faces. Additionally, consider contrasting the colors of your thumbnail's foreground and background to really make it pop.</p> \n<p>Once you’ve attracted users’ attention, you can engage them by creating a bingeable series or show. You can also create playlists about a certain topic that start off with the videos that have the highest audience retention rate. This will increase the odds that users will watch most of the videos in your playlists, boosting your channel and videos’ watch time.</p> \n<p>Another way to refine your overall video strategy is by measuring your videos’ performance against other engagement metrics, like average watch percentage, average view duration, audience retention, and average session duration. If you can figure out which topics and videos generate the most engagement, and you solely focus on creating those types of content, you’ll be able to shoot up in YouTube’s search results page and suggested videos feed.</p> \n<p>Now that we’ve covered how the YouTube algorithm works and how you can optimize your videos for it, let’s take a look at how the algorithm has changed over the years.</p> \n<h2>YouTube Algorithm Change</h2> \n<p>Like the <a href=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/marketing/google-updates\">Google algorithm</a>, the YouTube algorithm has changed over the years — albeit less frequently and without a dedicated name to each update. Knowing how the algorithm has changed is key to understanding the platform and optimizing your videos to rank.</p> \n<h3>2005 - 2012: Views</h3> \n<p>Before there was ever a “formal” YouTube algorithm, YouTube ranked videos by view count. If a video had been watched hundreds of thousands of times, it’d be suggested to everyone, regardless of their interest in the topic or genre of the video.</p> \n<p>This was an easy system to cheat. Constantly refreshing the page was one method creators used to up the view count. Others used clickbait titles to get more clicks.</p> \n<h3>2012 - 2015: Watch Time</h3> \n<p>While watch time is still highly relevant to YouTube’s algorithm, it’s not the central piece. But it was from 2012 to 2015.</p> \n<p>YouTube wants users to stay on the platform. As such, videos with long watch times were favored over others and placed on the home page. It signaled to YouTube that the video was worth watching and that it was providing a positive experience to users.</p> \n<p>Creators tried to optimize for this change by creating extra long videos — or really short videos that users would watch from beginning to end. In response, YouTube began to focus on overall viewer satisfaction, <a href=\"https://blog.youtube/news-and-events/continuing-our-work-to-improve\">including</a> “measuring likes, dislikes, surveys, and time well spent” on each video.</p> \n<h3>2016: “Deep Learning” for Recommendations</h3> \n<p>Since there are millions of videos on the platform, YouTube found it challenging to recommend the most relevant and watch-worthy videos to individual users. Using a practice called “deep learning,” YouTube started to take a close look at the user’s history to generate candidates and rank those videos based on the user’s activity.</p> \n<p>The “video corpus” goes through two funnels: a “candidate generation” and “ranking” funnel. First, YouTube examines the user’s history to create a pool of candidates, which are then sent through the “ranking” funnel.</p> \n<p><img src=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/hs-fs/hubfs/youtube-deep-learning-funnel.png?width=650&amp;name=youtube-deep-learning-funnel.png\" alt=\"YouTube deep learning funnel visualizing how users get tailored recommendations\" width=\"650\" style=\"width: 650px; margin-left: auto; margin-right: auto; display: block;\" /></p> \n<p style=\"text-align: center; font-size: 12px;\"><a href=\"https://static.googleusercontent.com/media/research.google.com/en//pubs/archive/45530.pdf\" style=\"font-style: italic;\">Image Source</a></p> \n<p>Once the videos reach the ranking funnel, they’re assigned a score and presented to the user from highest to lowest score. This is still a prominent part of the algorithm and likely the way we still get recommendations.</p> \n<h3>2017 - 2020: Removal of “Borderline Content”</h3> \n<p>On the <a href=\"https://www.youtube.com/howyoutubeworks\">How YouTube Works</a> website, YouTube advertises the four Rs of the platform:</p> \n<p>“We <strong>Remove</strong> content that violates our policies, <strong>Reduce</strong> the spread of harmful misinformation and borderline material, <strong>Raise up </strong>authoritative sources for news and information, and <strong>Reward</strong> trusted Creators.”</p> \n<p>While the four Rs have been in place since 2015, they were only used to deprioritize junk comments and launch a dedicated platform for the news industry. The four Rs became a more prominent part of the algorithm in 2017 when the platform redirected users seeking extremist propaganda, then in <a href=\"https://blog.youtube/news-and-events/continuing-our-work-to-improve\">2019</a> when the platform started to systematically remove content that “borderline” violates its <a href=\"https://www.youtube.com/howyoutubeworks/policies/community-guidelines/#community-guidelines\">Community Guidelines</a>.</p> \n<p>YouTube launched over <a href=\"https://blog.youtube/inside-youtube/the-four-rs-of-responsibility-raise-and-reduce\">30 changes</a> to diminish the promotion of videos spreading false and harmful misinformation. It also uses external evaluators to gauge whether a video qualifies as “borderline content” by using Google’s <a href=\"https://static.googleusercontent.com/media/guidelines.raterhub.com/en//searchqualityevaluatorguidelines.pdf\">public guidelines</a>.</p> \n<h3>Present: More Deep Learning and Tighter Control on Misinformation</h3> \n<p>YouTube has yet to announce any new changes to its algorithm, but we can assume that it continues using deep learning to personalize the user experience and continues upholding the four Rs to control the spread of misinformation.</p> \n<h2>Keep Track of the YouTube Algorithm to Succeed on the Platform</h2> \n<p>As the YouTube algorithm evolves, it’s important to keep track of its changes so that you know what does and doesn’t get promoted on the platform. If you’re a business or individual creator trying to grow an audience on YouTube, be sure to optimize your videos for the algorithm so that your channel wins a loyal list of subscribers.</p> Chi)","articleImgCdnMap":{"https://no-cache.hubspot.com/cta/default/53/b33cfd44-133a-49e3-a943-086c5679d485.png":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx23/cdn19@2020_6/2021/04/23/17-35-44-716_cf13f3171c1652e5.webp","https://blog.hubspot.com/hs-fs/hubfs/youtube-search-results.jpeg?width=650&name=youtube-search-results.jpeg":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx7/cdn20@2020_6/2021/04/23/17-35-50-093_7072d2df0c8d50e6.webp","https://blog.hubspot.com/hs-fs/hubfs/youtube-home-page.jpeg?width=650&name=youtube-home-page.jpeg":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx/cdn97@2020_1/2021/04/23/17-35-48-401_19f3eebaa9fa8fe2.webp","https://blog.hubspot.com/hs-fs/hubfs/youtube-trending-page.jpeg?width=650&name=youtube-trending-page.jpeg":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx10/cdn20@2020_3/2021/04/23/17-35-50-547_e913476b9033f55e.webp","https://blog.hubspot.com/hs-fs/hubfs/youtube-subscription-page.jpeg?width=650&name=youtube-subscription-page.jpeg":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx6/cdn39@2020_3/2021/04/23/17-35-50-598_fc10e514668d6e48.webp","https://blog.hubspot.com/hs-fs/hubfs/youtube-subscribe-to-notifications-bell.png?width=650&name=youtube-subscribe-to-notifications-bell.png":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx11/cdn71@2020_5/2021/04/23/17-35-48-393_568b21672f976be3.webp","https://blog.hubspot.com/hs-fs/hubfs/youtube-deep-learning-funnel.png?width=650&name=youtube-deep-learning-funnel.png":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx7/cdn88@2020_3/2021/04/23/17-35-50-301_d05b0ee8b008a052.webp","https://no-cache.hubspot.com/cta/default/53/7e8681b3-9162-45a4-b6a1-f33ff244a78a.png":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx31/cdn51@2020_2/2021/04/23/17-35-49-022_61f66f8328bd53cd.webp","https://track.hubspot.com/__ptq.gif?a=53&k=14&r=https%3A%2F%2Fblog.hubspot.com%2Fmarketing%2Fyoutube-algorithm&bu=https%253A%252F%252Fblog.hubspot.com%252Fmarketing&bvt=rss":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx21/cdn14@2020_2/2021/04/23/17-35-50-463_0c4cfae8778c3317.webp"},"publishedOrCreatedDate":1619199338326},{"createdTime":"2021-04-24 01:35:38","updatedTime":"2021-04-24 01:35:38","title":"7 Incredible Answers to \"What Is Your Greatest Weakness?\" — That Aren't \"Perfectionism\"","link":"https://blog.hubspot.com/marketing/what-is-your-greatest-weakness","description":"<p>So, you’ve finally got your foot in the door at your <a href=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/marketing/job-search?_ga=2.236823617.1786432847.1618237811-965946931.1618237811\">dream company</a>. You’ve submitted the <a href=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/marketing/how-to-write-a-standout-resume\">perfect resume</a> and made a lasting impression during the phone screen. All there’s left to do now is to win over the hiring manager in the face-to-face interview.</p> \n<p>As a <a href=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/marketing/signs-informed-candidate\">well-informed candidate</a>, you’re doing your research on the company and preparing your answers to the most important interview questions you can think of — the most notorious of them all being: “What is your greatest weakness?”</p> \n<p>You don't want to respond, \"I tend to work <em>too </em>hard,\" or \"I am too much of a perfectionist.\" That can easily come across as scripted and insincere at best and lacking in self-awareness at worst.</p> \n<p>Alternatively, you don't want to respond with weaknesses that will prevent you from succeeding in the role. For instance, if you're applying to be a project manager, you don't want to admit that you’re, “not very good with time management.\"</p> \n<p>Fortunately, there are ways to answer this question that will help you demonstrate your value as a candidate. Here, we've cultivated some incredible answers to the mainstay, \"What is your greatest weakness\" question — and don’t worry, these answers aren't \"perfectionism\".</p> \n<p><a class=\"cta_button\" href=\"https://www.hubspot.com/cs/ci/?pg=c213d2ee-1947-4655-8699-e2ecc7a1d8c9&amp;pid=53&amp;ecid=&amp;hseid=&amp;hsic=\"><img class=\"hs-cta-img \" style=\"border-width: 0px; /*hs-extra-styles*/; margin: 0 auto; display: block; margin-top: 20px; margin-bottom: 20px\" alt=\"Click Here to Subscribe to HubSpot's Marketing Blog\" src=\"https://no-cache.hubspot.com/cta/default/53/c213d2ee-1947-4655-8699-e2ecc7a1d8c9.png\" align=\"middle\"></a></p> \n<p></p> \n<h3>1. Choose a weakness that will not prevent you from succeeding in the role.</h3> \n<p>When an interviewer asks, \"What is your greatest weakness?\" they want to find out:</p> \n<ul> \n <li>Whether you have a healthy level of self-awareness</li> \n <li>Whether you can be open and honest, particularly about shortcomings</li> \n <li>Whether you pursue self-improvement and growth opportunities to combat these issues, as opposed to letting these weaknesses hold you back</li> \n</ul> \n<p>Ultimately, you'll want to use this question to demonstrate how you've used a weakness as motivation to learn a new skill or grow professionally. Everyone has weaknesses — your interviewer doesn't expect you to be perfect.</p> \n<p>If you're applying for a copywriting position with little necessity for math skills, you might admit, \"I struggle with numbers, and don't have much experience with data analytics. While math is not directly tied to my role as a writer, I believe it's important to have a rudimentary understanding of Google Analytics to ensure my work is performing well. To tackle this weakness, I've been taking online courses in data analytics.\"</p> \n<p>An answer like this shows the hiring manager that you recognize your areas for growth and are able to act on them without being told to do so. This kind of self-starter attitude is a plus for virtually any team.</p> \n<h3>2. Be honest and choose a real weakness.</h3> \n<p>The answer “perfectionism” won’t cut it when talking about your biggest weakness is simply because it’s <em>not</em> a real weakness. Perfectionism can never be attained — it’s a fear-based pattern that leads to short-term rewards like getting the job done early and exceeding expectations. However, in the long-term, trying to attain perfectionism leads to burnout, low-quality work, and missed deadlines. Burnout is one of the biggest contributors to <a href=\"https://www.business.com/articles/why-you-need-to-worry-about-burnout/#:~:text=Aside%20from%20the%20added%20costs,expectations%20or%20maximize%20their%20potentials.\">decreased productivity</a>, turnover, and low employee engagement — all of which cost a company money, time, and talent.</p> \n<p>Instead, choose a real weakness. Underneath the desire to do perfect work may lie a weakness of trust. Perhaps you don’t trust that you’ll be able to make mistakes on the team, so you strive to do everything perfectly. That’s a real weakness that you can definitely overcome.</p> \n<h3>3. Provide an example of how you've worked to improve upon your weakness or learn a new skill to combat the issue.</h3> \n<p>Hiring managers don’t expect you to overcome your weaknesses completely overnight. Everyone has areas they must constantly work on to keep them sharp. Think of it this way — if you’ve dedicated six months to working out, you won’t be able to stop one day and maintain your progress. It’s an ongoing process that you have to work at.</p> \n<p>By providing an example of how you’re working to improve your area of weakness, you’ll give the interviewer a glimpse into a few positive attributes about your work style:</p> \n<p style=\"padding-left: 40px;\">1. You know how to identify and mitigate issues that come up.</p> \n<p style=\"padding-left: 40px;\">2. You’ve found a helpful solution to a problem that you and perhaps others on the team face, which means you can be an immediate resource to the team.</p> \n<h3>4. You demonstrate self-awareness and an ability to look to others to provide you with resources necessary for growth.</h3> \n<p>More often than not, you’re going to need to look outside of yourself to overcome a weakness. Whether you look to your supervisor, <a href=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/\">the HubSpot Blog</a>, or a mentor for help, the simple act of asking for help demonstrates self-awareness and resourcefulness — two skills that are hard to teach, but valuable to learn. Tapping into your resources shows the interviewers that you can solve problems when the answer is not yet clear. That’s a character trait that has a place on any team.</p> \n<p>Briefly share an example of a time where you asked someone for help in an area that you’ve identified as a weakness. This gives the hiring team a clear picture of how you’ll work with the team to balance out that weakness.</p> \n<h3>5.Don't be arrogant and don't underestimate yourself.</h3> \n<p>The most important thing you can do when responding to the question “What is your greatest weakness?” is exhibit confidence in your answer. (If confidence is your weakness, keep reading.) Even if you’re not the most confident person, I’m going to assume you’re at least honest with yourself. If you’ve identified an area of weakness and you’re sure about it, let that assurance shine through in your answer. There’s no need to feel embarrassed about something you’re genuinely not good at as long as you’re working to get better.</p> \n<p>Before you start expressing a genuine weakness to your interviewer, get comfortable with the types of answers that make hiring managers want to work with you. Take a look at the following examples and find a few that fit your personality and work style. Then, practice reciting them aloud so they come naturally to you.</p> \n<p>Here are seven examples of how you might answer \"What is your greatest weakness?\" and why they work.</p> \n<p>Here are seven examples of how you might answer \"What is your greatest weakness\", and why they work.</p> \n<p></p> \n<h3>1. Patience</h3> \n<p><em>\"I don't have much patience when working with a team — I am incredibly self-sufficient, so it's difficult when I need to rely on others to complete my work. That's why I've pursued roles that require someone to work independently. However, I've also worked to improve this weakness by enrolling in team-building workshops. While I typically work independently, it's nonetheless important I learn how to trust my coworkers and ask for outside help when necessary.\"</em></p> \n<p>This answer works because the weakness — the inability to be patient when working with a team — doesn't hinder your ability to perform well in the role since it’s a job that doesn't rely on teamwork to succeed. Additionally, you display an eagerness to develop strategies to combat your weakness, which is a critical skill in the workplace.</p> \n<h3>2. Organization</h3> \n<p><em>\"I struggle with organization. While it hasn't ever impacted my performance, I've noticed my messy desk and cluttered inbox nonetheless could interfere with my efficiency. Over time, I've learned to set aside time to organize my physical and digital space, and I've seen it improve my efficiency levels throughout the week.\"</em></p> \n<p>Plenty of people have messy desks. This answer works because it's a relatable and fixable weakness. You note that disorganization doesn't interfere with your ability to do your job, which is critical, but you also acknowledge it might make you less efficient. To ensure you're performing at 100%, you mention personal steps you've taken to improve your organization skills for the sake of self-improvement alone, which suggests a level of maturity and self-awareness.</p> \n<h3>3. Delegation</h3> \n<p><em>\"I'm incredibly self-motivated, and I sometimes find it difficult to delegate responsibility when I feel I can finish the task well myself. However, when I became manager in my last role, it became critical I learn to delegate tasks. To maintain a sense of control when delegating tasks, I implemented a project management system to oversee the progress of a project. This system enabled me to improve my ability to delegate efficiently.\"</em></p> \n<p>This answer allows you to demonstrate an ability to pursue a new skill when a role calls for it and suggests you're capable of flexibility, which is critical for long-term growth. Additionally, you are able to showcase a level of initiative and leadership when you mention the successful implementation of a new process that enabled you to succeed in your past role, despite your weakness.</p> \n<h3>4. Timidity</h3> \n<p><em>\"Oftentimes, I can be timid when providing constructive feedback to coworkers or managers, out of fear of hurting someone's feelings. However, in my last role, my coworker asked me to edit some of his pieces and provide feedback for areas of improvement. Through my experience with him, I realized feedback can be both helpful and kind when delivered the right way. Since then I've become better at offering feedback, and I've realized that my empathy can be used to my advantage to provide thoughtful, productive feedback.\"</em></p> \n<p>This answer works because you've explained how you were able to turn a weakness into a strength through real-world experience. Typically, timidity can be seen as a flaw in the workplace, particularly if a role requires someone to provide feedback to others. In this case, you're able to demonstrate how timidity can be used as a strength, through thoughtful reflection and practice.</p> \n<h3>5. Candidness</h3> \n<p><em>\"My blunt, straightforward nature has allowed me to succeed over the years as a team manager, because I'm able to get things done efficiently, and people often appreciate my honesty. However, I've recognized my bluntness doesn't always serve my employees well when I'm delivering feedback. To combat this, I've worked to develop empathy and deeper relationships with those I manage. Additionally, I took an online leadership management course, and worked with the professor to develop my ability to deliver feedback.\"</em></p> \n<p>Oftentimes, facets of our personalities can help us in certain areas of our work, while hindering us in others. That's natural. However, you must demonstrate an ability to recognize when your personality interferes with the functions of your role, and how you can solve for that.</p> \n<p>In this example, you first explain how your blunt nature allows you to be successful in certain situations. Then, you mention that you understand your bluntness can be seen as a lack of empathy and provide examples of how you've attempted to solve this issue. Ultimately, your awareness of how you might be perceived by others shows a level of emotional intelligence, which is a critical asset for a team leader.</p> \n<h3>6. Public Speaking</h3> \n<p><em>\"Public speaking makes me nervous. While I don't need to do much public speaking in my role as a web designer, I still feel that it's an important skill — especially when I want to offer my opinion during a meeting. To combat this, I spoke with my manager and she recommended I speak at each team meeting for a few minutes about our project timeline, deadlines, and goals when developing a website for a client. This practice has enabled me to relax and see public speaking as an opportunity to help my team members do their jobs effectively.\"</em></p> \n<p>In this example, you mention a skill that isn't applicable to the role, but one which you nonetheless have been working to improve. This shows your desire to meet more business needs than necessary in your current role, which is admirable. Additionally, it's impressive if you can show you're willing to reach out to your manager with areas in which you want to improve, instead of waiting for your manager to suggest those areas of improvement to you — it demonstrates a level of ambition and professional maturity.</p> \n<h3>7. Data Analysis</h3> \n<p><em>\"I'm not great at analyzing data or numbers. However, I recognize this flaw can prevent me from understanding how my content is performing online. In my last role, I set up monthly meetings with the SEO manager to discuss analytics and how our posts were performing. Additionally, I received my Google Analytics certificate, and I make it a point to analyze data related to our blog regularly. I've become much more comfortable with data through these efforts.\"</em></p> \n<p>In this example, you're able to show your desire to go above and beyond a job description and actively seek out skills that could be helpful to the success of your company as a whole. This type of company-first mentality shows the interviewer you're dedicated to making yourself a valuable asset, and try your best to understand the needs of the whole department, rather than just your role.</p> \n<h2>There’s Strength In Every Weakness</h2> \n<p>Regardless of whether you’re bad with numbers or you tend not to speak up in group settings, there’s a strength behind every weakness. The strength is in how you work to overcome it. Leaning on your teammates who excel in those areas is a great way to show that you’ll work well on the team and that you know how to use your resources to solve problems. Taking professional development courses shows that you’re willing to work toward improvement. No matter which of these answers you share with the hiring team, they’ll be more than happy to help you grow and exceed the expectations of the role.</p> \n<p><em>Editor's note: This post was originally published in December 2018 and has been updated for comprehensiveness.</em></p> \n<p><a class=\"cta_button\" href=\"https://www.hubspot.com/cs/ci/?pg=995a3e7c-4d36-47d3-bb42-9f9f76888cac&amp;pid=53&amp;ecid=&amp;hseid=&amp;hsic=\"><img class=\"hs-cta-img \" style=\"border-width: 0px;
