\">","descriptionType":"html","publishedDate":"Wed, 21 Apr 2021 11:00:00 +0000","feedId":54,"bgimg":"https://no-cache.hubspot.com/cta/default/53/c213d2ee-1947-4655-8699-e2ecc7a1d8c9.png","linkMd5":"8845dc33967381a87af98eb912d19608","bgimgJsdelivr":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx31/cdn9@2020_2/2021/04/23/17-35-44-660_e560b1f3229e5641.webp","destWidth":471,"destHeight":59,"sourceBytes":5808,"destBytes":7726,"author":"Caroline Forsey","articleImgCdnMap":{"https://no-cache.hubspot.com/cta/default/53/c213d2ee-1947-4655-8699-e2ecc7a1d8c9.png":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx31/cdn9@2020_2/2021/04/23/17-35-44-660_e560b1f3229e5641.webp","https://no-cache.hubspot.com/cta/default/53/995a3e7c-4d36-47d3-bb42-9f9f76888cac.png":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx1/cdn91@2020_6/2021/04/23/17-35-50-044_b3ae4ea45fae0d4c.webp","https://track.hubspot.com/__ptq.gif?a=53&k=14&r=https%3A%2F%2Fblog.hubspot.com%2Fmarketing%2Fwhat-is-your-greatest-weakness&bu=https%253A%252F%252Fblog.hubspot.com%252Fmarketing&bvt=rss":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx24/cdn55@2020_4/2021/04/23/17-35-48-806_a1381184389ccb34.webp"},"publishedOrCreatedDate":1619199338325},{"createdTime":"2021-04-24 01:35:38","updatedTime":"2021-04-24 01:35:38","title":"Facebook Advertising Myths to Leave Behind in 2021","link":"https://blog.hubspot.com/marketing/facebook-ad-myths","description":"<p>Every day, there's a new article on <a href=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/marketing/facebook-paid-ad-checklist\">Facebook Ads</a>. Case in point, this one right here.</p>  \n<p>Given how powerful the advertising platform is, there are tons of recommendations out there aiming to steer you in the right direction for your next campaign.</p> \n<p><a class=\"cta_button\" href=\"https://www.hubspot.com/cs/ci/?pg=0e17c46b-0ab9-43a4-8ddb-bdf86aa56e78&amp;pid=53&amp;ecid=&amp;hseid=&amp;hsic=\"><img class=\"hs-cta-img \" style=\"border-width: 0px; /*hs-extra-styles*/; \" alt=\"Download Now: Free Facebook Advertising Checklist\" src=\"https://no-cache.hubspot.com/cta/default/53/0e17c46b-0ab9-43a4-8ddb-bdf86aa56e78.png\"></a></p> \n<p>However, not all recommendations are worth implementing.</p> \n<p>Let's revisit some of the most common Facebook Ads assumptions out there and get to the truth. It won't be as dramatic as an episode of <a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Maury_(talk_show)\">The Maury Show</a>, but it will do.</p> \n<h2>Myth 1. Facebook Ads don't work for B2B brands.</h2> \n<h3>Truth: Facebook is a great platform for B2B advertising.</h3> \n<p>When it comes to advertising to businesses, the first place people think of is LinkedIn, a network known for fostering professional relationships. Facebook has always been seen as a strictly direct-to-consumer (DTC) advertising platform.</p> \n<p>Facebook wasn't designed to be a business networking app, said <a href=\"https://www.linkedin.com/in/rex-gelb-43445b1b/\">Rex Gelb</a>, paid ads director at HubSpot, and thus, wasn't a top consideration for B2B lead generation. He argues it should be.</p> \n<p>\"To some extent, people are always open to business-related content, even if they're just mindlessly scrolling through their Facebook and Instagram feeds after a long day at the office,\" said Gelb. \"If you work in B2B, don't hesitate to give Facebook a try – you might be surprised by the results.\"</p> \n<p>Based on <a href=\"https://www.hubspot.com/state-of-marketing\">HubSpot's 2020 Not Another Marketing Report</a>, brands see the most return on investment (ROI) on Facebook compared to other social media platforms.</p> \n<p>SaaS companies like <a href=\"https://www.honeybook.com/\"><span>Honeybook</span></a> say Facebook is their largest acquisition channel, <a href=\"https://www.facebook.com/business/industries/b2b\"><span>according to the social network.</span></a> And they're not the only B2B company that relies on Facebook Ads to generate leads.</p> \n<p>\"We find it to be successful for B2B companies like ourselves to promote content and signups,\" said <a href=\"https://www.linkedin.com/in/nicole-ondracek-095024b0\"><span>Nicole Ondracek</span></a>, paid ads marketing manager at HubSpot.</p> \n<p>If you want to ensure you reach the right audience, Facebook Ads' lookalike audience feature allows you to target users based on their job title, industry, and employer – similar to LinkedIn.</p> \n<h2>Myth 2. You need a lot of money to get started.</h2> \n<h3>Truth: You only need $1 a day to compete with the big brands.</h3> \n<p>While some advertising channels require a decent budget to compete, brands can reach Facebook users for as little as $1 a day. <br><br>\"There's no big upfront commitment required and no large minimums,\" said Gelb. \"You're free to take things as slowly as you'd like and only scale when it makes sense to do so.\"<br><br>He adds that while one dollar will limit the ad inventory you have access to, you'll be on an even playing field with everyone else.<br><br>Ondracek echoes this sentiment. <br><br>\"While it's nice to have a large budget to bring in enough conversions and learnings to optimize your campaigns,\" she said, \"sometimes all you need is a small daily budget to start bringing in leads and customers.\"<br><br>On Facebook Ads, a little can go a long way.</p> \n<h2>Myth 3. You should create small, targeted audiences.</h2> \n<h3>Truth: Build your target audience but leave some wiggle room.</h3> \n<p><a href=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/marketing/facebook-advertising-targeting-options\">Facebook Ads' targeting </a>capabilities are impressive. You combine that with the idea that the more targeted your campaign, the better the results, and you run the risk of getting too narrow.<br><br>\"It's all about testing,\" said Ondracek. \"In some cases where we've tested large audiences (20M+), we've seen better success than narrowed audiences [and] going after a specific list of contacts.\"</p> \n<p>Creating exclusions during your audience creation process makes sense most of the time. For instance, excluding users located outside of a specific region. However, when your targeting gets too narrow, you can miss out on opportunities to reach audiences who would convert on your ad.</p> \n<p>\"Within your target audience, don't restrict Facebook too much by layering on dozens of filters such as age, device, placement, and gender,\" said Gelb. \"Facebook's ad serving algorithm was designed to find the most qualified audience at the cheapest cost.\"</p> \n<p>\"If you give Facebook the freedom to go find those people,\" he adds, \"in many cases, you'll end up with more scale and at a cheaper cost.\"</p> \n<p>Essentially, let the algorithm do its job. Define the key characteristics of your target audience and leave some room for your ad to reach those you may not have considered.</p> \n<h2>Myth 4. You should retarget all of your website visitors.</h2> \n<h3>Truth: Not everyone should be retargeted.</h3> \n<p>The Facebook pixel allows you to track user behavior on your website and retarget those same users on Facebook to guide them down the funnel. However, not every person who visits your website should be retargeted on Facebook Ads.</p> \n<p>You should still segment which website visitors to focus on, as not everyone who visits your site is ready for retargeting.</p> \n<p>For instance, let's say someone visits your \"About Us\" page. There are many reasons for this: They could be interested in your products, but they could also be looking for a new role. With that in mind, retargeting users based on any action taken on your website may not be valuable or cost-effective.</p> \n<p>Instead, focus on visitors who exhibit high-intent behaviors and will be more likely to convert. For instance, visitors who add products to their shopping carts, visit your pricing page or read your testimonials.</p> \n<p>Being selective will not only help you manage your budget better (especially if you have a small one) but it can also help you yield better results. <br><br>Ondracek highlights that sometimes, you should re-evaluate if retargeting is even the right strategy.<br><br>\"When retargeting works, it's great,\" she said, \"but we've found, in some cases, that retargeting site visitors is actually more expensive than prospecting.\"<br><br>It's all about finding what works for your brand. Just because Facebook is known for retargeting, doesn't mean that's the strategy that will work for your company every time.</p> \n<h2>Myth 5. Boosting a post will yield the same results as a campaign<span style=\"font-size: 16px;\">.</span></h2> \n<h3>Truth: Boosting may not always align with your goals.</h3> \n<p>When you boost a post on Facebook, it's a quick and easy way to expand your reach and gain some quick exposure. However, boosting a post won't necessarily convert users in the same way a campaign would.</p> \n<p>Why? Well, if your post isn't already designed to drive a particular action and you boost it, you may gain more impressions but no conversions.</p> \n<p>Depending on your goals, you may yield better results for less by creating an ad campaign. With the manual bidding feature, you can monitor how much you spend. You can also optimize your campaign based on your conversion goal.</p> \n<p>So, while boosting a post may seem like the best solution for a brand with limited Facebook Ads experience and a small budget, it may be quite the opposite.</p> \n<p>If you are going to use that strategy, be sure to consider the following:</p> \n<ul> \n <li>Does this post have a clear call-to-action (CTA)?</li> \n <li>Will boosting this post help you reach your goal?</li> \n <li>Could this work better as part of a larger campaign?</li> \n</ul> \n<p>Answering these questions will help you determine when to boost and when to go in another direction.</p> \n<p>The biggest takeaway here is that there aren't hard-and-fast rules when it comes to Facebook Ads. Some strategies may work for some brands and not for others. The only surefire way to figure out what works is by experimenting with various strategies.</p> \n<p>Ever wonder what's fact or fiction when it comes to Facebook Ads? In this article, we debunk some myths about the social network's advertising platform.</p> \n<p><a class=\"cta_button\" href=\"https://www.hubspot.com/cs/ci/?pg=32a90224-1f14-45bd-914a-d4053a3a4d35&amp;pid=53&amp;ecid=&amp;hseid=&amp;hsic=\"><img class=\"hs-cta-img \" style=\"border-width: 0px; /*hs-extra-styles*/; \" alt=\"New call-to-action\" src=\"https://no-cache.hubspot.com/cta/default/53/32a90224-1f14-45bd-914a-d4053a3a4d35.png\"></a></p> \n<p></p>  \n<img src=\"https://track.hubspot.com/__ptq.gif?a=53&amp;k=14&amp;r=https%3A%2F%2Fblog.hubspot.com%2Fmarketing%2Ffacebook-ad-myths&amp;bu=https%253A%252F%252Fblog.hubspot.com%252Fmarketing&amp;bvt=rss\" alt=\"\" width=\"1\" height=\"1\" style=\"min-height:1px!important;width:1px!important;border-width:0!important;margin-top:0!important;margin-bottom:0!important;margin-right:0!important;margin-left:0!important;padding-top:0!important;padding-bottom:0!important;padding-right:0!important;padding-left:0!important; \">","descriptionType":"html","publishedDate":"Wed, 21 Apr 2021 11:00:00 +0000","feedId":54,"bgimg":"https://no-cache.hubspot.com/cta/default/53/0e17c46b-0ab9-43a4-8ddb-bdf86aa56e78.png","linkMd5":"1dd2893e1a2f632f93721629d009f62a","bgimgJsdelivr":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx14/cdn12@2020_3/2021/04/23/17-35-38-475_2b065da29ad9384e.webp","destWidth":473,"destHeight":59,"sourceBytes":5649,"destBytes":7704,"author":"mbretous@hubspot.com (Martina Bretous)","articleImgCdnMap":{"https://no-cache.hubspot.com/cta/default/53/0e17c46b-0ab9-43a4-8ddb-bdf86aa56e78.png":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx14/cdn12@2020_3/2021/04/23/17-35-38-475_2b065da29ad9384e.webp","https://no-cache.hubspot.com/cta/default/53/32a90224-1f14-45bd-914a-d4053a3a4d35.png":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx14/cdn32@2020_4/2021/04/23/17-35-48-441_83636ffc61a7b708.webp","https://track.hubspot.com/__ptq.gif?a=53&k=14&r=https%3A%2F%2Fblog.hubspot.com%2Fmarketing%2Ffacebook-ad-myths&bu=https%253A%252F%252Fblog.hubspot.com%252Fmarketing&bvt=rss":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx30/cdn47@2020_4/2021/04/23/17-35-48-561_6c4351ecacea78f9.webp"},"publishedOrCreatedDate":1619199338326},{"createdTime":"2021-04-24 01:35:38","updatedTime":"2021-04-24 01:35:38","title":"The Ultimate Round-Up of Content Marketing Tips","link":"https://blog.hubspot.com/marketing/content-marketing-tips","description":"<p>There are nearly <a href=\"https://www.statista.com/statistics/617136/digital-population-worldwide/\">five billion</a> active internet users and over <a href=\"https://www.statista.com/statistics/617136/digital-population-worldwide/\">four billion</a> social media users worldwide — simply put, that's a ton of opportunity for your brand to engage with an audience and achieve massive growth for your business.</p>  \n<p>One of the most effective methods for spreading brand awareness and attracting new customers is through content marketing.</p> \n<p><a href=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/marketing/content-marketing\">Content marketing</a> is a marketing strategy that focuses on creating, publishing, and distributing valuable and relevant content online with the purpose of reaching a targeted audience and incentivizing profitable customer action. Ultimately, content marketing is a critical component for long-term, sustainable growth.</p> \n<p>And yet, despite its immense impact, many marketers don't know how to implement a successful content marketing strategy.</p> \n<p>To ensure you're able to cultivate a truly valuable marketing strategy, we've created this round-up of content marketing tips. Keep reading to become a true content marketing expert.</p> \n<a class=\"cta_button\" href=\"https://www.hubspot.com/cs/ci/?pg=a145a75e-59f6-4b51-a482-4f3ea486e740&amp;pid=53&amp;ecid=&amp;hseid=&amp;hsic=\"><img class=\"hs-cta-img \" style=\"border-width: 0px; /*hs-extra-styles*/; margin: 0 auto; display: block; margin-top: 20px; margin-bottom: 20px\" alt=\"Free Resource: Content Marketing Planning Template\" src=\"https://no-cache.hubspot.com/cta/default/53/a145a75e-59f6-4b51-a482-4f3ea486e740.png\" align=\"middle\"></a> \n<h3><img src=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/hs-fs/hubfs/seth-godin-content-marketing-quote.png?width=650&amp;name=seth-godin-content-marketing-quote.png\" alt=\"Content marketing tip by Seth Godin: &quot;Content marketing is all the marketing that's left.&quot; \" width=\"650\" style=\"width: 650px; margin-left: auto; margin-right: auto; display: block;\"></h3> \n<h3>1. Make sure your content has a clear, measurable business goal.</h3> \n<p>You might be overwhelmed by the sheer amount of content you can create for your business — anything from <a href=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/marketing/instagram-stories\">Instagram Stories</a>, to blog posts and e-books, to podcasts.</p> \n<p>However, as Karla Cook, Senior Manager of the HubSpot Blogs, notes, \"[It's critical] every single piece of content you're creating has a clear, measurable business goal in mind — and simply 'getting views' isn't a complete business goal. Take the time to think about how content can serve your overall marketing strategy, and create pieces that tie back to that.\"</p> \n<p>For instance, let's say you decide you want to lean heavily into a blogging strategy. Simply crafting and publishing content isn't enough — instead, it's important you identify your target audience and decide how your content can best serve that group. Additionally, you'll want to use analytics to ensure your content is able to reach the right people with the appropriate search intent.</p> \n<p>Once you identify how to serve your audience, you'll want to ask yourself, \"How does this tie back to the business?\" While it's critical you write quality content to grow your audience, it won't attract prospects if it doesn't tie back to your business.</p> \n<p>Take a look at <a href=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/marketing/hubspot-blog-traffic-record-flat-year?_ga=2.205438297.81589904.1554671928-644648569.1551722047\">the strategy that helped the HubSpot blog break a year-long traffic plateau</a> to learn more about cultivating a business-focused strategy for content creation.</p> \n<h3>2. Know your audience.</h3> \n<p>Content marketing is all about attracting the right audience — that is, those who are most likely to engage with your brand and buy your products. But you can’t write content that attracts the right audience until you know your audience.</p> \n<p>No need to go out and interview every customer who’s ever done business with you, although that could definitely be helpful. Sit down with your team and create a <a href=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/marketing/buyer-persona-definition-under-100-sr\">buyer persona</a>, the ideal customer who’s best served by your products. You’ll want to take into account both <a href=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/insiders/marketing-psychographics\">psychographic</a> and demographic information, and <a href=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/marketing/buyer-persona-research\">create a buyer persona document</a> that your team can refer to.</p> \n<p>Knowing your audience helps you create content that speaks to them as they go through the <a href=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/sales/what-is-the-buyers-journey\">buyer’s journey</a>.</p> \n<h3>3. Understand your buyer's journey.</h3> \n<p>A good content marketer understands that their strategy needs to engage and delight readers at any stage of the buyer's journey. While your content should initially attract new visitors to your business, it should also convince hesitant prospects to purchase, and encourage customer retention and long-term brand loyalty.</p> \n<p>For instance, perhaps some customers are hesitant to purchase your product because they believe you need extensive video knowledge to succeed with it. To help mitigate concerns and aid your sales team, you might create a video campaign to show customers how to use video marketing.</p> \n<p>If you’re feeling stumped, learn <a href=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/marketing/content-for-every-funnel-stage\">how to create content for every stage of the buyer's journey</a>.</p> \n<p><img src=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/hs-fs/hubfs/nate-elliot-content-marketing-quote.png?width=650&amp;name=nate-elliot-content-marketing-quote.png\" alt=\"Content marketing tip by Nate Elliot: &quot;If you want to create messages that resonate with your audience, you need to know what they care about.&quot; \" width=\"650\" style=\"width: 650px; margin-left: auto; margin-right: auto; display: block;\"></p> \n<h3>4. Solve for the reader.</h3> \n<p>When you're creating content, you have two primary goals: to educate and to help someone solve a problem. While the objective is to generate leads or drive readers toward a purchase, you also want to establish your brand as a trustworthy source of information first. Then, after they’ve come to trust you, readers can convert and turn into paying customers.</p> \n<p>Every piece of content should solve for the reader by answering their questions, offering useful resources and tips, and getting them slowly acquainted with what you offer and how you can help.</p> \n<p>For example, if your brand offers vacation rentals, your content should revolve around travel and provide important information that potential travelers need. You would write city-specific travel guides, lists of best places to visit, lists of best practices for traveling solo, and so forth. Once a reader continues to come to you as an authoritative source of information, they’ll trust you enough to make you their provider.</p> \n<h3>5. Adopt the pillar-cluster model.</h3> \n<p>If you want to create a better reading experience while improving your SEO, organize your content using the <a href=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/marketing/pillar-cluster-model-transform-blog\">pillar-cluster model</a>.</p> \n<p>In this model, a pillar page covers an umbrella topic, then cluster pages support that topic. You then use <a href=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/blog/tabid/6307/bid/31388/how-to-use-internal-linking-to-improve-your-website-s-seo.aspx\">internal linking</a> to connect all the topics together and signal to Google that they’re related.</p> \n<p>For example, if you’re a web design firm, your umbrella topic might be web design. You’d write a pillar page titled, “The Ultimate Guide to Web Design.” Then, you would write pages such as “UX Design 101” and “How to Use HTML &amp; CSS” to support that umbrella topic.</p> \n<h3>6. Write in-depth content.</h3> \n<p>It’s been well-established that, <a href=\"https://www.sweor.com/seocontentlength#:~:text=Longer%20Content%20Produces%20Higher%20Search,search%20queries%20by%20content%20length.&amp;text=The%20first%20result%20typically%20has,10th%20result%20has%202%2C032%20words.\">on average</a>, longer content performs better in search engines than shorter content. So, when writing content for your website, you should make it long — but not just for the sake of it.</p> \n<p>As you seek to solve for the reader, you should include everything they need to know in one post about the specific topic they’re looking for. You shouldn’t write long content with paragraphs upon paragraphs of fluff. Rather, answer related questions and bring up any tips that will help them walk away with all the information they need.</p> \n<p>To find out the types of questions people need answers to, look at the “People also ask” box when you search the keyword you’re targeting. This will tell you the types of queries Google has picked up on that are related to your search.</p> \n<p>Keep in mind that each post or page should only cover one highly specific topic and only target one to two keywords. You’ll want to do this for various reasons:</p> \n<ul> \n <li>You’ll avoid self-cannibalization because you won’t be writing about general topics.</li> \n <li>You’ll strengthen topical authority by writing in-depth content on one specific keyword.</li> \n <li>With less keywords covered per page or post, you’ll have more keywords to target in other pages.</li> \n</ul> \n<h3><img src=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/hs-fs/hubfs/ann-handley-content-marketing-quote.png?width=650&amp;name=ann-handley-content-marketing-quote.png\" alt=\"Content marketing tip by Ann Handley: &quot;You need to create ridiculously good content — content that is useful, enjoyable, and inspired.&quot; \" width=\"650\" style=\"width: 650px; margin-left: auto; margin-right: auto; display: block;\"></h3> \n<h3>7. Rely on analytics to track your performance.</h3> \n<p>Quality content is important, but it doesn't mean much for your business if your visitors and viewers don't convert into customers. This is why analytics is so important — by carefully monitoring, tracking, watching, and reporting on the numbers, you'll be able to gauge what's working, what isn't, and what could be working better.</p> \n<p>Traffic is important, but it's important you also focus on conversion rates. Perhaps your Instagram account has only 1,000 followers — alternatively, your blog has 7,000 readers. However, your Instagram page has a conversion rate of seven percent, and your blog only converts at about .01. This should tell you that, while your blog is important for an initial introduction to your business, your Instagram is critical for sales and shouldn't be ignored.</p> \n<p>Additionally, focusing on analytics will help you refine and improve your strategy for the future. For instance, let's say you notice your blog readers are particularly interested in blog topics related to e-commerce. This can help direct your future strategy — you can choose to focus more heavily on e-commerce topics, which will increase traffic (signaling your readers are happy with your content), and ensure you're spending time and effort where it matters.</p> \n<h3>8. Keep content consistent and up-to-date.</h3> \n<p>Victor Pan, Head of Technical SEO at HubSpot, urges content strategists to implement simple SEO tactics to ensure content remains up-to-date and relevant to search engines. He says, \"You can tell if being up-to-date is important to your topic if 'keyword+year' shows up in the 'related searches' of a Google search result.\"</p> \n<p>To ensure your content remains relevant and updated, Pan recommends the following three tips:</p> \n<ul> \n <li>Exclude the year in the URL when you're optimizing your content. Great URLs don't change.</li> \n <li>Include the year in the title of your content.</li> \n <li>Schedule your editorial calendar to revisit this content every year so you can keep it up-to-date, which could include updating the title tag, meta description, and content itself.</li> \n</ul> \n<p>It's important to note that if you do implement an optimization strategy, it's critical you don't update the URL. The URL should remain the same to ensure you don't need to re-earn backlinks. Additionally, you don't want to create unnecessary redirects.</p> \n<p>Overall, consistency is key. Publishing consistent content will help you rank in the SERPs, but it will also establish trust with your audience.</p> \n<p><img src=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/hs-fs/hubfs/jason-miller-content-marketing-quote.png?width=650&amp;name=jason-miller-content-marketing-quote.png\" alt=\"Content marketing tip by Jason Miller: &quot;Content marketing is no longer a numbers game. It's a game of relevance.&quot; \" width=\"650\" style=\"width: 650px; margin-left: auto; margin-right: auto; display: block;\"></p> \n<h3>9. Adopt a historical optimization strategy.</h3> \n<p>A few years ago, the blogging team at HubSpot figured out the importance of adopting a <a href=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/marketing/historical-blog-seo-conversion-optimization?_ga=2.38279658.81589904.1554671928-644648569.1551722047\">historical optimization strategy</a>. Through repurposing old (yet still high-quality) content, the team was able to double monthly leads, and increase monthly organic search views by an average of 106%.</p> \n<p>Ultimately, you don't want old content to go to waste. If a topic is particularly evergreen (like \"how to create a blog\"), it makes sense you'd put time and effort behind repurposing it.</p> \n<h3>10. Repurpose your content.</h3> \n<p>It takes time and talent to craft highly useful, engaging content — so, by finding ways to recycle existing content, you're ensuring peak efficiency. Additionally, repurposing content allows you to reach new audiences. For instance, let's say your podcast team published a high-performing episode. Why not turn that episode's topic into a blog post?</p> \n<p>Alternatively, maybe you created a blog post that performed significantly well — now, you might consider creating a YouTube video that covers a similar topic to reach an audience that prefers video over text.</p> \n<p>Repurposing your content will also ensure your audience has more than one chance to see it. Your readers, viewers, and followers are busy. Consider simply implementing a new content promotional strategy on a piece of content that deserves to be resurfaced.</p> \n<h3>11. Ensure your brand voice remains steady across channels.</h3> \n<p>Whether you visit Spotify's Twitter page, YouTube account, or stumble across one of its billboard advertisements, you can quickly get a sense for the brand's funny, candid, youthful voice. This is what makes me feel connected to Spotify — its unwavering brand consistency, regardless of the channel on which I choose to engage.</p> \n<div>\n <img src=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/hubfs/The%20Ultimate%20Round-Up%20of%20Content%20Marketing%20Tips.png\" alt=\"\">\n</div> \n<p style=\"text-align: center; font-size: 12px;\"><a href=\"https://www.adweek.com/brand-marketing/spotify-creative-shares-how-the-brand-came-up-with-its-latest-witty-work/\" style=\"font-style: italic;\">Image Source</a></p> \n<p>Even if you have a marketing team of 30, it's critical to produce similar messaging that aligns with your brand's voice and values across channels. A viewer should watch one of your YouTube videos and then click a link to a blog post and think, \"Ah, yes — this is definitely the same company.\"</p> \n<p>If you need help crafting or refining a brand voice, check out <a href=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/marketing/brand-voice?_ga=2.205107673.81589904.1554671928-644648569.1551722047\">How to Find Your Brand's Voice</a>.</p> \n<h3>12. Personalize your content.</h3> \n<p>Have you ever visited a website multiple times, and each time, the experience gets more and more tailored to your tastes? (Think Amazon.)</p> \n<p><a href=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/agency/personalize-website-content\">Personalizing your website content</a> is crucial. Your business doesn't own a social media site, meaning you can't personalize content there based on your follower's behaviors. That's why personalizing your website's content is so important. On your website, you have complete control over what certain users see based on the pages they’ve visited, their dwell time, their account activity, and so on. You can also personalize by device and buyer persona.</p> \n<p>One way you can get started is by including a reorder button on a product page for users who’ve ordered that product before. You can also create a popup that contains a CTA to download a guide that helps them get the most out of the product. To better serve each prospect or customer, consider using <a href=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/marketing/content-mapping-template-personalize-marketing\">content mapping</a>, which will help you figure out which content serves which buyer persona at certain stages of the buyer’s journey.</p> \n<p>You don’t have to implement personalization manually: you can use <a href=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/service/best-personalization-software\">personalization software</a> to trigger certain actions, show certain content, and send personalized emails.</p> \n<h3><img src=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/hs-fs/hubfs/craig-davis-content-marketing-quote.png?width=650&amp;name=craig-davis-content-marketing-quote.png\" alt=\"Content marketing tip by Craig Davis: &quot;We need to stop interrupting what people are interested in and be what people are interested in.&quot; \" width=\"650\" style=\"width: 650px; margin-left: auto; margin-right: auto; display: block;\"></h3> \n<h3>13. Use data to strengthen your points.</h3> \n<p>83% of marketers don’t use data and statistics in their content marketing.</p> \n<p>Just kidding — I made that up. But using data is a great way to highlight the importance of a piece and strengthen your points.</p> \n<p>Using stats and data provides an irresistible hook and allows you to show why one should read the piece in the first place. For example, I opened this piece with stats on how many people are online, highlighting the fact that content marketing can help you reach a large segment of the population.</p> \n<p>The great thing about data is that it can be used both on your website and on social media platforms. Whenever you use one, be sure to tie it into the value of your product or use it to validate your points. For instance, if you’re a water bottle brand, you can write a caption that reads: Did you know that people who don’t regularly drink water are 15X more likely to get dehydrated? Stay hydrated with your [water bottle brand].</p> \n<p>I also made that statistic up, but you see my point: statistics and data can prove the value of the product or substantiate your arguments.</p> \n<p>Whenever you use statistics, be sure to cite recent research (two years at the latest) whenever possible. More importantly, make sure to use factual, accurate data from reputable sources. Data integrity is critical — especially if your blog is widely read.</p> \n<h3>14. Publish original research.</h3> \n<p>Publishing original research can help you look more authoritative and knowledgeable, spurring brand trust and giving your content an edge over your competitors’.</p> \n<p>While you often see Fortune 500 companies undertaking this task, it doesn’t have to be left to big names in the industry. You can publish original data, too, by carrying out surveys of your customers or prompting your followers on social media to take a questionnaire. You can survey them on a variety of product-, service-, or industry-related topics.</p> \n<p>For instance, if you’re a content marketer at a travel agency, you can conduct a survey about the ways people grappled with the lack of traveling opportunities during the pandemic. You can then cite this original research in a blog post about restarting travel plans after the pandemic becomes a thing of the past.</p> \n<h3>15. Go beyond written formats.</h3> \n<p>The rise of video is not about to stop — and with rich video and image packs taking precedence in SERPs, you’d be remiss to not include video in your <a href=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/marketing/content-marketing-strategy-guide\">content marketing strategy</a>.</p> \n<p>Content marketers have long heralded infographics as one of the best multimedia formats to include in blog posts. Indeed, infographics have the advantage of being pinnable and easy to scan. And, while they’re still important, it’s time to diversify.</p> \n<p>Creating a YouTube video is one of the easiest answers, but you don’t necessarily have to go down that route, especially if you’re not sure how to create a <a href=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/marketing/video-marketing\">video marketing strategy</a>. You can also include other formats such as interactive photos, editable code modules, interactive charts and graphs, and more.</p> \n<p><img src=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/hs-fs/hubfs/doug-kessler-content-marketing-quote.png?width=650&amp;name=doug-kessler-content-marketing-quote.png\" alt=\"Content marketing tip by Doug Kessler: &quot;Traditional marketing talks at people. Content marketing talks with them.&quot; \" width=\"650\" style=\"width: 650px; margin-left: auto; margin-right: auto; display: block;\"></p> \n<h3>16. Prioritize the user experience.</h3> \n<p>User experience is king. You can have the most well-written, well-researched piece of content, but if your website’s user experience is buggy, you’ll lose readers and have them bounce off the page — which is a highly negative ranking factor. Most importantly, those are leads that you won’t convert.</p> \n<p>Make sure your site loads quickly, is mobile optimized, and has navigability features such as a table of contents and back-to-top button. Your content should be easy to read on all devices, with a series of clear, consistent headings and a sans-serif typeface.</p> \n<p>Be sure to also optimize for accessibility website standards. You should provide alt text for all images, include captions in videos, offer a high-contrast setting for the website, and ensure that your content can be read out loud by a software.</p> \n<h3>17. Remarket your content.</h3> \n<p>When you repurpose your content, you take a previously-covered topic and turn it into a new format. When you <a href=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/marketing/design-content-remarketing-campaigns\">remarket your content</a>, you take the content that already existed and try to re-engage users who interacted with that content but didn’t convert.</p> \n<p>There are so many variables that aren’t on our side. A visitor may not be looking for your product right at that moment; it may not be their pay day; it may not be the right day. By intentionally remarketing your content to those who’ve already shown an interest, you increase your chances of capturing their interest at just the right time. And that’s what content marketing is all about.</p> \n<h2>Content Marketing Tips for the Modern Marketer</h2> \n<p>Content marketing is here to stay. While it evolves every day, its essence never changes: content marketing is all about the reader, not about the brand. In your content marketing campaigns, seek to know your target audience, serve their needs, and solve their problems, and you’ll soon have an army of brand evangelists who market your brand for you.</p> \n<p><em>Editor's note: This post was originally published in April 2019 and has been updated for comprehensiveness.</em></p> \n<p><a class=\"cta_button\" href=\"https://www.hubspot.com/cs/ci/?pg=870b6a31-0a25-444f-b61e-ff427ef5d5e9&amp;pid=53&amp;ecid=&amp;hseid=&amp;hsic=\"><img class=\"hs-cta-img \" style=\"border-width: 0px; /*hs-extra-styles*/; margin: 0 auto; display: block; margin-top: 20px; margin-bottom: 20px\" alt=\"New Call-to-action\" src=\"https://no-cache.hubspot.com/cta/default/53/870b6a31-0a25-444f-b61e-ff427ef5d5e9.png\" align=\"middle\"></a></p> \n<p></p>  \n<img src=\"https://track.hubspot.com/__ptq.gif?a=53&amp;k=14&amp;r=https%3A%2F%2Fblog.hubspot.com%2Fmarketing%2Fcontent-marketing-tips&amp;bu=https%253A%252F%252Fblog.hubspot.com%252Fmarketing&amp;bvt=rss\" alt=\"\" width=\"1\" height=\"1\" Forsey","articleImgCdnMap":{"https://no-cache.hubspot.com/cta/default/53/a145a75e-59f6-4b51-a482-4f3ea486e740.png":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx27/cdn27@2020_4/2021/04/23/17-35-38-450_f8c910eb1e0201f6.webp","https://blog.hubspot.com/hs-fs/hubfs/seth-godin-content-marketing-quote.png?width=650&name=seth-godin-content-marketing-quote.png":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx15/cdn78@2020_6/2021/04/23/17-35-50-923_ffcb16fa4887f139.webp","https://blog.hubspot.com/hs-fs/hubfs/nate-elliot-content-marketing-quote.png?width=650&name=nate-elliot-content-marketing-quote.png":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx25/cdn71@2020_3/2021/04/23/17-35-50-306_d551e31848bf943a.webp","https://blog.hubspot.com/hs-fs/hubfs/ann-handley-content-marketing-quote.png?width=650&name=ann-handley-content-marketing-quote.png":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx8/cdn32@2020_2/2021/04/23/17-35-49-148_c1fb7c25a76490a4.webp","https://blog.hubspot.com/hs-fs/hubfs/jason-miller-content-marketing-quote.png?width=650&name=jason-miller-content-marketing-quote.png":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx29/cdn63@2020_2/2021/04/23/17-35-48-974_114db0e0e91c1a31.webp","https://blog.hubspot.com/hubfs/The%20Ultimate%20Round-Up%20of%20Content%20Marketing%20Tips.png":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx25/cdn35@2020_2/2021/04/23/17-35-51-174_83e7a7fd60305d30.webp","https://blog.hubspot.com/hs-fs/hubfs/craig-davis-content-marketing-quote.png?width=650&name=craig-davis-content-marketing-quote.png":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx4/cdn52@2020_6/2021/04/23/17-35-50-745_d3ab87148170f7da.webp","https://blog.hubspot.com/hs-fs/hubfs/doug-kessler-content-marketing-quote.png?width=650&name=doug-kessler-content-marketing-quote.png":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx5oss/cdn84@2020_6/2021/04/23/17-35-49-670_02805f87d5b64ec2.webp","https://no-cache.hubspot.com/cta/default/53/870b6a31-0a25-444f-b61e-ff427ef5d5e9.png":null,"https://track.hubspot.com/__ptq.gif?a=53&k=14&r=https%3A%2F%2Fblog.hubspot.com%2Fmarketing%2Fcontent-marketing-tips&bu=https%253A%252F%252Fblog.hubspot.com%252Fmarketing&bvt=rss":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx23/cdn59@2020_1/2021/04/23/17-35-48-838_4136a3063b3b6732.webp"},"publishedOrCreatedDate":1619199338326},{"createdTime":"2021-04-24 01:35:38","updatedTime":"2021-04-24 01:35:38","title":"4 Ways Brands Can Gain Awareness on Clubhouse [+Examples]","link":"https://blog.hubspot.com/marketing/how-brands-use-clubhouse-for-marketing","description":"<p>If you've been on social media, marketing news sites, or the HubSpot Blog lately, you might have heard about Clubhouse.</p>  \n<p>The nearly one-year-old social media platform which allows users to drop into audio-only chat rooms has grown from <a href=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/marketing/what-is-clubhouse?_ga=2.189705379.942201750.1618518861-1283315606.1618518861\">600,000 to 10 million active users in just a few short months</a>. &nbsp;Although the <a href=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/marketing/how-to-use-clubhouse\">app is invite-only</a>, more and more people are gaining access and tuning into discussions related to their industry, hobbies, and other interests each day.</p> \n<p>Users also love Clubhouse for its entertainment factor. When surfing through Clubhouse, you might find celebrities, like <a href=\"https://www.nytimes.com/2021/02/25/technology/clubhouse-audio-app-experience.html\">Joe Rogan</a>, chatting with fellow influencers; <a href=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/marketing/what-is-clubhouse?_ga=2.189705379.942201750.1618518861-1283315606.1618518861\">audio-only musical productions</a>, comedy nights; or even standup comedy events.</p> \n<p>But, when exploring Clubhouse's vast and highly-creative audio rooms as a marketer, you might wonder if and how you can leverage it within your marketing strategy.</p> \n<p>At this point, most Clubhouse content is still highly experimental. However, one major theme to note is that it's users want to hear from people -- not just brands.</p> \n<p>Because Clubhouse's users crave authentic human discussion, they'll likely disengage from rooms that prioritize promotional content over a relatable conversation.</p> \n<p>However, while building brand awareness on an ultra-personal app like Clubhouse takes time, energy, and lots of community management, we're already starting to see brands begin to connect with the channel's growing audience.</p> \n<p>To help marketers who are just learning about Clubhouse, I spent the last few days surfing the app to learn how brands are reaching users. Below I'll highlight four common brand awareness tactics and offer a few actual examples.</p> \n<p><a class=\"cta_button\" href=\"https://www.hubspot.com/cs/ci/?pg=3dc1dfd9-2cb4-4498-8c57-19dbb5671820&amp;pid=53&amp;ecid=&amp;hseid=&amp;hsic=\"><img class=\"hs-cta-img \" style=\"border-width: 0px; /*hs-extra-styles*/; \" alt=\"Download Now: Social Media Trends in 2021 [Free Report]\" src=\"https://no-cache.hubspot.com/cta/default/53/3dc1dfd9-2cb4-4498-8c57-19dbb5671820.png\"></a></p> \n<h2>How Brands Leverage Clubhouse</h2> \n<h3>1. Fireside Chats or Q&amp;As</h3> \n<p>When I first heard about Clubhouse and explored the app, a lot of rooms I dropped into felt like audio-only video calls or webinars where only the hosts began with speaking privileges. To me, it's not surprising that brand-affiliated room creators and moderators have begun to leverage Q&amp;As, panels, and fireside-chat formats to create interactive -- yet well-managed -- discussions on the platform.</p> \n<p>When watching a panel or interview affiliated with a brand, it's often formatted in one of two ways:</p> \n<ul> \n <li>The moderator -- who works for the brand coordinating the room -- asks thought leaders or influencers affiliated with their industry questions. This moderator might also permit audience members to ask questions or come to the stage to the speaker as well.</li> \n <li>An employee or leader from a brand serves as an interviewee or panel member while an influencer that does not work for the brand asks questions or moderates questions from the audience.</li> \n</ul> \n<p>Regardless of which role the brand member holds in the chat, these rooms have very similar formats. They usually begin with the moderator announcing who they are, who they'll be talking to, and the topic of the room. From there, the moderator will either ask questions to the speakers or giving speaking privileges to other users who raise their hands.</p> \n<p>Below I'll highlight two examples of rooms I've seen. Because Clubhouse is still invite-only and positioned as a safe space for communities to discuss thoughts, topics, or ideas, I will only note key parts of the conversations and room formats. I also did not record these rooms.</p> \n<p>Below are two recent fireside chat examples:</p> \n<h4>Coinbase</h4> \n<p>A recent Clubhouse room, shown below, featured an interview with <a href=\"https://www.coinbase.com/plp/nar3?utm_source=google_search_b&amp;utm_medium=cpc&amp;utm_campaign=1711534994&amp;utm_content=68048698078&amp;utm_term=coinbase&amp;utm_creative=409186026435&amp;cb_device=c&amp;cb_placement=&amp;cb_country=us&amp;cb_city=open&amp;cb_language=en_us&amp;gclid=Cj0KCQiA1KiBBhCcARIsAPWqoSp23MoI-xsL96keTFSV7Qn3_exrSyCcBznpfnOKNchkT2ugtu-ryUUaApM5EALw_wcB\">Coinbase</a>&nbsp;Co-Founder and CEO <a href=\"https://www.linkedin.com/in/barmstrong/\">Brian Armstrong</a>. During the room, Sriram Krishman, a moderator from the club Good Time, asked Armstrong questions about how he got started in bitcoin and grew his company. They also discussed the future of cyber currency. Krishman, also invited listeners to raise their hands and ask questions to Armstrong to create more discussion around the complex cyber topic.</p> \n<p style=\"text-align: center;\"><img alt=\"Clubhouse Room description for an event where the CEO of Coinbase is interviewed by the Club Good Time\" src=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/hs-fs/hubfs/Google%20Drive%20Integration/4%20Ways%20Brands%20Can%20Boost%20Awareness%20on%20Clubhouse%20%5B+Examples%5D.png?width=200&amp;height=433&amp;name=4%20Ways%20Brands%20Can%20Boost%20Awareness%20on%20Clubhouse%20%5B+Examples%5D.png\" style=\"margin-left: auto; margin-right: auto; display: block;\" title=\"\" width=\"200\" height=\"433\"></p> \n<p>In rooms like the one above, users can learn more about a brand like Coinbase and ask its leader questions about the company or its industry. Through this experience, Coinbase and other brands could boost both company awareness and credibility with audiences who tune in to hear their canned, unedited discussion.</p> \n<h4>HubSpot</h4> \n<p>Recently, HubSpot also launched a fireside chat-styled room where our <a href=\"https://www.linkedin.com/in/kippbodnar/\">Chief Marketing Officer Kipp Bodnar</a>, <a href=\"https://www.hubspot.com/company/management/dharmesh-shah?_ga=2.89108243.942201750.1618518861-1283315606.1618518861\">CTO and Co-Founder Dharmesh Shah</a>, and <a href=\"https://www.linkedin.com/in/kieranjflanagan/?originalSubdomain=ie\">Sr. VP of Marketing Kieran Flanagan</a>&nbsp;invited prominent Clubhouse influencers including <a href=\"https://twitter.com/iambomanix?lang=en\">Bomani X</a>&nbsp;to discuss \"The Future of Marketing and Clubhouse.\"</p> \n<p>During the panel, Bodnar asked the Clubhouse influencers a few questions related to how they’ve grown their audiences on the platform; what they’ve done to optimize their profile, rooms, or clubs; and brand awareness etiquette. He also took similar questions or comments from a vast group of listeners including a weight-loss business founder, a scientist, and a Rubix cube enthusiast looking to build Clubhouse communities.</p> \n<p style=\"text-align: center;\"><img alt=\"The Future of Marketing on Clubhouse Room hosted by HubSpot\" src=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/hubfs/Google%20Drive%20Integration/4%20Ways%20Brands%20Can%20Boost%20Awareness%20on%20Clubhouse%20%5B+Examples%5D-4.png\" style=\"margin-left: auto; margin-right: auto; display: block;\" title=\"\"></p> \n<p>While HubSpot's leaders haven't claimed to be Clubhouse experts yet, they created a room to highlight what they know so far and connect listeners with some of Clubhouse's high-profile early-adopters of the app with millions of followers. This is a great example of how the brand positions itself as a marketing thought leader even when they're experimenting with a new, unique platform.</p> \n<h3>2. Sponsoring Room Events</h3> \n<p>While people might not want to join a room that discusses a product or brand positively the entire time, they might enter an interesting conversation or Clubhouse event that is sponsored by a brand.</p> \n<p>When you drop into a sponsored room, you might not hear speakers from the brand speak much -- or at all. However, when reintroducing the room, a speaker might mention that the room or Clubhouse audio experience is paid for or sponsored by the brand. You might also see a sponsor listed in the room's title or description.</p> \n<p>Below is one interesting example:</p> \n<h4>Yummy</h4> \n<p>Below is an example of a scheduled event sponsored by <a href=\"https://www.yummy.com/\">Yummy</a>, a California-based grocery delivery app. During the room-based event -- scheduled for June 5 -- contestants will compete for a $100 Yummy gift card by performing an audio talent, such as singing or playing music.</p> \n<p style=\"text-align: center;\"><img alt=\"Clubhouse Talent Show Room Description noting that the event is sponsored by Yummy\" src=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/hubfs/Google%20Drive%20Integration/4%20Ways%20Brands%20Can%20Boost%20Awareness%20on%20Clubhouse%20%5B+Examples%5D-1.png\" style=\"margin-left: auto; margin-right: auto; display: block;\" title=\"\"></p> \n<p>By sponsoring an experimental performance contest on Clubhouse, Yummy not only gets to see how creative Clubhouse content could benefit their brand, but they also promote their delivery service to a large pool of Clubhouse users who are interested in audio entertainment or music.</p> \n<h3>3. Having team members participate in rooms related to your industry.</h3> \n<p>Another way brands can grow awareness is by having chief officers, leaders, or even general employees raise their hands and actively participate by speaking in rooms with large audiences.</p> \n<p>When speaking in a room, brand representatives don't necessarily need to talk all about their company. However, by adding to a conversation, talking about tactics they've tried at their role, and showing off their expertise, audience members learn to trust them and their company. As company members gain a following and fanbase, their brand might also gain a new audience.</p> \n<p>Below are two examples of brands that are embracing room participation.</p> \n<h4>Tax Nation LLC.</h4> \n<p>In a recent room titled \"Marketing That Works in 2021 (so far)\", moderators asked listeners to raise their hands and offer their best marketing tips.</p> \n<p style=\"text-align: center;\"><img alt=\"Marketing That Works Clubhouse Room\" src=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/hubfs/Google%20Drive%20Integration/4%20Ways%20Brands%20Can%20Boost%20Awareness%20on%20Clubhouse%20%5B+Examples%5D-Apr-15-2021-08-34-52-23-PM.png\" style=\"margin-left: auto; margin-right: auto; display: block;\" title=\"\"></p> \n<p>During the room, <a href=\"https://www.linkedin.com/in/cory-hughes-8516a364/\">Cory Hughes</a>, Vice President and Managing Partner of the tax preparation business, <a href=\"https://www.bbb.org/us/tx/arlington/profile/tax-return-preparation/tax-nation-usa-llc-0825-235977468\">Tax Nation LLC</a>, was chosen to speak. He mentioned his company by name and explained that they create marketing content based on \"stories\" and positive feedback from \"happy customers.\"</p> \n<p>After Hughes made his point, a few other listeners chimed in to agree with how important his tip was.</p> \n<p>Not only did Hughes offer valuable advice to participants, but he naturally mentioned his company and its happy customers without sounding like he was trying to plug his tax preparation product.</p> \n<h4>Start Scale Sail</h4> \n<p>In another room, titled \"Scale Your Business With Digital Products,\" hosted by business consultant <a href=\"https://www.instagram.com/almajbradford/?hl=en\">Alma Bradford</a>, entrepreneurs, marketers, and consultants shared tips for growing brands based on their experience,</p> \n<p>For example, <a href=\"https://www.linkedin.com/in/natasha-o-banion-2bb237203/https://www.linkedin.com/in/natasha-o-banion-2bb237203/\">Natasha O'Banion</a>, CEO of <a href=\"https://www.startscalesail.com/\">Start Scale Sail</a>, a business automation and consulting firm, explained that she was a big fan of quiz content and added that her team's successfully generated leads through interactive content.</p> \n<p style=\"text-align: center;\"><img alt=\"Scale Your Business with Digital Products Clubhouse Room\" src=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/hs-fs/hubfs/Google%20Drive%20Integration/4%20Ways%20Brands%20Can%20Boost%20Awareness%20on%20Clubhouse%20%5B+Examples%5D-2.png?width=286&amp;name=4%20Ways%20Brands%20Can%20Boost%20Awareness%20on%20Clubhouse%20%5B+Examples%5D-2.png\" style=\"margin-left: auto; margin-right: auto; display: block;\" title=\"\" width=\"286\"></p> \n<p>Although O'Banion didn't plug her company by name, her explanation of how she's used quizzes in her own strategy led to questions and more discussion from other attendees. Because she gave valuable input, listeners with similar interests in digital lead generation might be interested in following her or even learning more about her brand.</p> \n<h3>4. Hosting informal chats</h3> \n<p>Because Clubhouse is all about discussion and authenticity, many brands have also tried to show their human side and seem more accessible to audiences by hosting informal chats with no obvious goal or topic. This method is more casual, and potentially less intimidating, for listeners who might not raise their hand to speak in a fireside chat with a full agenda.</p> \n<p>Below is one example:</p> \n<h4>DRK Beauty</h4> \n<p>One brand that hosts inviting, casual rooms is <a href=\"https://thisisdrkbeauty.com/\">DRK Beauty,</a>&nbsp;a website and commerce platform for people of color, which regularly publishes content around mental health, fashion, beauty, lifestyle, and culture.</p> \n<p>At the end of each week, DRK's team hosts \"Weekly Wine Down\" rooms aimed to feel like visiting a bar with colleagues or friends at the end of a long week.</p> \n<p>While DRK rooms, often hosted by <a href=\"https://www.linkedin.com/in/misswilmamae/\">DRK Beauty CEO Wilma Mae Basta</a>, don't have a set topic or agenda, the team often introduces themselves as speakers, begins a casual conversation about whatever is on their minds, and allows other audience members to raise their hands and chime in at any time.</p> \n<p style=\"text-align: center;\"><img alt=\"Weekly Wine Down description with hosts from DRK Beauty\" src=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/hs-fs/hubfs/Google%20Drive%20Integration/4%20Ways%20Brands%20Can%20Boost%20Awareness%20on%20Clubhouse%20%5B+Examples%5D-3.png?width=228&amp;height=493&amp;name=4%20Ways%20Brands%20Can%20Boost%20Awareness%20on%20Clubhouse%20%5B+Examples%5D-3.png\" style=\"margin-left: auto; margin-right: auto; display: block;\" title=\"\" width=\"228\" height=\"493\"></p> \n<p>While DRK Beauty rooms aren't usually aimed to promote the brand's site, DRK still enables its audience and prospective web visitors to learn about the people behind the company in a casual, authentic setting. This makes the brand seem <a href=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/marketing/social-media-predictions-2017?_ga=2.135302969.942201750.1618518861-1283315606.1618518861\">accessible, authentic, and trustworthy</a>, three things <a href=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/marketing/social-media-predictions-2017?_ga=2.135302969.942201750.1618518861-1283315606.1618518861\">social media users value</a>&nbsp;when researching brands in 2021.</p> \n<h2>The key to Clubhouse? Be human.</h2> \n<p>It's key to remember that Clubhouse is all about authentic human connection, not branding or self-promotion.</p> \n<p>While <a href=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/marketing/what-is-clubhousehttps://blog.hubspot.com/marketing/what-is-clubhouse?_ga=2.94259605.942201750.1618518861-1283315606.1618518861\">Clubhouse began as a platform where users could only hear from industry \"elites,\"</a>&nbsp;the app's now open to a wide range of creatives and every-day people who want to communicate or interact with others. Because of this, learning about a brand is likely not the first thing a user wants to do when logging on to the app.</p> \n<p>Regardless of which strategy you use on Clubhouse, remember to embrace the human side of the app. For example, rather than hosting a room where you explain your brand or products to audiences, consider hosting a fireside chat with a thought leader in your industry or participate in a room that allows you to discuss your industry with others in it.</p> \n<p>While focusing on natural conversation and valuable room participation won't enable you to outright market your product all the time, leaning into the platform's conversational and personal nature could help you grow a following that trusts your expertise -- and eventually -- your brand.</p> \n<p>Want to learn more about the latest social media marketing trends? Check out the free resource below.</p> \n<p><a class=\"cta_button\" href=\"https://www.hubspot.com/cs/ci/?pg=5fc2491c-cd3c-4adb-ad3c-b082ce2793d3&amp;pid=53&amp;ecid=&amp;hseid=&amp;hsic=\"><img x33/cdn8@2020_4/2021/04/23/17-35-48-675_c9845f80cf0e1a36.webp","https://no-cache.hubspot.com/cta/default/53/5fc2491c-cd3c-4adb-ad3c-b082ce2793d3.png":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx15/cdn52@2020_6/2021/04/23/17-35-50-205_73ab6e288063122a.webp","https://track.hubspot.com/__ptq.gif?a=53&k=14&r=https%3A%2F%2Fblog.hubspot.com%2Fmarketing%2Fhow-brands-use-clubhouse-for-marketing&bu=https%253A%252F%252Fblog.hubspot.com%252Fmarketing&bvt=rss":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx7/cdn100@2020_4/2021/04/23/17-35-48-908_313c3aed3f2aa809.webp"},"publishedOrCreatedDate":1619199338326},{"createdTime":"2021-04-24 01:35:38","updatedTime":"2021-04-24 01:35:38","title":"Hulu Introduces New Ad Tool for SMBs: What Marketers Need to Know","link":"https://blog.hubspot.com/marketing/hulu-advertising","description":"<p>Hulu gave us \"<a href=\"https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=81PyH5TH-NQ\">The Handmaid's Tale</a>,\" then gave us \"<a href=\"https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=k2nC7bepGpk\">Little Fires Everywhere</a>.\" So, personally, I don't need another reason to love the streaming platform. But if I had a small business, I would have just gotten one.</p> \n<p>In July 2020, Hulu announced <a href=\"https://home.admanager.hulu.com/\">Hulu Ad Manager</a><a href=\"https://home.admanager.hulu.com/\">,</a> a self-service advertising platform designed for smaller advertisers with limited budgets.</p> \n<p><a class=\"cta_button\" href=\"https://www.hubspot.com/cs/ci/?pg=da1bfbbd-7ee9-4bf1-89d1-6d7a833deb08&amp;pid=53&amp;ecid=&amp;hseid=&amp;hsic=\"><img class=\"hs-cta-img \" style=\"border-width: 0px; /*hs-extra-styles*/; \" alt=\"Download Now: Free Ad Campaign Planning Kit\" src=\"https://no-cache.hubspot.com/cta/default/53/da1bfbbd-7ee9-4bf1-89d1-6d7a833deb08.png\"></a></p> \n<p>Previously, Hulu ads were only accessible to top brands with the finances to fund large campaigns. Now, small- and mid-size businesses (SMBs) can reach the platform's 92 million ad-supported viewers without dishing out thousands of dollars.</p> \n<p>So, how exactly does the Ad Manager work? We'll cover that and more below.</p> \n<h2>How to Use Hulu's Ad Service</h2> \n<p>Currently, Hulu's self-service solution is in the beta phase.</p> \n<p>To access the platform as a beta user, you must first <a href=\"https://home.admanager.hulu.com/rsvp/\">submit an RSVP form</a> with information on your business.</p> \n<p><img alt=\"Hulu Ad Manager RSVP page\" src=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/hubfs/Google%20Drive%20Integration/Hulu%20Now%20Offers%20Advertising%20Tools%20for%20SMBs%20What%20Marketers%20Need%20to%20Know-1.jpeg\" style=\"margin-left: auto; margin-right: auto; display: block;\" title=\"\"></p> \n<p>If accepted, setting up your ad is easy. Here are the steps.</p> \n<h3>1. Select the dates within which you want to run your ad campaign.</h3> \n<h3>2. Build your audience.</h3> \n<p>On Hulu Ad Manager, you can target users by age, interest, gender, location, and of course show genre. When it comes to location, you can narrow it down by state, city, ZIP code, or a designated marketing area (DMA).</p> \n<p>However, you cannot select which shows you want your ads to run on, only the genre. If you're not sure what will align best with your brand, look through the current show selections to get an idea of what to expect.</p> \n<h3>3. Set your budget.</h3> \n<p>To run an ad on Hulu, you must have a minimum budget of $500 per campaign, which is considerably less than the usual cost of ads on streaming platforms. For comparison, <a href=\"https://advertising.amazon.com/solutions/products/video-ads?ref_=a20m_us_p_va_anchr_outstrm#out-stream\">Amazon's self-service platform for video ads</a> typically requires a minimum ad spend of $35,000.</p> \n<h3>4. Upload your video ad.</h3> \n<p>There are a few requirements your ad must meet to be approved:</p> \n<ul> \n <li>Be between 15 to 30 seconds long</li> \n <li>Formatted in MP4 or MOV</li> \n <li>Be in HD and have stereo sound</li> \n <li>Fit the <a href=\"https://home.admanager.hulu.com/tech-specs-for-video-ads/\">tech specs </a>outlined by Hulu</li> \n <li>Comply with <a href=\"https://home.admanager.hulu.com/terms/#3-ads-and-campaigns\">Hulu's advertising policies</a>.</li> \n</ul> \n<p>The approval process usually takes up to three business days.</p> \n<h3>5. Make a payment.</h3> \n<p>Currently, Hulu doesn't accept business bank accounts or debit cards for payments. You must use a credit card. If you choose to pause or cancel your campaign, you will only pay for the delivered impressions.</p> \n<h3>6. Track your ad performance.</h3> \n<p>Once your ad is live, you can start tracking its performance in the Hulu Ad Manager.</p> \n<p>Note that you will not be able to find out what times your ad aired and during which shows. However, you can expect to find standard metrics, such as impressions and clicks.</p> \n<h2>Hulu Advertising Options</h2> \n<p>In addition to Hulu's most recent self-service option, the streaming service also offers two other advertising options:</p> \n<ul> \n <li><strong>Premium Programmatic</strong> – This is ideal for brands who want to leverage lookalike audiences, audience CRM matching, and behavioral segmenting in their campaign.</li> \n <li><strong>Action With Broad Appeal </strong>– With this option, you can integrate your brand with Hulu's, create branded content collections, and deliver ads in innovative formats.</li> \n</ul> \n<p>Each option caters to your brand's specific goals and can be designed to fit your budget.</p> \n<p>For instance, you can run brand lift studies, which are ads designed to measure consumer perception of your brand after a campaign.</p> \n<p><a href=\"https://www.linkedin.com/in/jillianricciardelli/\">Jillian Hope</a>, senior marketing manager of brand advertising at HubSpot, explains that they can help brand advertisers understand the impact Hulu campaign exposure has on key brand KPIs.</p> \n<h2>Pros and Cons of Hulu Ads</h2> \n<h3>Pro: Hulu has extensive targeting capabilities.</h3> \n<p>With any one of the three advertising options available on Hulu, you can use Hulu's targeting features to reach your ideal viewers.</p> \n<p>\"[You have] the ability to define target audiences using Hulu's first-party audience data or leverage lookalike audiences using your own first-party data,\" said Hope.</p> \n<p>The extent of the targeting parameters will depend on which option you are using. For instance, if you are using programmatic buying, you can use lookalike audiences to match the exact users you're looking for with Hulu's viewers.</p> \n<p>However, on the current beta version of the self-service solution, you can only target users by demographic and show genre.</p> \n<p>Despite this, Hope adds that targeting on a platform like Hulu is much more advanced than it would be with traditional, linear TV.</p> \n<h3>Pro: Innovative ad formats allow you to experiment.</h3> \n<p>On Hulu, you're only limited to video commercials if you're using the self-service option. The platform offers over 15 ad products to reach viewers.</p> \n<p><strong>\"</strong>There are multiple ad formats available and lots of innovation happening,\" said Hope. \"For example, [there's the] new QR code integration that is more desirable to direct response advertisers.\"</p> \n<p>It's just a matter of figuring out which ad product best aligns with your goals.</p> \n<p>For instance, there's the cover story brand placement, which allows you to seamlessly integrate your branding on Hulu's homepage.</p> \n<p><img alt=\"Hulu Ad Manager Ad Product Example\" src=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/hubfs/Google%20Drive%20Integration/Hulu%20Now%20Offers%20Advertising%20Tools%20for%20SMBs%20What%20Marketers%20Need%20to%20Know-2.jpeg\" style=\"margin-left: auto; margin-right: auto; display: block;\" title=\"\"></p> \n<p style=\"text-align: center; font-size: 12px;\"><a href=\"https://advertising.hulu.com/ad-products/cover-story-brand-placement/\">Image Source</a></p> \n<p>Then, there's the ad selector, which puts the power back in the consumers hands by letting them select which ad they want to see.</p> \n<p><img alt=\"Hulu Ad Manager Ad Selector \" src=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/hs-fs/hubfs/Google%20Drive%20Integration/Hulu%20Now%20Offers%20Advertising%20Tools%20for%20SMBs%20What%20Marketers%20Need%20to%20Know.jpeg?width=562&amp;name=Hulu%20Now%20Offers%20Advertising%20Tools%20for%20SMBs%20What%20Marketers%20Need%20to%20Know.jpeg\" style=\"margin-left: auto; margin-right: auto; display: block;\" title=\"\" width=\"562\"></p> \n<p style=\"text-align: center; font-size: 12px;\"><a href=\"https://advertising.hulu.com/ad-products/ad-selector/\">Image Source</a></p> \n<p>These are just a few of the ad formats you can pick from, each one creating a different experience for the user. To see all the ad formats available on Hulu, visit Hulu's <a href=\"https://advertising.hulu.com/ad-products/\">ad product page</a>.</p> \n<h3>Con: You can only accomplish so much with a limited budget.</h3> \n<p>One of the downsides of Hulu ads is that certain campaigns will require a bigger budget than you may have available.</p> \n<p>\"Some of the more premium ad placements, as well as brand lift studies, require budget minimums in order to reach statistical significance,\" said Hope. \"So, they are less attainable to smaller advertisers.\"</p> \n<p>In this case, Hulu may not be the best platform on which to run these types of campaigns. You may want to opt for another ad platform, like Facebook Ads, where you can reach more users who still fall within your target audience for less money.</p> \n<h2>How Hulu Ad Examples Can Inform Your Next Campaign</h2> \n<p>If you're not ready to pull the trigger on a Hulu campaign, get inspiration in the meantime.</p> \n<p>See how other brands – notably your competitors – are using the platform to reach their target audience. This means looking at their creative, reviewing case studies, and monitoring consumer sentiment via social media.</p> \n<p>This competitive intelligence can help you devise a strategy during the ideation phase of your campaign.</p> \n<p>Given that the Hulu Ad Manager is still in beta, the platform will likely include more features once it fully launches. In the meantime, SMBs can reach TV viewers for a fraction of what it used to cost.</p> \n<p><a class=\"cta_button\" href=\"https://www.hubspot.com/cs/ci/?pg=46d72524-f4a7-44e9-9af0-935be9bb3891&amp;pid=53&amp;ecid=&amp;hseid=&amp;hsic=\"><img class=\"hs-cta-img \" style=\"border-width: 0px; /*hs-extra-styles*/; \"
