Bretous)","articleImgCdnMap":{"https://no-cache.hubspot.com/cta/default/53/da1bfbbd-7ee9-4bf1-89d1-6d7a833deb08.png":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx30/cdn13@2020_6/2021/04/23/17-35-38-453_91a8856cb36791e3.webp","https://blog.hubspot.com/hubfs/Google%20Drive%20Integration/Hulu%20Now%20Offers%20Advertising%20Tools%20for%20SMBs%20What%20Marketers%20Need%20to%20Know-1.jpeg":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx33/cdn56@2020_3/2021/04/23/17-35-50-842_18e56caf50acd8e0.webp","https://blog.hubspot.com/hubfs/Google%20Drive%20Integration/Hulu%20Now%20Offers%20Advertising%20Tools%20for%20SMBs%20What%20Marketers%20Need%20to%20Know-2.jpeg":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx31/cdn63@2020_4/2021/04/23/17-35-49-813_80fab8389b881f07.webp","https://blog.hubspot.com/hs-fs/hubfs/Google%20Drive%20Integration/Hulu%20Now%20Offers%20Advertising%20Tools%20for%20SMBs%20What%20Marketers%20Need%20to%20Know.jpeg?width=562&name=Hulu%20Now%20Offers%20Advertising%20Tools%20for%20SMBs%20What%20Marketers%20Need%20to%20Know.jpeg":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx14/cdn54@2020_5/2021/04/23/17-35-49-172_7043802b36129b57.webp","https://no-cache.hubspot.com/cta/default/53/46d72524-f4a7-44e9-9af0-935be9bb3891.png":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx23/cdn83@2020_1/2021/04/23/17-35-49-960_8e21eaa098288b31.webp","https://track.hubspot.com/__ptq.gif?a=53&k=14&r=https%3A%2F%2Fblog.hubspot.com%2Fmarketing%2Fhulu-advertising&bu=https%253A%252F%252Fblog.hubspot.com%252Fmarketing&bvt=rss":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx19/cdn11@2020_5/2021/04/23/17-35-48-172_dba8891e2cf07026.webp"},"publishedOrCreatedDate":1619199338326},{"createdTime":"2021-04-24 01:35:38","updatedTime":"2021-04-24 01:35:38","title":"19 Best Practices for Webinars or Webcasts","link":"https://blog.hubspot.com/blog/tabid/6307/bid/2391/10-best-practices-for-webinars-or-webcasts.aspx","description":"<div class=\"hs-migrated-cms-post\"> \n <p>Webinars are a highly effective tool for moving prospects along the sales funnel.</p> \n <p>After you’ve loaded them with product and industry knowledge, your prospects become warm leads who can then have fruitful conversations with your sales team. But here’s the thing: the content and execution of the <a href=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/marketing/what-is-a-webinar\">webinar</a> affect prospects’ experience and will impact the quality of the <a href=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/marketing/beginner-inbound-lead-generation-guide-ht?_ga=2.210068755.746190466.1616611928-2127255386.1616611928\">leads you generate</a>.</p> \n <p>If the information is misaligned with your prospects’ needs, you risk deterring them from doing further business with you. If the webinar is boring or too long, you may lose prospects before you deliver your final product pitch at the end.</p> \n <p>If you don’t place the appropriate calls-to-action at the right time, you may not get enough attendees or fail to prove the ROI to your company’s leadership team.</p> \n <p>When <a href=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/marketing/are-webinars-dead-how-to-make-a-webinar\">creating a webinar</a>, the stakes are high. That’s why using a <a href=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/marketing/webinar-planning-list\">webinar planning list</a> and following best practices is essential. Below, I go over the best practices for creating webinar invites and share top tips for hosting webcasts.</p> \n <p><a class=\"cta_button\" href=\"https://www.hubspot.com/cs/ci/?pg=96a2a16e-e138-4855-a967-1a190b6c0692&amp;pid=53&amp;ecid=&amp;hseid=&amp;hsic=\"><img class=\"hs-cta-img \" style=\"border-width: 0px; /*hs-extra-styles*/; margin: 0 auto; display: block; margin-top: 20px; margin-bottom: 20px\" alt=\"Download Now: Free Webinar Planning Kit\" src=\"https://no-cache.hubspot.com/cta/default/53/96a2a16e-e138-4855-a967-1a190b6c0692.png\" align=\"middle\" /></a></p> \n <h2>Webinar Invite Best Practices</h2> \n <p>In some ways, inviting people to come to your webinar is the toughest part.</p> \n <p>Typically, you’ll send a formal invitation over email. You can <a href=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/blog/tabid/6307/bid/33540/18-ways-to-guarantee-nobody-misses-your-next-webinar.aspx\">promote the webinar</a> via your company’s social media profiles, your LinkedIn, your website, and even your blog — but the webinar invite will be delivered over email.</p> \n <p>With this email, you have one goal: to communicate your event’s value so that prospects have no choice but to sign up.</p> \n <p>Let’s go over how you can do that.</p> \n <h3>1. Create a short sentence with your value proposition.</h3> \n <p>Before ever sitting down to write your webinar invitation email, you should sum up what your attendees will get out of your event in one short sentence. This will be your guidepost as you write the invitation.</p> \n <h3>2. Craft a subject line that shows the value of the event.</h3> \n <p>Next, it’s time to write a subject line that showcases the skills and tools attendees will walk away with. Don’t forget to include the word “webinar” in the subject line.</p> \n <p><strong>Here are some good examples</strong>:</p> \n <ul> \n  <li>[Webinar] Grow Your Brand 3X with This Proven Method by [Industry Leader]</li> \n  <li>[Webinar] Learn How to Close More Deals with [Industry Leader]</li> \n  <li>[Webinar] Want Your Company to Become the Next Apple?</li> \n </ul> \n <p><strong>Here are some so-so webinar subject lines you should avoid using</strong>:</p> \n <ul> \n  <li>You’re Invited to a Can’t-Miss Customer Service Webinar</li> \n  <li>Come to Our Marketing Webinar on February 15</li> \n  <li>Don’t Miss Our Next Webinar About Social Media Strategies</li> \n </ul> \n <h3>3. Include an engaging banner image.</h3> \n <p>Your banner image should include the title of the webinar and a clear call-to-action. You could also include the date and time, but that’s optional. Keep it light on text.</p> \n <p>Here’s an excellent example from Elementor, a WordPress plugin.</p> \n <p><img src=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/hs-fs/hubfs/elementor-webinar-invite-banner.jpeg?width=650&amp;name=elementor-webinar-invite-banner.jpeg\" alt=\"Elementor webinar invite header\" width=\"650\" style=\"width: 650px; margin-left: auto; margin-right: auto; display: block;\" /></p> \n <p>This is a great example because it features high-contrast lettering and the word “webinar” in the upper right-hand corner. Most importantly, it has a call-to-action button that says “Save Your Seat.” <a href=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/blog/tabid/6307/bid/2391/10-best-practices-for-webinars-or-webcasts.aspx#webinar-invite-cta\">Every webinar invite should include a CTA</a>.</p> \n <h3>4. Include a header that makes your event’s value clear.</h3> \n <p>In an email, the header acts as a title that comes right after the banner. The header can be the title of your webinar or be the same as the subject line. Either way, it should communicate the value of the event. What will people learn? How will they grow?</p> \n <p>Your invitees should immediately be able to tell based on the header alone.</p> \n <p><strong>Here are some great examples</strong>:</p> \n <ul> \n  <li>Webinar: Learn How to Boost Sales with 5 Simple Tricks</li> \n  <li>Want to Double Your Organic Traffic? Find Out How in This Webinar</li> \n  <li>These Proven Strategies Will Triple Your Conversion Rates</li> \n </ul> \n <p><strong>Here are some so-so examples</strong>:</p> \n <ul> \n  <li>Join Our SEO Webinar on May 15th</li> \n  <li>Sales Training Seminar by [Company]</li> \n  <li>Leadership Innovation Summit with [Industry Leader]</li> \n </ul> \n <h3>5. Include a brief description of the event.</h3> \n <p>Right after the header, include two to three sentences describing the event. The description should briefly outline a challenge and establish the insights and tips that will help attendees surmount those challenges. Alternatively, you can identify a goal, then tell attendees how the webinar will help them achieve those goals.</p> \n <p>Remember: value is the name of the game here. People won’t spend an hour on just anything, so make it clear why your webinar is worth their while.</p> \n <p><strong>Here’s a great example from HubSpot</strong>:</p> \n <p>“Creating an outstanding customer journey is a challenge felt by many marketing, sales, and customer service teams. A great experience is always the end goal, but the path to success isn't always clear. On March 2nd, join CX Spotlight and learn how to better market, sell, and service your audience.”</p> \n <p>This example is great because it tells attendees, in no uncertain terms, the insights they’ll walk away with.</p> \n <p><strong>Here’s a so-so example</strong>:</p> \n <p>“Come to our exclusive webinar on February 5th, where we discuss everything in the industry, including email marketing, SEO, and social media. Your host, XYZ, is an industry veteran with 20 years of experience. The presentation will cover key topics and trends happening in marketing today. Don’t miss it.”</p> \n <p>This is a poor example because of three reasons. First, it’s too general; second, it doesn’t identify a challenge or a goal (such as growing organic traffic or creating a great customer experience); and third, it doesn’t tell attendees the skills they’ll gain from the event.</p> \n <h3>6. Include a list of bullet points telling people what they’ll learn.</h3> \n <p>Now that you’ve provided an overview of the event, feel free to include more detail about what attendees will learn throughout the webinar.</p> \n <p><strong>Here’s a great example from HubSpot</strong>:</p> \n <p>“In this webinar, we're focusing on the data that really matters when it comes to business growth. Our panel will discuss:</p> \n <ul> \n  <li>What info you should be gathering across your web, chat, and email assets</li> \n  <li>How to stay organized with this new influx of data</li> \n  <li>Best practices for personalizing the buying experience”</li> \n </ul> \n <p>Notice how the bullet points address the attendee directly, telling them what they’ll learn and how they can apply it in their role.</p> \n <a></a> \n <h3>7. Seal the deal with a call-to-action button.</h3> \n <p>All throughout the email, you’ve constantly communicated the value of your event. Now, it’s time to invite your prospects to sign up with a clear, high-contrast <a href=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/marketing/what-is-call-to-action-faqs-ht\">call-to-action button</a>.</p> \n <p><strong>Consider using the following phrases</strong>:</p> \n <ul> \n  <li>Save your seat</li> \n  <li>Register now</li> \n  <li>Register today</li> \n  <li>Claim your spot</li> \n </ul> \n <p>Now that you know the best practices for webinar invites, let’s go over best practices for running your webinar. Use this <a href=\"https://offers.hubspot.com/sales-marketing-webinar-alignment\">webinar planning kit</a> to make sure you’re following all the steps.</p> \n <h3 style=\"text-align: center;\">Featured Resource: <a href=\"https://offers.hubspot.com/sales-marketing-webinar-alignment\">Webinar Planning Kit </a></h3> \n <p><a href=\"https://offers.hubspot.com/sales-marketing-webinar-alignment\"><img src=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/hs-fs/hubfs/webinar-planning-kit.jpeg?width=650&amp;name=webinar-planning-kit.jpeg\" alt=\"The Ultimate Webinar Planning Kit\" width=\"650\" style=\"width: 650px; margin-left: auto; margin-right: auto; display: block;\" /></a></p> \n <p style=\"text-align: center;\"><a href=\"https://offers.hubspot.com/sales-marketing-webinar-alignment\">Download Your Free Kit Now</a></p> \n <h3>1. Schedule your webinar for 60 minutes.</h3> \n <p>How long should your webinar be? The answer is one hour. It’s a well-known fact that 60 minutes is the optimal length of a webinar, with the average viewing time being 56 minutes (<a href=\"https://communications.on24.com/rs/848-AHN-047/images/ON24_benchmarks_20200309.pdf\">ON24</a>).</p> \n <h3>2. Host it on Wednesday or Thursday at 10 AM or 11 AM.</h3> \n <p>Both <a href=\"https://communications.on24.com/rs/848-AHN-047/images/ON24_benchmarks_20200309.pdf\">ON24</a> and <a href=\"https://logmeincdn.azureedge.net/gotomeetingmedia/-/media/pdfs/gotowebinar-the-big-book-of-webinar-stats-final.pdf\">GoToWebinar</a> report that Wednesdays and Thursdays are the best days to deliver your event. As far as time, 10 AM and 11 AM have long been established as top performers in both attendee engagement and attendance rates.</p> \n <h3>3. Send reminder emails.</h3> \n <p>Leading up to the webinar, send a reminder email twice — one day before the event and one hour before the event. Your webinar platform should also offer the option to automatically send these reminders to those who’ve signed up.</p> \n <h3>4. Practice accessing the webinar with a teammate.</h3> \n <p>Two days before the webinar, have someone on your team access the event link to make sure it’s working for participants. Have this person send you a question, raise their hand, show you what the presentation looks like on the other end, and interact with the webinar interface.</p> \n <h3>5. Establish proceedings for the Q&amp;A section.</h3> \n <p>Let the audience know in the introduction how you’ll be answering their questions — whether you'll respond to select questions at the end or answer them as you go. Our recommendation is to schedule 15 minutes at the end for questions.</p> \n <h3>6. Move slowly through product demonstrations.</h3> \n <p>When doing a demo or showing software, try not to move too quickly or scroll up and down a web page too quickly. It might take 2 to 5 seconds every time you change your screen for everyone to see the change.</p> \n <h3>7. Create a clear stop to the presentation.</h3> \n <p>Have a definitive \"stop\" to the core material at around 50 to 55 minutes. It's okay to extend beyond the end time as long as the \"officially scheduled program\" has a clean end, and those who need to leave can leave.</p> \n <h3>8. Keep your desktop and digital workspace clean.</h3> \n <p>Close all unnecessary applications, especially your email clients, file browser, and web browser. If possible, carry out the webinar on a separate desktop (both macOS and Windows OS allow you to create another desktop). You do not want any personal or confidential info displayed, and you just don't want to interrupt the webinar with any notifications that pop up.</p> \n <h3>9. Start 2 minutes after the hour.</h3> \n <p>This gives people time to call in, but does not make those on time wait too long. It is tempting as a presenter to wait for more people to join, but the max you should wait is 2 minutes.</p> \n <h3>10. Enter the webinar room early.</h3> \n <p>Enter the event at least 15 minutes early. That will give you time to prepare, troubleshoot any issues, and double-check that your microphone and camera are working.</p> \n <h3>11. Use pre-webinar slides and announcements.</h3> \n <p>Put up a slide that introduces you and your company. Show links to your website, social media, and other pertinent sites.</p> \n <h3>12. Send out a recording and the slides to attendees (with a call-to-action).</h3> \n <p>Do this within 24 hours, and tell them during the webinar you will do this. A fast follow-up encourages attendees to continue engaging with your company (or <a href=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/marketing/convert-webinar-leads-into-sales\">convert</a>) while the webinar is still on their mind. This follow-up should contain a clear call-to-action button.</p> \n <h2>Use Webinar Best Practices to Host a Great Webinar</h2> \n <p>Hosting a webinar is proven to be a great return on investment. By following the best practices we’ve shared in this post, you can make sure your event drives lead generation, establishes your brand as an authority, and grows your revenue.</p> \n <p><em>Editor's note: This post was originally published in November 2007 and has been updated for comprehensiveness.</em></p> \n <div class=\"cta-post cta-document\"> \n  <div class=\"cta-content\"> \n   <a class=\"cta_button\" href=\"https://www.hubspot.com/cs/ci/?pg=b1081fa4-6cba-48de-af74-ff3f1a4501c1&amp;pid=53&amp;ecid=&amp;hseid=&amp;hsic=\"><img class=\"hs-cta-img \" style=\"border-width: 0px; /*hs-extra-styles*/; \" alt=\"New Call-to-action\" src=\"https://no-cache.hubspot.com/cta/default/53/b1081fa4-6cba-48de-af74-ff3f1a4501c1.png\" /></a> \n  </div> \n  <div class=\"cta-content\"></div> \n </div> \n</div> \n<img src=\"https://track.hubspot.com/__ptq.gif?a=53&amp;k=14&amp;r=https%3A%2F%2Fblog.hubspot.com%2Fblog%2Ftabid%2F6307%2Fbid%2F2391%2F10-best-practices-for-webinars-or-webcasts.aspx&amp;bu=https%253A%252F%252Fblog.hubspot.com%252Fmarketing&amp;bvt=rss\" alt=\"\" width=\"1\" height=\"1\" style=\"min-height:1px!important;width:1px!important;border-width:0!important;margin-top:0!important;margin-bottom:0!important;margin-right:0!important;margin-left:0!important;padding-top:0!important;padding-bottom:0!important;padding-right:0!important;padding-left:0!important; \" />","descriptionType":"html","publishedDate":"Thu, 15 Apr 2021 11:00:00 +0000","feedId":54,"bgimg":"https://no-cache.hubspot.com/cta/default/53/96a2a16e-e138-4855-a967-1a190b6c0692.png","linkMd5":"e989c27d1533e8b163f739ff713ce661","bgimgJsdelivr":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx1/cdn23@2020_2/2021/04/23/17-35-38-631_63ac0041fe3e0813.webp","destWidth":381,"destHeight":60,"sourceBytes":3686,"destBytes":5896,"author":"Ivelisse Rodriguez","articleImgCdnMap":{"https://no-cache.hubspot.com/cta/default/53/96a2a16e-e138-4855-a967-1a190b6c0692.png":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx1/cdn23@2020_2/2021/04/23/17-35-38-631_63ac0041fe3e0813.webp","https://blog.hubspot.com/hs-fs/hubfs/elementor-webinar-invite-banner.jpeg?width=650&name=elementor-webinar-invite-banner.jpeg":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx4/cdn92@2020_2/2021/04/23/17-35-48-389_08143c14d9ae0bf9.webp","https://blog.hubspot.com/hs-fs/hubfs/webinar-planning-kit.jpeg?width=650&name=webinar-planning-kit.jpeg":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx11/cdn15@2020_2/2021/04/23/17-35-50-267_fca8fb6e439cdefe.webp","https://no-cache.hubspot.com/cta/default/53/b1081fa4-6cba-48de-af74-ff3f1a4501c1.png":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx10/cdn88@2020_5/2021/04/23/17-35-49-066_006ddd1119efbc67.webp","https://track.hubspot.com/__ptq.gif?a=53&k=14&r=https%3A%2F%2Fblog.hubspot.com%2Fblog%2Ftabid%2F6307%2Fbid%2F2391%2F10-best-practices-for-webinars-or-webcasts.aspx&bu=https%253A%252F%252Fblog.hubspot.com%252Fmarketing&bvt=rss":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx18/cdn43@2020_2/2021/04/23/17-35-48-986_e56f64a33979b035.webp"},"publishedOrCreatedDate":1619199338326},{"createdTime":"2021-04-24 01:35:38","updatedTime":"2021-04-24 01:35:38","title":"11 Creative (But 100% White Hat!) Ways to Earn Backlinks in 2021","link":"https://blog.hubspot.com/marketing/backlink-strategies","description":"<p>If you want to drive organic traffic to your website, you must understand two critical aspects of SEO strategy:</p> \n<ul> \n <li>Relevance</li> \n <li>Authority</li> \n</ul>  \n<p>With <em>relevance</em>, the key is knowing what your audience is searching for and providing the highest quality and most relevant content so it's a no-brainer for Google to serve it up to them.</p> \n<p>But this isn't an exact science.</p> \n<a class=\"cta_button\" href=\"https://www.hubspot.com/cs/ci/?pg=1d7211ac-7b1b-4405-b940-54b8acedb26e&amp;pid=53&amp;ecid=&amp;hseid=&amp;hsic=\"><img class=\"hs-cta-img \" style=\"border-width: 0px; /*hs-extra-styles*/; margin: 0 auto; display: block; margin-top: 20px; margin-bottom: 20px\" alt=\"→ Download Now: SEO Starter Pack [Free Kit]\" src=\"https://no-cache.hubspot.com/cta/default/53/1d7211ac-7b1b-4405-b940-54b8acedb26e.png\" align=\"middle\"></a> \n<p><br>You could create the best content out there from your perspective, but it's a competitive landscape, and Google takes myriad other factors into account when ranking pages on the SERPs. One of those being... how <em>authoritative</em> (or trustworthy) the provider of that content is.</p> \n<p>You might think that \"authority\" is subjective, but Google has one critical way to measure it: backlinks.</p> \n<p></p> \n<h3>Why are backlinks important?</h3> \n<p>While there are <a href=\"https://backlinko.com/google-ranking-factors\">200 known Google ranking factors</a>, backlinks counts as one of the most important for Google search.</p> \n<p>That's because a link to another website is more than <em>just </em>a link -- it's a vote of confidence, a recommendation, a way for publishers to say to their readers: \"Here's a source I trust. Go check it out yourself.\"</p> \n<p>It's incredibly difficult to get that kind of endorsement, especially for small businesses or startups. But if you want to boost your SEO performance, you need to make sure you consistently earn high-quality backlinks to your website, better and faster than your competition.</p> \n<p>Additionally, Gabi Theard, Director of Marketing at <a href=\"https://trujay.com/\">Trujay</a>, says, \"A link building strategy doesn't <em>just</em> increase your SEO score and visibility on Google. It also shows readers where your company falls in relations to other brands — and reminds readers that there is, in fact, a human behind the screen. Backlinks can demonstrate a relationship between two sites and how each site is working to help the other grow.\"</p> \n<p>\"Plus, backlinks help readers get the highest degree of information that answers their questions.\"</p> \n<h3>High-Quality Backlinks</h3> \n<p>Keep in mind, though, that not all backlinks are created equal. If you think of a backlink as a vote of confidence, it only makes sense to also evaluate the credibility of that vote.</p> \n<p>In the past, tactics such as link farms, PBNs, and comment spam allowed black-hat SEOs to create vast backlink profiles and successfully game the system. However, these <a href=\"https://searchcontentmanagement.techtarget.com/definition/black-hat-link-building\">black-hat link-building techniques</a> no longer work because Google has gotten savvy to them. In fact, too many \"unnatural\" links may even earn your site a penalty.</p> \n<p>In other words, <em>quality</em> matters just as much as <em>quantity</em> when it comes to backlinks.</p> \n<p>Earning high-quality backlinks is probably the most challenging part of SEO. You'll want links that are:</p> \n<ul> \n <li><strong>Authoritative</strong> - The site has an authoritative backlink profile (many votes of confidence), generates a lot of traffic, and even ranks well in the SERPs itself. In addition, .gov and .edu sites tend to carry more weight, as do industry-leading sites.</li> \n <li><strong>Relevant</strong> - The referring page tackles a similar topic or niche. e.g. If your technology company's homepage gets a backlink from a blog post on \"how to golf,\" this would not be seen as a relevant or quality backlink.</li> \n <li><strong>Unique</strong> - You will get an edge if the site refers to you but does not refer to your competitors. Otherwise, the backlink may be good to have, but it's table stakes.</li> \n <li><strong>Natural</strong> - The link is not sponsored, the anchor text is not branded or spammy, and the referring page has a natural number of links on it.</li> \n</ul> \n<p>As an SEO strategist specifically focusing on link building at HubSpot, I'm no stranger to the challenge of finding high-quality sources that will link back to your site. To help you improve your company's SEO ranking, I've cultivated this list of creative and unique ways to earn backlinks.</p> \n<h3>1. Reclaim Unlinked Mentions</h3> \n<p>Reclaiming unlinked brand mentions is probably the easiest, quickest way to build high-quality backlinks.</p> \n<p>All you need to do is keep an eye on who is mentioning your brand, on blogs or in the news. You can do that using something as simple (and free) as Google Alerts. If you want more insights into your mentions, like the number of shares or the domain authority of the website where the mention comes from, you can opt for tools like <a href=\"https://buzzsumo.com/\">BuzzSumo</a>, <a href=\"https://ahrefs.com/content-explorer\">Ahrefs Content Explorer</a> or <a href=\"https://mention.com/en/\">Mention</a>.</p> \n<div>\n <img src=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/hubfs/11%20Creative%20(But%20100%25%20White%20Hat!)%20Ways%20to%20Earn%20Backlinks%20in%202019-2.png\" alt=\"ahrefs content explorer\">\n</div> \n<p style=\"font-size: 13px; text-align: center;\"><em><a href=\"https://ahrefs.com/content-explorer\">Image Source</a></em></p> \n<p>Oftentimes, you'll notice the author hasn't included a link back to your website when they mention your brand, product, or service. That's when you can send them a quick note, asking for a proper link attribution. This also allows the publisher to give their readers a better experience, letting them click through and learn more about the brand mentioned. It's a win, win.</p> \n<p>The creative part of this tactic is that you can use the same method to reclaim links for other mentions that are related to your brand -- including events you organize, employees names, research reports, etc.</p> \n<p>For example, you can keep a lookout for interviews that feature your company's executives and ask for a link back to their profile page on your website. Or, you can look for mentions of reports or statistics you've published, and ask for a proper link attribution to the original source.</p> \n<h3>2. Get Contextual Links</h3> \n<p>Have you noticed how some articles feature additional resources, either recommended in text or inside a \"Read more\" section?</p> \n<p>Here's an example of a \"read more\" section from <a href=\"https://www.searchenginejournal.com/\">SEJ</a>, where they link to a related piece:</p> \n<div>\n <img src=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/hubfs/11%20Creative%20(But%20100%25%20White%20Hat!)%20Ways%20to%20Earn%20Backlinks%20in%202019-1.png\" alt=\"\">\n</div> \n<p>These links embedded in the text of an article are called <em>contextual links</em>.</p> \n<p>The key to getting contextual links is to find the right link prospect to reach out to. You can find them by researching articles that are related to the content you're promoting <em>and </em>already have a \"Read more\" section.</p> \n<p>For instance, let's say you have a new study on email marketing. Try looking for articles that speak about marketing trends and recommend other articles.</p> \n<p>Here's how to find them using search engines like Google:</p> \n<ul> \n <li>marketing trends inurl:blog intext:”Read more”</li> \n <li>marketing trends inurl:blog intext:”Recommended articles”</li> \n <li>marketing trends inurl:blog intext:”Recommended reading”</li> \n</ul> \n<p>When you reach out to the author to pitch your study, don't forget to mention why your content is worth getting featured. A persuasive boilerplate and a personalized email will go a long way.</p> \n<p>Additionally, Theard says: \"Once you get into the habit of earning backlinks, you may start to notice that other publishers come to you directly. With the right relationship-building strategy, publishers come to <em>you</em> rather than you inquiring to them.\"</p> \n<p>She adds, \"Relationship-based backlinks are critical, as opposed to simple (and frequent) link exchanges. Google can, and will, pick up on backlink publications that are whimsy; a backlink for a backlink is not a good backlink. A relationship-based backlink is accepted by Google through relevant keywords, the credibility of websites, and genuine effort to have website referrals be at the top of calibers.\"</p> \n<h3>3. Get \"Best X\" List Mentions</h3> \n<p>Today's consumers look for all available options before making a purchasing decision. They often use comparison websites or articles, like \"<a href=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/marketing/best-free-email-marketing-tools?__hstc=233546881.b91aa3f008b03d6dad1a12e372c51254.1618167430453.1618167430453.1618167430453.1&amp;__hssc=233546881.1.1618167430454&amp;__hsfp=4183638795&amp;_ga=2.27976892.1441018980.1618167428-1676128231.1618167428\">The 13 Best Free Email Marketing Tools in 2021</a>\" to see what others recommend.</p> \n<p>To get a sense of how popular these <em>Best X </em>articles are in your industry, use a keyword research tool and check for monthly search volume. For instance, there are more than 3,400 searches per month for the query \"<a href=\"https://www.hubspot.com/products/crm/best/\">best CRM for small businesses</a>\" (according to data from Ahrefs).</p> \n<p>Getting mentioned on articles that list the best products like the one you offer is a fantastic way to reinforce your brand, get more people to try out your product and, of course, earn high-quality backlinks.</p> \n<p><a href=\"https://www.alexbirkett.com/\">Alex Birkett</a>, Senior Growth Marketing Manager at HubSpot, explains why getting featured on these lists is so important for your business: \"If you look at these search results in terms of pure click-through rate, there's an upper limit on how much traffic you can bring to your own product page by ranking on your <em>own</em> site's listicle.\"</p> \n<p>Birkett continues to say -- \"<a href=\"https://ftf.agency/serp-monopoly-strategy/\">As Nick Eubanks has mentioned</a>, if you can broaden your view from trying to rank #1 to trying to monopolize all of the sites on the first page of a search query, you can multiply the amount of click-throughs to your site, your website traffic, and, down the line, your sales volume. And that's not even factoring in the less trackable aspects, such as social proof and brand awareness.\"</p> \n<blockquote>\n \"In other words, this tactic goes beyond just link building and taps into acquisition and brand awareness potential, too.\"\n</blockquote> \n<p>To get your product or service included in a list round-up, start with a simple Google search to find high-ranking blogs that write about your product or industry.</p> \n<p>Here are some useful search terms to help you find relevant prospects:</p> \n<ul> \n <li>Best [X]</li> \n <li>Best [X] for [Y] e.g. <em>Best CRM for entrepreneurs</em></li> \n <li>Top [X]</li> \n <li>Top [X] for [Y] e.g. <em>Top 10 CRM for small businesses</em></li> \n</ul> \n<p>Collect the most relevant prospects in a list and prioritize them based on domain authority (or Domain Rating if you're using Ahrefs), backlink profile, ranking, and referral traffic potential.</p> \n<p>Once your final list is ready, write a short pitch for the author to show them <em>why</em> your product or service deserves to be included in their list.</p> \n<p>As per any outreach campaign, a short, persuasive pitch and a customized email will help you stand out.</p> \n<h3>4. Become a Source for Other Publishers</h3> \n<p>By using your expertise and unique data, you can become a source for other bloggers and journalists.</p> \n<p>Every time someone quotes you, you'll earn a backlink. But high-domain authority backlinks aren't the only benefit of this tactic (although they are a huge benefit on their own). By becoming a trusted source, you'll also increase your brand awareness and drive referral traffic to your website.</p> \n<p>Best of all, it isn't as difficult as you may think.</p> \n<p>To start, simply subscribe to <a href=\"https://www.helpareporter.com/\">HARO</a> (Help A Reporter Out). This is a free service that connects expert sources (like yourself) with bloggers and journalists who are looking for contributors.</p> \n<p>Here's how it works -- every day, HARO will send you an email with queries from writers in your industry. You can pick the ones that resonate with your business and respond via email, including your credentials.</p> \n<p>Speed is very important here, as most of these writers get <em>many</em> submissions. If you're among the first to respond, you have a bigger chance to be seen and selected for the final piece. If you're selected, you'll likely receive an email from a journalist or blogger letting you know the article is live.</p> \n<p>For instance, here's an email I got a few days after I submitted a quote on HARO:</p> \n<div>\n <img src=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/hubfs/11%20Creative%20(But%20100%25%20White%20Hat!)%20Ways%20to%20Earn%20Backlinks%20in%202019-5.png\" alt=\"email response from journalist stating that a quote submitted through HARO was accepted for publication\">\n</div> \n<p>From my experience with HARO, it takes about four weeks for an article to get published after you send your response. Even if you don't receive a follow-up email from the writer, keep an eye on the publication to see if your quote ends up making it into the piece.</p> \n<p>I found that, on average, two out of 10 answers get picked up. That isn't too bad, but if you're like me, you don't want to waste those eight other answers that don't get to be published.</p> \n<p>To ensure you still use those quotes elsewhere, I suggest you create a backlog of content and use it to answer similar questions on Quora, LinkedIn, or even your own blog or social channels.</p> \n<h3>5. Reach Out to Journalists</h3> \n<p>Bloggers and journalists are bombarded with emails pitching them information that is too promotional and doesn't add value to their readers. That's why many <a href=\"https://respona.com/blog/email-outreach/\">outreach emails</a> don't get any responses.</p> \n<p>However, there are effective methods to make your pitch stand out. Paddy Moogan, Co-Founder of <a href=\"https://www.aira.net/\">Aira</a>, explains how his team uses this tactic successfully to earn high-quality backlinks for their clients:</p> \n<p>\"We take an individual from a client's company, usually the founder, Managing Director, or CEO (although it can be anyone, really) and get them to provide us with their views and opinions on a set of topics.</p> \n<p>These topics should be a sweet spot between what their company is credible to talk about, and general newsworthy topics. Classic examples at the moment are things such as what Brexit means for the X industry or what the future of X industry is in the world of AI or automation.</p> \n<p>These broader topics are being talked about a lot in the press, so tying it to a topic that your client can talk about allows you to approach journalists and offer their comments for any upcoming articles. They often link to you because of this, and will also often link to profile pages on your client's website, as well.\"</p> \n<p>Jeff Previte, Content Manager at <a href=\"https://www.bluleadz.com/\">Bluleadz</a>, also shared with me a tip on how their agency stands out when pitching journalists: \"When we conduct outreach for new link building opportunities, we like to use <a href=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/customers/introducing-hubspot-video\">HubSpot video</a> in our emails. We record a short video introducing ourselves and our company. After the introduction, we briefly explain how our content can deliver value to their audience and make some suggestions of what they can link to. This lends a human element. Most link building outreach comes from cold email templates. With a video, we give recipients a name, a face, and a voice they can associate with our company. That small touch helps us stand out.\"</p> \n<h3>6. Update Old Content</h3> \n<p>If you find an article or a research report that hasn't been updated in a while, check how many backlinks the piece has. If there are many publications referencing that content, then you found yourself a real gem.</p> \n<p>You can simply go ahead and create a better, fresh piece, with more relevant data.</p> \n<p>Once the content is live, you can then reach out to bloggers or journalists who've linked to the old content to let them know about your updated version.</p> \n<p>Oftentimes, you'll see the results of your outreach in a matter of days or weeks in the form of backlinks or social media shares. But there are also other benefits that come out of building that relationship in the first place. For instance, you might end up collaborating on other projects that can help you grow your brand, and your traffic.</p> \n<blockquote> \n <p>Ultimately, when building your email outreach list, have a long-term benefit in mind and try building a relationship -- instead of just focusing on the backlink.</p> \n</blockquote> \n<h3>7. Build Free Tools</h3> \n<p>Creating free tools, like calculators or template generators, is an effective method for earning links and even generating new leads.</p> \n<p>In a nutshell, here's how to get started:</p> \n<ol> \n <li>Start with keyword research and see what comes up for \"templates\", \"tools\", or \"generator\" in your industry.</li> \n <li>Check out what tools appear in Top 10 search results for those keywords.</li> \n <li>Try to figure out which tool or generator receives the most backlinks right now.</li> \n <li>Build something similar but <em>way</em> better, e.g. better design, more customizable options, etc.</li> \n</ol> \n<p>For example, take HubSpot's<a href=\"https://www.hubspot.com/email-signature-generator\"> Email Signature Generator</a>. There are over 29,000 searches for \"signature generator\" on any given month on Google, and our tool offers a very simple, aesthetically-pleasing solution.</p> \n<p>Since we launched it, it's been highly used and recommended, having earned over 5,520 backlinks from 1,168 referring domains.</p> \n<h3>8. Publish Ultimate Guides</h3> \n<p>An Ultimate Guide is a piece of content designed to be the best, most comprehensive resource on a given topic. It covers enough information that you don't need to go elsewhere to learn more about that subject.</p> \n<p>Here are two examples from our own blog:</p> \n<ul> \n <li><a href=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/marketing/video-marketing\">The Ultimate Guide to Video Marketing</a></li> \n <li><a href=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/marketing/content-marketing\">The Ultimate Guide to Content Marketing</a></li> \n</ul> \n<p>The reason why these Ultimate Guides attract inbound backlinks is because they help bloggers and journalists reference a concept they mention.</p> \n<p>For instance, if someone writes an article titled \"How to get started with SEO\", they can focus on a few tips and tactics without explaining, in-depth, what SEO is -- instead, they can simply link to an SEO Ultimate Guide, if their readers have further questions.</p> \n<p>Here's an example:</p> \n<div>\n <img src=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/hubfs/11%20Creative%20(But%20100%25%20White%20Hat!)%20Ways%20to%20Earn%20Backlinks%20in%202019.png\" alt=\"Article on &quot;how to get started using seo&quot; featuring hubspot's ultimate guide to se\">\n</div> \n<p style=\"font-size: 13px; text-align: center;\"><em><a href=\"https://izea.com/2019/04/04/cotent-marketing-seo/\">Image Source</a></em></p> \n<p>Alex Birkett, Senior Growth Marketing Manager at HubSpot, uses this approach with his personal blog, as well. Here's how he explains it: \"An Ultimate Guide doesn't have to explicitly tell you it is an Ultimate Guide. It simply has to go above-and-beyond in its utility or perceived value.\"</p> \n<p>\"For example,\" Birkett continues, \"I recently wrote <a href=\"https://www.alexbirkett.com/ab-testing/\">a 6,500 word guide on A/B testing</a>. It ranges from beginner issues all the way through advanced topics and fringe cases. Basically, it's a bookmarkable article for anyone who runs A/B tests. Not only did it get a really solid initial spike of traffic from social shares, but it consistently gains organic links month-by-month.\"</p> \n<div>\n <img src=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/hubfs/11%20Creative%20(But%20100%25%20White%20Hat!)%20Ways%20to%20Earn%20Backlinks%20in%202019-4.png\" alt=\"ultimate guide on a/b testing\">\n</div> \n<h3>9. Use Images to Earn Links &amp; Mentions</h3> \n<p>Infographics are probably the most common visual asset used to earn backlinks. It's always good to experiment with them, if you haven't done it before.</p> \n<p>However, if you feel infographics don't work well for your brand, here are a few other visuals you might consider creating:</p> \n<ul> \n <li>Charts and graphs with original data</li> \n <li>Diagrams to visually explain complex concepts</li> \n <li>One-page templates</li> \n <li>Free photo galleries for others to use</li> \n</ul> \n<p>To give you an idea of how other brands use free photo galleries, check out this creative campaign from LinkedIn: <a href=\"https://business.linkedin.com/sales-solutions/real-face-of-sales\">The Real Face of Sales</a>. The brand has created a free downloadable library of photos that feature real, non-cliche salespeople.</p> \n<p>The photos are also available on <a href=\"https://unsplash.com/\">Unsplash</a> and <a href=\"https://www.pexels.com/@linkedin\">Pexels</a> (where they got over 35 million views), which helped with distribution.</p> \n<div>\n <img src=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/hubfs/11%20Creative%20(But%20100%25%20White%20Hat!)%20Ways%20to%20Earn%20Backlinks%20in%202019-3.png\" alt=\"\">\n</div> \n<h3>10. Use Directories (yes, Directories!)</h3> \n<p>Despite what you may have heard, directories aren't dead. In fact, they are probably one of the best ways to improve your local SEO and help potential customers find your business.</p> \n<p>Of course, I'm not talking about spammy directories that are there just for the sake of links. Those are more likely to harm your SEO performance than anything else.</p> \n<p>The directories you need to be on are the ones people actually use -- like Google My Business, Yelp, and TripAdvisor. Beyond these famous ones, there are many other general and niche directories that can help your rankings and traffic.</p> \n<p>Here are a few resources to help you find relevant directories:</p> \n<ul> \n <li><a href=\"https://www.searchenginejournal.com/web-directories-list/287799/#close\">21 Web Directories That Still Have Value</a> (Search Engine Journal)</li> \n <li><a href=\"https://www.brightlocal.com/resources/top-local-citations-by-business-category/\">Top Local Citations by Business Category</a> (BrightLocal)</li> \n <li><a href=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/blog/tabid/6307/bid/10322/the-ultimate-list-50-local-business-directories.aspx\">The Ultimate List: 57 Online Local Business Directories</a> (HubSpot)</li> \n <li><a href=\"https://www.linkio.com/directory-submission-sites/\">600+ Directory Sites and How To Do Directory Link Building</a> (Linkio)</li> \n</ul> \n<h3>11. Use the Broken Link Building Method</h3> \n<p>This tactic involves reaching out to a website that has a broken outbound link (a link to an external source) and suggest they update it with a link to one of your pages. Of course, your page has to be a good resource on the topic to which they were originally linking, so it makes sense to swap the broken link with yours.</p> \n<p>The reason this tactic works so well is because it's adding a ton of value to the webmasters -- it helps them fix an error on their website and it improves the experience for their readers.</p> \n<p>The challenge with this tactic is, of course, finding these broken links.</p> \n<p>You have a couple of options here:</p> \n<ol> \n <li>You can look for websites with broken links and find relevant resources on your website that you might suggest in its place.</li> \n <li>You can look for one dead page (404) that used to get a ton of links, recreate that article or offer with better, more relevant content, and then reach out to those who linked to the initial piece.</li> \n</ol> \n<p>Either way, you'll need a good SEO tool to help you identify broken links. You can try <a href=\"http://siteliner.com\">Siteliner</a>, which is free if you have under 250 pages to review, or Ahrefs, which also published a <a href=\"https://ahrefs.com/blog/broken-link-building/\">guide</a> on how to use the broken link building method using their tool.</p> \n<p>Once you identify the target websites and have your content ready, you can start working on your outreach. Make sure to keep your email short and sweet and focus on being helpful, rather than just getting a backlink.</p> \n<h3>Make Sure You Have The Right Backlink Checkers in Your SEO Toolbox</h3> \n<p>Now that you have a list of tactics to try out in your next link building campaign, it's time to make sure you also have the tools you need to succeed.</p> \n<p>Because there are so many options out there, I thought I'd end this article with a list of my top free, tried-and-tested backlinks checkers.</p> \n<p>To make it easier for you to pick the right tool for your next project, I went ahead and tested each tool to see how many backlinks they can find, as well as other unique features they each offer.</p> \n<p>I used our domain (www.hubspot.com) to test the capabilities of each tool and here's what I found:</p> \n<h3>1. <a href=\"https://ahrefs.com/backlink-checker\">Ahrefs Backlink Checker </a></h3> \n<p>With the second most active crawler besides Google, Ahrefs has the most comprehensive backlink database, giving you up-to-date data. In the free version of the tool, Ahrefs shows you Top 100 backlinks, Top 5 anchors, and Top 5 pages. That's enough to get a birds-eye view of your website's backlinks.</p> \n<p>If you'd like to get into more details, the paid version offers far more extensive data and access to other tools that might be useful in a link building campaign, like Content Explorer or Broken Outbound links, to name a few.</p> \n<h3>2. <a href=\"https://neilpatel.com/backlinks/\">Backlinks by Neil Patel</a></h3> \n<p>It may not pick up as many backlinks or referring domains as Ahrefs, but this tool gives a lot of value in the free version. For one, you can export to CSV up to 5,000 backlinks and see the Source Page Title, URL, and anchor text. You can also filter the view by including or excluding domains, anchors or zones (.es, .de etc.). All in all, I'd definitely recommend checking out this free tool.</p> \n<h3>3. <a href=\"https://monitorbacklinks.com/seo-tools/backlink-checker\">MonitorBacklinks</a></h3> \n<p>MonitorBacklinks picks up almost as many referring domains as Ahrefs. Additionally, what's unique about MonitorBacklinks is that it offers details on the top backlinks that you can see based on Trust Flow or Citation Flow. However, to access more of their database, you need to switch to their paid version.</p> \n<h3>4. <a href=\"https://www.openlinkprofiler.org/\">OpenLinkProfiler</a></h3> \n<p>OpenLinkProfiler is a great tool for analyzing your backlink profile. The downside is that their database of links is fairly limited compared to Ahrefs or MonitorBacklinks. Still, there's a lot of insights you can gain (for free) by filtering the available backlinks by categories such as industry, TLDs, anchors, or LIS (Link Influence Score). That's something I haven't seen in other free tools.</p> \n<p>This tool also provides charts to show you which pages get the most links, or which countries link most to your website.</p> \n<h3>5. <a href=\"https://www.rankwatch.com/backlinks/\">RankWatch</a></h3> \n<p>RankWatch has a great Dashboard feature where you can visualize your backlink profile. Among other things, you can see your link acquisition trend for the past three months, referring domains acquisition, and anchor distribution. The overall summary charts are available for free. However, if you want to see the exact list of backlinks or referring domains you've earned, you need to switch to the paid version.</p> \n<h3>6. <a href=\"https://cognitiveseo.com/site-explorer/\">CognitiveSEO</a></h3> \n<p>CognitiveSEO is great for getting an overall view of the total backlinks and referring domains -- and, most importantly, checking your link velocity. You can see the link acquisition trend for the past 6 months for free, even without creating an account. Another interesting visual report is the Top 5 website pages, where you can see how your website performs by backlinks or referral domains.</p> \n<p>All of the above tools provide valuable insights that can help you get started with link building. They all give a macro view on your backlink profile, but each one comes with different additional information. Try them out and see which one is best for you.</p> \n<p><em>Editor's note: This post was originally published in September 2019 and has been updated for comprehensiveness.</em></p> \n<p><a 01:35:38","updatedTime":"2021-04-24 01:35:38","title":"How to (Easily) Make Perfect Content Calendars in Google Sheets","link":"https://blog.hubspot.com/marketing/make-calendar-google-sheets","description":"<p>What do you use spreadsheets for?</p> \n<p>If you're anything like me, you likely use them to collect data, track campaign or <a href=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/blog/tabid/6307/bid/30737/10-amazing-blogging-insights-your-analytics-can-tell-you.aspx\">blog post analytics</a>, or keep track of weekly assignments.</p> \n<p>But have you ever thought about using spreadsheets to make a calendar?</p>  \n<div> \n <p>And, more specifically, have you ever thought about using Google Sheets to make a functional calendar?</p> \n <p><a class=\"cta_button\" href=\"https://www.hubspot.com/cs/ci/?pg=40f08350-c04e-4bc2-b319-ebacc4f04050&amp;pid=53&amp;ecid=&amp;hseid=&amp;hsic=\"><img class=\"hs-cta-img \" style=\"border-width: 0px; /*hs-extra-styles*/; margin: 0 auto; display: block; margin-top: 20px; margin-bottom: 20px\" alt=\"Free Download: Marketing Editorial Calendar Template\" src=\"https://no-cache.hubspot.com/cta/default/53/40f08350-c04e-4bc2-b319-ebacc4f04050.png\" align=\"middle\"></a></p> \n <p>If you often work on campaigns for a few different clients, creating individual calendars in Google Sheets could be uniquely useful for ensuring the client understands when certain content will go live. Alternatively, perhaps you need to create an internal Google Sheet calendar for your team to keep track of upcoming projects.</p> \n <p>Making a calendar in a tool that's commonly used for spreadsheets sounds a little intimidating, but don't worry, the process is actually pretty intuitive. And with the help of some tips, you can easily make a functional calendar that you can sync your schedule with.</p> \n <p>Below, we'll go over how to make a calendar in Google Sheets and include some tips that'll help you elevate the design. At the end, your calendar will look something like this:</p> \n <div>\n  <img src=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/hs-fs/hubfs/google-sheets-calendar-example.png?width=1486&amp;name=google-sheets-calendar-example.png\" alt=\"Google Sheets calendar January to May\" width=\"1486\" style=\"width: 1486px;\">\n </div> \n <p>So start a new spreadsheet and get ready to create your very own calendar. 📅</p> \n <h3>1. Open a new spreadsheet and choose your month.</h3> \n <p>First, open a <a href=\"http://sheets.google.com/?__hstc=20629287.bcd2ff33136b804dec7cbf541860d7f1.1613681847534.1615500944706.1615506448582.20&amp;__hssc=20629287.1.1615506448582&amp;__hsfp=512429567\">new spreadsheet</a>. Then, delete columns H — Z. They won't be needed.</p> \n <p>Then, choose your month. For this example, I decided to do January 2021, so I filled that into the first cell. What's great about Google Sheets is that it automatically recognizes dates, so typing in a month, followed by the year in YYYY format will tell Google that you're going to be working with dates.</p> \n <h3>2. Begin to format your calendar.</h3> \n <p>Next, format your calendar. I selected the text, January 2021, in Column A, Row 1. I highlighted seven columns (A-G), and clicked <strong>Merge</strong> to make that cell span across the entire column. You can find this button to the right of the Fill tool.</p> \n <div>\n  <img src=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/hs-fs/hubfs/formatting-calendar.gif?width=650&amp;name=formatting-calendar.gif\" alt=\"Formatting the January title in a Google Sheets calendar\" width=\"650\" style=\"width: 650px; margin-left: auto; margin-right: auto; display: block;\">\n </div> \n <p>Here, I also center-aligned my text using the tool next to Merge. Then, I increased the font size and bolded the month.</p> \n <h3>3. Use a formula to fill in the days of the week.</h3> \n <p>Next, fill in the days of the week in each column (A-G). You can do this manually but I decided to use a formula. Sheets has a function that lets you type in formulas to complete certain actions at once.</p> \n <p>To fill in days of the week, in the cell where you want your first weekday to be, type: <strong>=TEXT(1, \"DDDD\")</strong>. What this tells Google is that your number will be replaced by a date or time and the format you're using is weekdays.</p> \n <div>\n  <img src=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/hs-fs/hubfs/sunday-google-sheets-calendar.png?width=650&amp;name=sunday-google-sheets-calendar.png\" alt=\"Entering the weekday formula in a Google Sheets calendar\" width=\"650\" style=\"width: 650px; margin-left: auto; margin-right: auto; display: block;\">\n </div> \n <p>Highlight the number 1 in the formula and replace it with: <strong>COLUMN()</strong>. Then, press enter and select your first day. You're going to copy the formula in Sunday's cell by dragging the selector to the end of your row, (A-G), and pressing enter again.</p> \n <div>\n  <img src=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/hs-fs/hubfs/fill-in-days-google-sheets-calendar.gif?width=650&amp;name=fill-in-days-google-sheets-calendar.gif\" alt=\"Filling in the weekdays in a Google Sheets calendar\" width=\"650\" style=\"width: 650px;\">\n </div> \n <p>Pressing enter should automatically fill in the rest of the week. Remember, if this doesn't work for you, you can always fill in the days manually.</p> \n <p>Pressing enter should automatically fill in the rest of the week. Remember, if this doesn't work for you, you can always fill in the days manually.</p> \n <h3>4. Fill in the numbers.</h3> \n <p>Excellent! You have your days of the week. Now we're going to fill in the numerical values. Before this step, I took the time to add color to the days row and changed the font to one I liked a little more.</p> \n <p>For the numerical values, we’ll simply identify the first day of the month and <strong>click and drag </strong>to fill in the rest.</p> \n <p>How?</p> \n <p>Place the number 1 on the box right underneath the first day of the month, the click and drag horizontally.</p> \n <div>\n  <img src=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/hs-fs/hubfs/filling-in-numbers.gif?width=650&amp;name=filling-in-numbers.gif\" alt=\"Filling in the day numbers in a Google Sheets calendar\" width=\"650\" style=\"width: 650px; margin-left: auto; margin-right: auto; display: block;\">\n </div> \n <h3>5. Fill in the rest of the numbers.</h3> \n <p><strong>Note</strong>: In this step, I filled in the calendar numbers every other row to help with my formatting later.</p> \n <p>Now that you’ve filled out your first row, it’s time to fill in the rest. Manually insert the next number under “Sunday,” then <strong>click and drag</strong> horizontally to fill in the rest.</p> \n <div>\n  <img src=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/hs-fs/hubfs/filling-in-numbers-calendar-day-3.gif?width=650&amp;name=filling-in-numbers-calendar-day-3.gif\" alt=\"Filling in the rest of the numbers in a Google Sheets calendar\" width=\"650\" style=\"width: 650px; margin-left: auto; margin-right: auto; display: block;\">\n </div> \n <p>Repeat the process for the next rows. You’ll insert the first number manually, the click and drag down the row. Here’s what that looks like for the next row in January.</p> \n <p><img src=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/hs-fs/hubfs/filling-in-numbers-calendar.gif?width=650&amp;name=filling-in-numbers-calendar.gif\" alt=\"Filling in the next row of day numbers in a Google Sheets calendar \" width=\"650\" style=\"width: 650px; margin-left: auto; margin-right: auto; display: block;\"></p> \n <p><strong>Note</strong>: Make sure to end the month on the right number! For January, that would be the 31st.</p> \n <h3>6. Reformat your calendar if necessary.</h3> \n <p>Everything is starting to look like a calendar, right? At this stage, I reformatted things to clean up the look of my calendar a little.</p> \n <p>Remember those extra rows in between the numbered rows? I expanded those rows to create boxes underneath the numbers. To do this, I simply dragged the rows down to make those cells bigger. <img src=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/hs-fs/hubfs/creating-boxes-in-spreadsheet-calendar.gif?width=650&amp;name=creating-boxes-in-spreadsheet-calendar.gif\" alt=\"Expanding the cells in a Google Sheets calendar\" width=\"650\" style=\"width: 650px; margin-left: auto; margin-right: auto; display: block;\"></p> \n <p><strong>Here are some additional formatting tips</strong>:</p> \n <ul> \n  <li>Select the empty rows underneath your numbers and <strong>center them</strong> using the center text alignment tool.</li> \n  <li>Select your entire calendar and <strong>vertically align</strong> all elements so that they’re in the center of their cells. To do this, use the vertical alignment tool.</li> \n  <li><strong>Bold</strong> your day numbers.</li> \n  <li>If desired, <strong>lightly shade</strong> your numbered rows.</li> \n  <li>If desired, <strong>gray out</strong> the Saturday and Sunday columns so that your workdays stand out.</li> \n </ul> \n <h3>7. Add design elements to professionalize the look.</h3> \n <p>Finally, you can add in some fun design elements to personalize the look and feel of your calendar. If it's for a client or upcoming project, you'll want to incorporate necessary launch days here.</p> \n <p><img src=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/hs-fs/hubfs/completed-google-sheets-calendar.png?width=650&amp;name=completed-google-sheets-calendar.png\" alt=\"Completed Google Sheets calendar\" width=\"650\" style=\"width: 650px; margin-left: auto; margin-right: auto; display: block;\"></p> \n <p>For this step, I added in a few fun images, included a few hypothetical calendar events, and played with font sizes.</p> \n <h3>8. Repeat the process from February to December.</h3> \n <p>It’s time to repeat for the month of February to December. Simply duplicate your January calendar once you’ve designed it how you want it to look. To do this, right click the sheet’s tab and select <strong>Duplicate</strong> from the menu.</p> \n <p><img src=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/hs-fs/hubfs/duplicate-google-sheets-calendar.png?width=650&amp;name=duplicate-google-sheets-calendar.png\" alt=\"Duplicate tab option in Google Sheets \" width=\"650\" style=\"width: 650px; margin-left: auto; margin-right: auto; display: block;\">To fill in the numbers, you’ll only need to know the beginning day, then click and drag to fill in the rest of the rows. <strong>Here are the first days for every month for the year 2021: </strong></p> \n <ul> \n  <li><strong>January</strong>: Friday</li> \n  <li><strong>February</strong>: Monday</li> \n  <li><strong>March</strong>: Monday</li> \n  <li><strong>April</strong>: Thursday</li> \n  <li><strong>May</strong>: Saturday</li> \n  <li><strong>June</strong>: Tuesday</li> \n  <li><strong>July</strong>: Thursday</li> \n  <li><strong>August</strong>: Sunday</li> \n  <li><strong>September</strong>: Wednesday</li> \n  <li><strong>October</strong>: Friday</li> \n  <li><strong>November</strong>: Monday</li> \n  <li><strong>December</strong>: Wednesday</li> \n </ul> \n <p>Next, you’ll want to know how many days you’ll need to fill in. <strong>Here are the number of days you’ll need for each month: </strong></p> \n <ul> \n  <li><strong>January</strong>: 31</li> \n  <li><strong>February</strong>: 28 or 29</li> \n  <li><strong>March</strong>: 31</li> \n  <li><strong>April</strong>: 30</li> \n  <li><strong>May</strong>: 31</li> \n  <li><strong>June</strong>: 30</li> \n  <li><strong>July</strong>: 31</li> \n  <li><strong>August</strong>: 31</li> \n  <li><strong>September</strong>: 30</li> \n  <li><strong>October</strong>: 31</li> \n  <li><strong>November</strong>: 30</li> \n  <li><strong>December</strong>: 31</li> \n </ul> \n <p>And then, you're done!</p> \n <p>It's handy to use Sheets because you can open your calendar right on your browser. You can also keep track of your schedule in a place that's separate from your phone.</p> \n <p>Alternatively, you can create important business documents such as social and editorial calendars. Below, I share a template that’s perfect for the task.</p> \n <h2>Google Sheets Calendar Template</h2> \n <p>Here’s an editorial calendar template for all of your editorial planning needs. engine optimization (SEO) may seem like a straightforward concept.</p> \n<p>You pick keywords related to your business, create content with those keywords, and you’re set to watch your site grow — a simple three-step process, right? Nope.</p> \n<p>While those are fundamental elements of SEO, it can actually be quite challenging to create a <a href=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/marketing/seo-strategy?_ga=2.226306842.1208004828.1617998542-1928572388.1617998542\">strategy</a> that helps you drive traffic and enough of it to meet your overall business goals.</p> \n<p>It can be difficult to get your feet off the ground. Thankfully, there are various tools specifically designed to help you with SEO, build domain authority, and achieve high ROI. In this post, we’ll hear inspiring stories from HubSpot clients that have used <a href=\"https://www.hubspot.com/products/marketing/seo?_ga=2.234710558.1208004828.1617998542-1928572388.1617998542\">our SEO tools</a> to achieve business success.</p> \n<p><a class=\"cta_button\" href=\"https://www.hubspot.com/cs/ci/?pg=1d7211ac-7b1b-4405-b940-54b8acedb26e&amp;pid=53&amp;ecid=&amp;hseid=&amp;hsic=\"><img class=\"hs-cta-img \" style=\"border-width: 0px; /*hs-extra-styles*/; margin: 0 auto; display: block; margin-top: 20px; margin-bottom: 20px\" alt=\"→ Download Now: SEO Starter Pack [Free Kit]\" src=\"https://no-cache.hubspot.com/cta/default/53/1d7211ac-7b1b-4405-b940-54b8acedb26e.png\" align=\"middle\"></a></p> \n<h2>5 SEO Success Stories To Inspire Your 2021 Strategy</h2> \n<h3>1. Ironpaper</h3> \n<p><a href=\"https://www.ironpaper.com/\">Ironpaper</a> is a digital marketing agency that helps their B2B clients grow. They worked with one of their clients, Goddard, to <a href=\"https://www.ironpaper.com/webintel/articles/harnessing-hubspot-for-measurable-growth-how-ironpaper-influenced-over-3-5-million-in-opportunities-for-goddard/\">achieve significant success</a> using HubSpot’s SEO tools.</p> \n<p>Jonathan Franchell, CEO and Founder of Ironpaper, says, “While Goddard fills a real need for their customers by designing medical devices, historically they’ve struggled to find quality leads that could use their services. Instead, their website attracted a lot of spam and unqualified contacts.” Ironpaper began making critical SEO updates with HubSpot tools on Goddard’s site, focusing on internal linking, content strategy with business-relevant keywords, and technical SEO issues like broken links and meta tags.</p> \n<p>Over an eight-month campaign, Ironpaper helped Goddard gain 2,361 Google positions across various keywords relevant to their offerings. Franchell says, “Because we created targeted content centered on strategic keywords, Goddard’s Google rankings increased even throughout a dip in traffic.”</p> \n<p>The company also now ranks in the top 100 for 50 strategically targeted terms and can use HubSpot’s insights reports and dashboards to monitor their progress to ensure that their future marketing efforts are hyper-targeted for the audience they’ve worked hard to develop.</p> \n<h3>2. Apptega</h3> \n<p><a href=\"https://www.apptega.com/\">Apptega</a> is a cybersecurity and compliance platform. As they grew their business, they knew they would need an optimized website that generated leads. They also recognized that their existing WordPress site wouldn’t be enough for them to reach their goals.</p> \n<p>Joelle Palmer, Apptega’s Digital Marketing Manager, says, “We had built a Frankenstein monster in WordPress. Our dev team would constantly have to drop what they were doing and fix our website.” Apptega then decided to migrate its existing site into CMS Hub.</p> \n<p>Apptega saw<a href=\"https://www.hubspot.com/case-studies/apptega-inc?_ga=2.234710558.1208004828.1617998542-1928572388.1617998542\"> almost immediate success </a>with HubSpot’s SEO tools: “We saw one of our core pages move from a number100+ ranking on Google to position number three in two weeks. SEO usually takes three to six months to work...that was truly amazing for us as a company to experience.”</p> \n<p>Some of the tools Apptega used within Marketing Hub to achieve their growth are the on-page SEO recommendations that direct users to pages that need attention and additional ways to optimize content.</p> \n<h3>3. Beacon Digital Marketing</h3> \n<p>Beacon Digital Marketing specializes in driving results for FinTech, SaaS, and B2B businesses.</p> \n<p>As HubSpot Platinum Partners, they understand how to use and implement HubSpot tools to drive growth and success. While they typically assist other businesses, they took an internal look in August 2020 and decided to implement an <a href=\"https://www.beacondigitalmarketing.com/b2b-marketing-case-studies/seo-case-study-increases-traffic\">SEO overhaul</a> of a post on their blog that they believed could perform better than it already was.</p> \n<p>They focused on a few critical areas for improvement: updating metadata, optimizing for a featured snippet, and re-targeting original keywords. The HubSpot content mapping tool helped them create a strategic pillar-cluster plan, and the on-page SEO recommendations provided them with helpful tips. After implementing their new strategy, they noticed an almost immediate 50% increase in page views: July 2020 showed 991 organic search traffic views, and August 2020 had 1,552.</p> \n<p>Their optimization allowed them to draw more traffic to an existing blog post, and they have also seen an increase in organic traffic to additional pages on their website. This goes to show that a well-rounded SEO strategy can impact all areas of your business, as an increase in traffic leads to curious customers eager to learn more about what you have to offer.</p> \n<h3>4. Take Note</h3> \n<p>Take Note is a UK-based business that provides a range of audio and video transcription services, captions, and on-site note-taking. When demand for their business grew, they struggled with balancing disconnected tools to support their needs and obtain consistent growth. Thomas Carter, Director of Marketing at Take Note, said, “I think for us, SEO is the way to grow within such a competitive market.”</p> \n<p>The business officially signed on to HubSpot in 2018 and has since increased its website traffic by <a href=\"https://www.hubspot.com/case-studies/take-note?_ga=2.234710558.1208004828.1617998542-1928572388.1617998542\">22%</a>. At the same time, their customer base and revenue have grown by 16-22%. They’ve also seen an increase in leads. Carter adds, “Long term, we want to continue to focus on ensuring the quality of our services remains exceptionally high while using technology such as HubSpot to automate and optimize behind the scenes.”</p> \n<h3>5. Revenue River</h3> \n<p><a href=\"https://www.revenueriver.co/\">Revenue River</a> is a digital sales and marketing agency that helps companies scale and become competitive in their industry. One of their clients, Kofinas Fertility Group, saw their site traffic significantly impacted by COVID-19. Eric Pratt, the Managing Partner at Revenue River, says, “The site saw declines from mid-February all the way through May.”</p> \n<p>The business got to work and conducted competitive analysis and keyword research to identify areas of opportunity for growth. They decided that the best course of action was to create pillar content and supporting content clusters, which would help them establish their domain as a source of authority in their industry.</p> \n<p>Since implementing the new strategy in November of 2020, the site has nearly doubled its organic traffic. Between March and June of 2020, they saw 86K impressions, and January-March 2021 saw 1.1M.</p> \n<p>Pratt says this success “Came about because of a combination of SEO strategy planning for research, topic clustering, and on-site/page optimization features to enrich the SEO appeal of the content we’re producing and publishing through HubSpot.”</p> \n<h2>Improving Your SEO Doesn’t Have To Be A Challenge.</h2> \n<p>The success stories we’ve highlighted in this post show that SEO doesn’t have to be a challenge, especially with the help of a high-powered SEO tool.
